# M10 Phase 9 — Tier T2 findings — interrogation view

**Cluster:** M10 — Sin, Guilt and Transgression
**Tier:** T2
**Prompts in tier:** 31
**Characteristics:** 22
**Finding blocks below:** 682

Each prompt in this tier is shown in catalogue order. Under each prompt, all 22 characteristics' findings are stacked verbatim. No analytics, no grouping, no synthesis suggestions — just the raw data organised tier-by-tier for open exploration.

Status codes: **E** = evidenced; **S** = silent; **G** = gap.

---

## T2.1 — Spirit-Level Location

### T2.1.1

**Question:** Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-1]** S — The 98-verse corpus contains no explicit location of wilful sinning at the spirit level. The Hebrew ruach or Greek pneuma terms do not appear in the CHAR-1 evidence base in connection with the sinning act. The verse evidence locates sinning in the will, the soul (nephesh — Eze 18:4), the heart (Job 1:5), and the body/lips (Psa 39:1; Job 2:10), but not explicitly in the spirit.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — The 18-verse CHAR-2 corpus contains no explicit spirit-level location. The Hebrew ruach or Greek pneuma terms do not appear in connection with unintentional sinning in this corpus. The characteristic is not explicitly located at the spirit level.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(S)*

**[CHAR-3]** S — The 34-verse corpus contains no explicit spirit-level (ruach/pneuma) location for confession. The characteristic is located in the heart (2Sa 24:10), the knowledge of the inner person (2Sa 19:20), and the mouth/speech organ, but not specifically in the spirit.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(S)*

**[CHAR-4]** S — The 8-verse corpus contains no explicit spirit-level (ruach/pneuma) location for conscience suppression. The characteristic operates at the level of conscience, cognition, and moral orientation without specific spirit-level terminology.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(S)*

**[CHAR-5]** S — The 18-verse corpus contains no explicit spirit-level (ruach/pneuma) location for refusal to repent. The characteristic operates through the heart (2Ki 10:31), the will (throughout), and bodily-metaphor terms (Neh 9:29 — shoulder/neck) but not through explicit spirit-level terminology.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — The 14-verse corpus contains no explicit spirit-level (ruach/pneuma) location for habitual defection. The characteristic operates through the heart (Exo 9:34), the will (throughout), and relational orientation (2Ki 17:7), but not through explicit spirit-level terminology.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-7]** S — The 19-verse corpus contains no explicit spirit-level (ruach/pneuma) location for contagious sin. The characteristic operates through the will (leader's committed direction), the authority relationship (institutional), and the community's redirected orientation — without explicit spirit-level vocabulary.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — The 9-verse corpus contains no explicit spirit-level (ruach/pneuma) location for political revolt. The characteristic operates through political-social action (breaking submission, establishing independent authority) without explicit spirit-level vocabulary.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Mat 12:31 — "the blasphemy against the Spirit will not be forgiven" — the Holy Spirit is named as the target of the most severe form of sinful speech. This is not spirit-level location of sinful speech in the practitioner but the identification of the Spirit as the one against whom sinful speech can be directed. The uniqueness of this formulation — blasphemy against the Spirit being unforgivable — implies that the Holy Spirit occupies a unique constitutive position in relation to sinful speech's gravity.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — The 5-verse corpus contains no explicit spirit-level (ruach/pneuma) location for enticement, collective hypocrisy, or apostasy. The mechanisms operate through the desire-faculty, social-identity, and covenantal-standing levels without explicit spirit-level vocabulary.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes. Eph 2:1 — "dead in the trespasses and sins" — the spiritual death named here is a spirit-level condition: the inner person is spiritually lifeless in its relationship with God. The condition produces death at the deepest level of the person's orientation toward God. Act 26:18 — "from darkness to light and from the power of Satan to God" — the transformation addressed by the gospel involves a spirit-level reorientation from the dark spiritual domain (under sin's condition) to God's domain; the sin-condition is located in the realm that the Spirit must address. Heb 3:13 — "hardened by the deceitfulness of sin" — the hardening is at the level of the heart/spirit's responsiveness to God.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Yes. 1Jo 3:9 — "no one born of God makes a practice of sinning, for God's seed abides in him" — the new birth and God's seed are spirit-level realities; the fact that they prevent the enslaving power confirms that the enslaving power operates at the spirit level where it competes with the new-birth-constitution. 1Jo 3:8 — "of the devil" — the allegiance-capture at the deepest level ("of the devil") is a spirit-level identity claim; the person's spirit-level belonging has been redirected from God to the devil's domain. The enslaving power thus operates at the spirit level by competing with and displacing the God-relationship at the person's deepest constitutional identity-level.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes — through the separation from God that the record produces. Isa 59:2 — "your iniquities have made a separation between you and your God, and your sins have hidden his face from you so that he does not hear" — the separation is at the spirit level: the person's capacity for God-relationship (the spirit's primary orientation) has been disrupted by the accumulated record. Act 26:18 (referenced in CHAR-12 but its principle applies here) — the darkness/light distinction that sin creates operates at the spirit level. The record's most fundamental effect — hiding God's face — is a spirit-level consequence: it severs the deepest channel between the person and God.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes — through the Spirit's reception as the consequence of forgiveness. Act 2:38 — "repent and be baptized every one of you in the name of Jesus Christ for the forgiveness of your sins, and you will receive the gift of the Holy Spirit" — the Spirit's indwelling follows forgiveness and is its most direct spirit-level consequence. The forgiveness operates at the spirit level precisely because it opens the person to the Spirit who was previously blocked by the sin-record. Col 2:13 — "dead in your trespasses... God made alive" — the death-to-life movement is a spirit-level restoration; the spiritual death produced by sin is reversed by forgiveness at the same constitutional level.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Yes — through the defilement and cleansing language. Eze 37:23 — "they shall not defile themselves anymore with their idols and their detestable things, or with any of their transgressions. But I will save them from all the backslidings in which they have sinned, and will cleanse them" — the defilement and cleansing operate at the spirit level: idolatry defiles the inner person's spirit-orientation toward God; the divine cleansing restores it. The "shall be my people, and I will be their God" restoration names the spirit-level relational restoration that follows cleansing.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes — through the defilement and separation language. Heb 7:26 — "holy, innocent, unstained, separated from sinners, and exalted above the heavens" — the sinner's moral character is the polar opposite of holiness, innocence, and unstained purity; these are spirit-level characterisations. Isa 33:14 — "who among us can dwell with the consuming fire?" — the sinners' dread before God's holy presence reveals that their spirit-level incompatibility with God is the issue; the consuming fire is God's holiness that the sinner's spirit-level character cannot withstand. Jam 4:8 — "cleanse your hands, you sinners, and purify your hearts, you double-minded" — the heart-purification called for alongside the sinner's hand-cleansing names the spirit-level inner defilement.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes — through the standing-before-God dimension. Ezr 9:15 — "we are before you in our guilt, for none can stand before you because of this" — the guilt creates a spirit-level barrier between the person and God; the inability to stand before God is a spirit-level relational disruption. Hos 5:5 — "Israel and Ephraim shall stumble in his guilt; Judah also shall stumble with them" — the stumbling produced by guilt operates at the spirit-level of the community's orientation toward God. The characteristic's definition identifies it as "the conscience's recognition of moral liability before God" — the "before God" is the spirit-level relational field in which guilt operates.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes — through the separation-from-God dimension. Isa 59:2 — "your iniquities have made a separation between you and your God, and your sins have hidden his face from you so that he does not hear" — iniquity operates as a spirit-level barrier severing the person's communication with God; the separation is at the deepest relational level. Psa 32:2 — "blessed is the man against whom the Lord counts no iniquity, and in whose spirit there is no deceit" — the spirit is explicitly named as the locus where iniquity (or its absence) is assessed; the spirit's moral condition is the location of the iniquity-count.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes — through the God-relationship and covenantal-allegiance dimensions. Eze 18:31 — "cast away from you all the transgressions that you have committed, and make yourselves a new heart and a new spirit!" — the call for a new heart and new spirit follows directly from the casting-away of transgressions; the spirit-level renewal is the designated remedy for transgression's spirit-level damage. Hos 8:1 — "they have transgressed my covenant and rebelled against my law" — covenant-transgression is a spirit-level relational rupture; 2Jo 9 — "everyone who goes on ahead and does not abide in the teaching of Christ, does not have God" — the transgression of going beyond Christ's teaching severs the spirit-level God-relationship.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes — most explicitly of any M10 characteristic studied. Mal 2:15 — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and let none of you be faithless to the wife of your youth" — the spirit (*rûaḥ*) is the explicitly named locus requiring vigilance against faithlessness; Mal 2:16 — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and do not be faithless" — repeated. The double injunction to "guard yourselves in your spirit" names the spirit as the level at which faithlessness must be resisted. This is the only verse in M10's studied corpus that names the spirit (*rûaḥ*) as the specific inner level from which a M10 characteristic must be guarded against.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes — through two passages. (1) Job 17:1 — "my spirit is broken; my days are extinct; the graveyard is ready for me" — the spirit (*rûaḥ*) is the entity broken by corruption's action; though this is Job under affliction rather than Job's own perversity, it evidences the spirit as the level at which corruption's damage is registered; (2) Gal 6:8 — "for the one who sows to his own flesh will from the flesh reap corruption, but the one who sows to the Spirit will from the Spirit reap eternal life" — the Spirit-level sowing is set in opposition to the flesh-sowing that produces corruption; the Spirit is named as the counter-dimension where corruption does not operate.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(S)*

**[CHAR-22]** S — The 72-verse corpus does not explicitly name the spirit (*rûaḥ/pneuma*) as the locus of injustice. The characteristic operates at the heart, hand, tongue, and conscience levels without direct spirit-level naming. This is analytically significant: unlike CHAR-20 (faithlessness), where Mal 2:15/16 explicitly calls for spirit-level guarding, CHAR-22 locates its operation at adjacent but distinct constitutional levels.

---

### T2.1.2

**Question:** Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-1]** S — No evidence in the CHAR-1 corpus locates the origin of wilful sinning at the spirit level. The origin language in the corpus points to the heart as the inner source (Job 1:5 — "cursed God in their hearts"), the will as the active faculty (Eze 18:4; Gen 39:9), and external temptation as the triggering condition (Neh 13:26; Neh 6:13; 1Sa 15:24). Spirit-level origin is not evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — No evidence locates the origin of unintentional sinning at the spirit level. The origin evidence (T1.7.1) points to epistemic limitation (lack of knowledge, limited perception) as the enabling condition — a feature of creaturely cognitive constitution, not specifically a spirit-level phenomenon.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(S)*

**[CHAR-3]** S — No evidence locates confession's origin at the spirit level. The origin evidence points to the heart/conscience (2Sa 24:10 — "David's heart struck him") and to inner knowledge (2Sa 19:20 — "your servant knows that I have sinned") as the originating faculties.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(S)*

**[CHAR-4]** S — No evidence locates the origin of conscience suppression at the spirit level. The origin evidence points to: absence of God-knowledge (1Cor 15:34), absence of fear of God (Ecc 8:12), and self-interested false innocence claims (Jer 2:35) — all of which are mid-level inner-being phenomena rather than explicitly spirit-level.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(S)*

**[CHAR-5]** S — No evidence locates the origin at the spirit level. The origin evidence points to the heart (2Ki 10:31 — "not with all his heart"), inherited moral orientation (the Jeroboam-sin pattern), and deliberate volitional choice (Heb 10:26). These are heart-and-will-level phenomena.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — No evidence locates the origin at the spirit level. The origin evidence points to the heart's hardening (Exo 9:34), transferred allegiance to other gods (2Ki 17:7), and inherited communal patterns (Hos 10:9). These are heart-will-relational-level phenomena.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-7]** S — No evidence locates the origin at the spirit level. The origin evidence points to the leader's personal inner will (walking in the sinning path — 1Ki 16:26) and their authority position (1Ki 16:2) rather than to spirit-level phenomena.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — No direct evidence locates the origin at the spirit level. The origin evidence points to volitional-social dynamics (the perceived weakness of authority — 2Ki 1:1/3:5; the ruler's spiritual abandonment — 2Ch 21:10) rather than to spirit-level phenomena.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(S)*

**[CHAR-9]** S — No evidence locates the origin of sinful speech at the spirit level of the practitioner. The origin evidence points to the heart (Mat 15:19) and to inner conditions of conceit and craving (1Ti 6:4), not to the spirit-level constitutional faculty.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — No evidence locates the origin at the spirit level. Enticement originates in the desire-faculty (Jam 1:14); hypocrisy in social conformity pressure (Gal 2:13); apostasy in the will's departure from covenantal identity (Act 21:21).

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Rom 5:12 — "sin came into the world through one man" — the origin is historical and corporate (through Adam) rather than at the spirit level of any individual person's constitution. The condition is received/inherited rather than self-originated at the spirit level. Joh 9:34 — "born in utter sin" — birth-origin framing: the condition is present from the person's beginning, not acquired through spirit-level choice. The origin is thus federal/representational (through Adam — Rom 5:12) rather than individual-spirit-level.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Partly. 1Jo 3:8 — "the devil has been sinning from the beginning" — the originary sinning is named as the devil's primordial activity; the devil's sinning from the beginning is the spirit-level source of the enslaving power's authority over those who practice sin. The enslaving power thus originates in the devil's originary spirit-level sinning, not in the creature's own spirit-level.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Not primarily. The record originates in acts (chat.tat as committed acts — Lev 4:23 — "the sin which he has committed"), in the heart's disposition (Deu 15:9 — "an unworthy thought in your heart"), and through inherited condition (Psa 51:5 — "in sin did my mother conceive me"). Jer 17:1 — the sin of Judah is engraved on the heart — the inscription is heart-level. The record thus originates in the heart's dispositional failures and the will's sinning acts rather than at the spirit level specifically; it produces spirit-level consequences (separation from God — Isa 59:2) without originating there.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — The seeking dimension does not primarily originate at the spirit level: it originates in the will's volitional turning (Act 2:38 — "repent"), in the conscience's recognition (Lev 4:14 — "becomes known"), and in the community's ritual response. The receiving dimension, however, has a spirit-level consequence (Act 2:38 — Spirit received) and is enacted by God's sovereign act (2Cor 5:19 — "God was reconciling the world to himself"). The divine granting of forgiveness thus has a spirit-level source (God) even if the human seeking does not originate there.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Partially. Isa 43:27 — "your first father sinned" — the originating act of the first father is a will-level sinning act rather than exclusively a spirit-level phenomenon. However, Psa 78:32 — "despite his wonders, they did not believe" — the unbelief that drives the persistent sinning is a spirit-level failure: the failure to trust God's power and faithfulness at the deepest level of the person's God-orientation. The generational pattern thus has a spirit-level dimension in its sustaining mechanism (unbelief) even if its origin is in a specific volitional act.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Partly. The constituted sinner-identity through Adam (Rom 5:19 — "made sinners through one man's disobedience") operates at the spirit-level of the person's fundamental God-standing. The extreme-type sinner (VCG-03) whose moral character is thoroughly defined by sin has a spirit-level orientation against God: Gen 13:13 — "great sinners against the Lord" — the "against the Lord" names the spirit-level directional opposition. Luk 5:8's Peter — "I am a sinful man, O Lord" — recognises his spirit-level condition in the presence of divine holiness.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Partly. The guilt originates in an act (VCG-01 — violation that becomes known) or an inherited condition (VCG-02 — generational accumulation), not at the spirit level specifically. However, the guilt's registration as a moral-liability-before-God is spirit-level: Ezr 9:15 — "we are before you in our guilt" — the guilt-before-God orientation is the spirit-level dimension. The guilt originates in the act (will-level); the guilt-awareness before God is spirit-level.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Partly — through the heart-seated VCG-08 register. Eze 14:3 — "these men have taken their idols into their hearts, and set the stumbling block of their iniquity before their faces" — the iniquity originates in the will's heart-level choice to receive idols inward; the crime begins at the spirit-level of the heart's allegiance. Job 15:5 — "your iniquity teaches your mouth, and you choose the tongue of the crafty" — the iniquity originates at the level of inner orientation that then drives speech. The spirit-level is the origin of the most deeply-rooted iniquity (VCG-08); other registres (VCG-01 cultic; VCG-04 personal act) originate at the will and conduct levels.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes — the heart-origin of VCG-09 and the revolt-speech origin of VCG-02 both point to spirit-level origin. Psa 36:1 — "transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart" — the most explicit inner-origin statement in the corpus; the transgression speaks from the deepest inner level. Isa 59:13 — "conceiving and uttering from the heart lying words" — the revolt is conceived at the heart-level before being uttered. Eze 14:3 (CHAR-18 cross-reference level) — the idol-taking into the heart is the analogous spirit-level origin for iniquity; for CHAR-19, Psa 36:1's "deep in his heart" is the origin location.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes — Mal 2:15/16's "guard yourselves in your spirit" confirms that faithlessness originates at the spirit level: the guarding is against what would arise from within the spirit if left unguarded. 2Ch 28:22 — Ahaz becoming "yet more faithless" in distress — the progressive deepening of faithlessness is a spirit-level orientation-change under pressure. Isa 48:8 — "I knew you would surely deal treacherously" — the foreknown constitutional bent toward treachery is a spirit-level constitutional characterisation.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Partially — through VCG-03's Isa 29:16's cognitive-relational inversion (the creature denying the creator) which is a spirit-level orientation-reversal. More clearly: Pro 6:14 — "with perverted heart devises evil" — the heart is the origin, and the heart operates at the person's deepest inner level. The primary originating faculty is the heart (Pro 6:14) and the desire-faculty (Eph 4:22 — "through deceitful desires") rather than the spirit specifically — but the heart-level origin is close to the spirit-level of covenantal orientation.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Partially — through the God-ignorance and heart-atheism passages that are adjacent to spirit-level. Psa 53:1 — "the fool says in his heart, 'There is no God'" — the heart-level denial of God is what produces the injustice; Job 18:21 — "him who knows not God" — the God-ignorance that defines the unjust person is a spirit-level relational condition (not knowing God at the spirit-level of covenantal relationship). The characteristic does not originate explicitly at the spirit level but arises from a spirit-level God-relationship deficit that then manifests at the heart and conduct levels.

---

### T2.1.3

**Question:** What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-1]** S — Since spirit-level location is not evidenced (T2.1.1 and T2.1.2), this prompt cannot be answered from the corpus. The absence of spirit-level location may indicate that wilful sinning operates in the middle layers of the inner constitution (will, heart, soul) rather than at the deepest constitutional depth where the person's orientation toward God is constituted. However, inferring from the absence is not warranted beyond noting it.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — Since spirit-level location is not evidenced (T2.1.1 and T2.1.2), this prompt cannot be answered from the corpus. The absence of spirit-level location may reflect that unintentional sinning operates at the surface of the inner person — at the level of action and knowledge rather than at the deepest constitutional orientation — but inferring from the absence is not warranted beyond noting it.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(S)*

**[CHAR-3]** S — Since spirit-level location is not evidenced (T2.1.1 and T2.1.2), this prompt cannot be answered from the corpus. The absence may indicate that confession operates in the middle register of the inner person (conscience, heart, will, speech) rather than at the deepest constitutional level.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(S)*

**[CHAR-4]** S — Spirit-level location is not evidenced (T2.1.1 and T2.1.2). This prompt cannot be answered from the corpus. Noted.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(S)*

**[CHAR-5]** S — Spirit-level location is not evidenced (T2.1.1 and T2.1.2). The prompt cannot be answered from the corpus. The absence may indicate that refusal to repent operates at the middle register of the inner person (heart/will) rather than at the deepest constitutional level.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — Spirit-level location is not evidenced (T2.1.1 and T2.1.2). This prompt cannot be answered from the corpus.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-7]** S — Spirit-level location is not evidenced (T2.1.1 and T2.1.2). The characteristic operates at the will/authority/community level without engaging the deepest spirit-level constitutional faculties explicitly.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — Spirit-level location is not evidenced (T2.1.1 and T2.1.2). This prompt cannot be answered from the corpus.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The spirit-level dimension (Mat 12:31) reveals that sinful speech can reach a depth of irreversibility that operates at the spirit level of the person's relationship with God: blasphemy against the Spirit is not forgivable, indicating that this form of sinful speech closes off the Spirit's operation in a way that cannot be reversed. The spirit-level is engaged not as the origin of the speech but as what is ultimately at stake in the most severe form — the Spirit's sustaining, forgiving presence can be sinfully spoken against in a way that forecloses access to it.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — Spirit-level location is not evidenced. This prompt cannot be answered from the corpus.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Spirit-level location (Eph 2:1 — spiritual death; Act 26:18 — spiritual darkness) reveals that sin as universal condition operates at the deepest level of the person's constitutive relation with God. The condition is not peripheral (merely moral-behavioural) but foundational (the spirit's capacity for life before God is extinguished). This explains why the remedy requires the Spirit's external convicting work (Joh 16:8/9 — "the Spirit will convict the world concerning sin") — the condition is at a level that cannot be self-diagnosed or self-corrected; it requires divine penetration.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Spirit-level location (1Jo 3:8/9 — devil's sinning as origin; new birth as counter at same level) reveals that the enslaving power is not merely a behavioural pattern but an identity-belonging claim at the deepest constitutional level. The enslaving power's spirit-level operation explains why new birth (a spirit-level transformation — 1Jo 3:9) is required for liberation: the power must be countered at the same constitutional depth at which it operates. Behavioural modification alone cannot address a spirit-level enslavement.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The spirit-level consequence (Isa 59:2 — separation and God's hidden face) reveals that the divine record's ultimate harm operates at the deepest constitutional level: it disrupts the person's most fundamental relational capacity — the spirit's access to God. The record is not merely a legal notation but a relational barrier at the spirit level. Jer 31:34's new-covenant promise — "I will remember their sin no more" — promises spirit-level restoration: the erasure of the record restores the spirit's God-access.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Spirit-level location (Act 2:38 — Spirit received after forgiveness; Col 2:13 — alive after dead-in-trespasses) reveals that forgiveness received operates at the deepest constitutional level of the person's capacity for God-relation: the Spirit's indwelling is the spirit-level consequence of the sin-record's removal. The forgiveness addresses what was blocking the spirit-level God-relationship (the sin-record creating separation — Isa 59:2 in CHAR-13's corpus) and opens the person to spirit-level restoration (Spirit received).

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Spirit-level location (Eze 37:23 — defilement through idolatry; unbelief — Psa 78:32) reveals that generational sin operates at the deepest constitutional level of the community's God-relationship: the idolatry that defiles (Eze 37:23) is a spirit-level misorientation of the community's allegiance from God toward idols; the unbelief (Psa 78:32) is the spirit-level failure of trust that perpetuates the sinning across generations. The divine cleansing required (Eze 37:23) is therefore spirit-level restoration, not merely behavioural correction.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Spirit-level location (Heb 7:26 — incompatibility with holiness; Isa 33:14 — cannot dwell with consuming fire; Jam 4:8 — hearts requiring purification) reveals that the sinner-identity is not merely a social or behavioural classification but a constitutional inner reality that produces spirit-level incompatibility with God. The sinner's character makes them structurally unable to stand in the divine presence (Isa 33:14) and requires constitutional cleansing (Jam 4:8 — purify your hearts) that addresses the deepest inner level. This explains why Christ's saving mission (1Ti 1:15 — "came into the world to save sinners") must operate at the spirit level.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Spirit-level location (Ezr 9:15 — standing-disability before God; Hos 5:15 — God withdrawing until guilt acknowledged) reveals that guilt-as-inner-state disrupts the deepest level of the person's God-relationship. The guilt operates as a spirit-level barrier: the guilty person cannot stand before God (Ezr 9:15), God withdraws from the guilty community until they acknowledge (Hos 5:15), and the indelible stain remains before God regardless of self-cleansing effort (Jer 2:22). Spirit-level disruption is thus the characteristic's most profound consequence.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Spirit-level location (Psa 32:2 — "in whose spirit there is no deceit" as iniquity's absence; Isa 59:2 — separation from God; Eze 14:3 — heart-originated idolatry as iniquity's source) reveals that iniquity-as-accumulated-crime is not merely a behavioural or social category but penetrates to the spirit-level of the person's God-relationship. The spirit-level iniquity (Eze 14:3 — idol-taking into the heart) is the most severe form precisely because it originates at the person's deepest inner level of allegiance and orientation. The separation it produces (Isa 59:2) is a spirit-level relational rupture.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Spirit-level location (Eze 18:31 — new heart and new spirit as remedy; Psa 36:1 — speaks deep in the heart; Hos 8:1 — covenant-transgression) reveals that transgression-as-deliberate-boundary-crossing is not merely a surface behavioural category but a spirit-level reality that requires spirit-level renewal for its resolution. The fact that the remedy is a "new heart and new spirit" (Eze 18:31) confirms that the transgression has damaged the person at the deepest constitutive level. The God-relationship rupture (2Jo 9 — "does not have God") is the most severe spirit-level consequence.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Spirit-level location (Mal 2:15/16 — guard your spirit; Isa 48:8 — foreknown constitutional bent) reveals that faithlessness-as-covenant-breaking-sin is the deepest-rooted characteristic in M10: it originates at the spirit's innermost level of covenantal orientation. The "guard yourselves in your spirit" command is remarkable for its precision — it identifies the spirit as the site of the characteristic's generation, requiring active vigilance at the deepest inner level to prevent faithlessness from arising. No other M10 characteristic is addressed with a spirit-vigilance command.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Spirit-level location (Job 17:1 — spirit broken; Gal 6:8 — flesh-sowing vs. Spirit-sowing) reveals that perversion-as-inner-inversion has a spirit-level impact dimension: the corruption damages or breaks the spirit as its deepest constitutional level. Gal 6:8's opposition between Spirit-sowing and flesh-corruption confirms that at the spirit-level the characteristic operates as the counter-dimension to God's Spirit — perversion is what happens when the person's sowing is oriented toward the flesh rather than Spirit.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — The spirit-level silence (T2.1.1) combined with the God-ignorance passages (T2.1.2) reveals that CHAR-22 is primarily a heart-and-conduct characteristic rather than a spirit-level characteristic. The God-ignorance (Job 18:21; Psa 53:1) functions as the spirit-level precondition whose absence enables injustice to arise, but injustice itself is primarily characterised and located at the heart (Psa 58:2) and conduct (hands, tongue, commercial dealings) levels.

---

### T2.1.4

**Question:** If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-1]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. No verse in §3 explicitly connects wilful sinning to the spirit. This is noted.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(S)*

**[CHAR-3]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(S)*

**[CHAR-4]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(S)*

**[CHAR-5]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-7]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Spirit-level evidence is present in Mat 12:31 (T2.1.1 and T2.1.3). The spirit level is engaged as the target of the most severe form, not as the origin of the speech. Noted.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Spirit-level location is evidenced (Eph 2:1; Act 26:18; Heb 3:13). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Spirit-level location is evidenced (1Jo 3:8/9 — devil's sinning; new birth as counter). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Spirit-level consequence (Isa 59:2 — separation from God; God's face hidden) is evidenced. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Spirit-level location is evidenced (Act 2:38 — Spirit received; Col 2:13 — made alive). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Spirit-level location (defilement — Eze 37:23; unbelief — Psa 78:32) is evidenced. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Spirit-level location is evidenced (Heb 7:26; Isa 33:14; Jam 4:8). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Spirit-level location is evidenced (Ezr 9:15; Hos 5:15; Jer 2:22). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Spirit-level location is evidenced (Psa 32:2; Isa 59:2; Eze 14:3). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Spirit-level location is evidenced (Psa 36:1; Eze 18:31; Hos 8:1; 2Jo 9). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Spirit-level location is the most explicitly evidenced constitutional dimension in the 101-verse corpus (Mal 2:15/16; Isa 48:8). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Spirit-level location is evidenced (Job 17:1; Gal 6:8). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(S)*

**[CHAR-22]** S — The spirit (*rûaḥ/pneuma*) is not explicitly named in the 72-verse corpus as the locus of injustice. Noted. The characteristic's constitutional home is primarily heart-and-conduct rather than spirit-level.

---

## T2.10 — Constitutional Movement

### T2.10.1

**Question:** Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other directions?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The corpus evidences constitutional movement primarily in the soul-to-body direction. Speech-based sinning (Psa 39:1 — "sin with my tongue"; Job 2:10 — "sin with his lips"; Ecc 5:6 — "let not your mouth lead you into sin") shows inner sinful intention expressing through the body's speech organs. 1Cor 6:18 shows the reverse — bodily sinning feeding back: "the sexually immoral person sins against his own body" — with the body as both the expressive medium and the site of the damage. The heart-to-action movement is evidenced in Job 1:5 (children may have "sinned, and cursed God in their hearts" — inner heart-orientation potentially producing culpable condition) and in the deterrence corpus (Psa 119:11 — word stored in heart to prevent the will's outward sinful action). Movement from inner to outer (heart/will → speech/act) is the dominant constitutional movement evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Limited movement evidence. The primary movement evidenced is from the *act-level* to the *conscience-level* upon disclosure: the unintentional sin is committed at the level of action (the outward deed), and when it surfaces to awareness the conscience engages (inner level). Lev 5:5 — "when he realizes his guilt" — names a movement from outer-act to inner-realisation. The cultic-purification register (VCG-02) involves movement in the opposite direction: the ritual blood application (outward act) addresses the defilement of the sacred object (external state). No constitutional movement within the person across spirit-soul-body levels is explicitly evidenced.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Yes. The primary constitutional movement evidenced is *inner-to-outer*: conscience (inner) → will (middle) → speech (outer/body). 2Sa 24:10 — "David's heart struck him" (inner conscience) → "David said to the Lord" (outer speech). Luk 15:18 — "I will arise and go to my father, and I will say to him" (inner resolution) → Luk 15:21 — "And the son said to him, 'Father, I have sinned'" (outer enacted speech). The constitutional movement of confession is the movement of the inner recognition through the will's agreement and out through the mouth. The reverse movement is also evidenced: the spoken confession shapes the inner person's self-understanding — naming sin as sin reinforces the conscience's assessment and the will's reorientation.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Limited movement evidence. The most visible constitutional movement is the active-denial mode (Jer 2:35) where the inner suppression externalises through speech: the inward refusal of the conscience's verdict moves outward through the mouth as the false claim "I have not sinned." The reverse movement is also implied: the speech-act of false innocence claiming reinforces the inner suppression — by stating the false claim aloud, the person consolidates the inner suppression. Tit 3:11 — "warped and sinful; he is self-condemned" — the inner moral distortion (soul-level) is visible in outward divisive behaviour, showing an inner-to-outer expression direction.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The most evidenced constitutional movement is from inner will to outer conduct. The Kings pattern shows the inner disposition (refusing to depart from Jeroboam's sins) expressed in outward conduct (walking in them, serving Baal — 1Ki 16:31). Neh 9:29 — "stubborn shoulder... stiffened their neck" — the inner wilful resistance is given bodily-metaphor expression: the inner refusal is embodied in a physical posture of resistance. The direction is inner-to-outer: the will's refusal expresses through outward behaviour (the sinful course continued). The reverse: the established outward pattern of sinning (walking in Jeroboam's sins) shapes and consolidates the inner refusal — the outer conduct of continued sinning feeds back to consolidate the inner disposition.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Yes. The primary constitutional movement is from inner disposition to outward structural expression. Hos 8:11 — "altars multiplied for sinning, they have become to him altars for sinning" — the inner sinning orientation moves outward through the building of altars (physical structures) that then feed back and reinforce the inner orientation. The direction is inner → outer (disposition produces structures) → inner (structures reinforce disposition). 2Ki 17:7 — "sinned against the Lord... and had feared other gods" — the inner transfer of fear/allegiance produces outward practices of worship directed elsewhere, which consolidate the inner defection.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Yes — both within the leader and from leader to community. Within the leader: the inner will-commitment to the sinning course moves outward through the exercise of authority into community-shaping actions (building altars — Jer 32:35; driving people from following the Lord — 2Ki 17:21). From leader to community: the leader's inner sinful orientation moves across the relational-authority boundary into the community's inner being, redirecting the community's will and allegiance (2Ki 21:11 — "made Judah also to sin"). The characteristic's defining constitutional movement is the cross-boundary transmission from one person's inner being to another's through the medium of authority.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The single verse that evidences constitutional movement is 2Ch 21:10 — "because he had forsaken the Lord, the God of his fathers." The causal chain here runs: inner spiritual abandonment (forsaking the Lord — an inner constitutional act) → outer political fragmentation (Edom and Libnah revolt). The constitutional movement is from the ruler's inner spiritual condition outward to political consequence: the inner forsaking produces the outer political revolt as its social-structural consequence. This is an inner-to-outer movement across constitutional levels, with the inner spiritual abandonment of the ruler causing the outer political revolts of subject peoples.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Yes. The primary constitutional movement is the inner-to-outer direction: Mat 15:19 — "out of the heart come evil thoughts... slander" — the heart (inner) generates the content; the mouth (outer/body) externalises it as speech. The movement is from heart → through the will's consent → through the mouth → outward as speech directed at God or persons. The reverse feedback direction is also implied: the habituated practice of sinful speech reshapes the inner heart toward greater corruption (1Ti 6:4 — conceit feeds on the slander it generates).

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Yes — each mechanism shows a distinct constitutional movement pattern. (1) *Enticement*: Jam 1:14 — "lured and enticed by his own desire" — the desire-faculty (inner) is exploited by the temptation (external bait), drawing the inner person outward toward sin. 2Pe 2:14 — "hearts trained in greed... entice unsteady souls" — the enticers' inner formation (heart trained in greed) produces outer behaviour that affects others' inner constitution. (2) *Collective hypocrisy*: Gal 2:13 — the social behaviour (outer — acting alongside others) reshapes the inner identity (Barnabas "led astray" — his inner moral orientation is redirected). (3) *Apostasy*: Act 21:21 — the inner departure from covenantal identity ("forsake" is an inner act of will) produces an outer change in practice (not circumcising, not walking in customs).

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes — the corpus evidences the condition moving across every constitutional level simultaneously. (1) *From spirit to body*: the condition's death-consequence (spiritual death — Eph 2:1) produces physical death (Rom 8:10 — "the body is dead because of sin"); (2) *Through the members*: Rom 7:23 — "the law of sin that dwells in my members" — the condition operates through the body's members as its instruments; (3) *Mind to body*: Rom 7:25 — "I myself serve the law of God with my mind, but with my flesh I serve the law of sin" — the condition creates a constitutional split between mind and flesh; (4) *From inner to outer*: Gen 4:7 — the predatory power crouches at the threshold between inner disposition and outer action.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Yes. The movement is from outer practice inward to constitutional identity. Joh 8:34 — "everyone who practices sin is a slave to sin" — the outer-level practice (sinning acts) produces the inner-level constitutional state (slavery). The direction is outer-practice → inner-captivity. Additionally, Gal 3:22 — "imprisoned everything under sin" — names a universal-structural confinement that operates across all constitutional levels simultaneously: everything is imprisoned, not merely specific faculties.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes — extensively evidenced. The record moves from inner (heart-level inscription — Jer 17:1) to outer (physical consequences — Psa 38:3; national consequences — Lev 26:18-28) and from outer consequences back to inner (the body's deterioration affecting the inner person — Psa 38:3 — "no health in my bones because of my sin" producing inner sorrow — Psa 38:18 — "I am sorry for my sin"). The record also moves from individual (chet — VCG-01 — personal liability) to corporate (VCG-04 — Jeroboam-sin affecting the whole nation) and back to individual (Deu 24:16 — each dies for their own sin).

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes. The movement is from outer to inner and from inner to restored. (1) *Outer-to-inner*: Lev 4:14 — the sin "becomes known" (external disclosure) → triggers inner recognition → volitional seeking begins; (2) *Inner-to-outer*: Lev 23:27 — "you shall afflict yourselves" — the inner posture of self-affliction is expressed through bodily behaviour; 2Ch 29:23 — "they laid their hands on them" — the inner identification with the offering is expressed through a bodily act; (3) *Outer-mechanism to inner-change*: the priestly blood ritual (outer) produces the condition of cleanness before God (inner relational standing — Lev 16:30); Christ's blood (outer historical event) produces the forgiveness of trespasses (inner debt cancelled — Eph 1:7).

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Yes. The characteristic moves from inner to outer and from outer-consequence back to inner. (1) *Inner-to-outer*: the ancestral sinning acts (Isa 43:27 — inner volitional acts) produce outer national consequences (Jer 8:14 — "doomed us to perish... has given us poisoned water to drink"); the inner sinning generates the outer catastrophic condition; (2) *Outer-consequence to inner-recognition*: the outer exile-condition (1Ki 8:47 — "the land to which they have been carried captive") produces the inner heart-turning and confession ("turn their heart... repent and plead"); the outer consequence drives the inner recognition.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes. The movement is from inner character outward to social expression and back inward through social reinforcement. (1) *Inner to outer*: the inner sinner-character produces outer social recognition — Mat 9:10/11 — the sinners' inner condition is expressed in their social association with tax collectors and recognised by the Pharisees; (2) *Outer to inner*: the social category of "sinner" shapes inner identity — Luk 18:13 — the tax collector's self-description "I am a sinner" reflects internalised social-moral verdict; (3) *Constitutional imputation to inner experience*: Rom 5:19 — "made sinners" through Adam — the constitutional outer-imputation produces the inner state of being-in-sin that Rom 5:8 names ("while we were still sinners").

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes — extensively. (1) *Inner conscience → outer confession/restitution*: Lev 5:5 — guilt-realisation (inner) → confession (speech-act) → restitution (outer conduct); Num 5:7 — "confess his sin... make full restitution" — the inner guilt-state produces outer corrective action; (2) *Inner weight → physical posture*: Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed and blush to lift my face" — the inner guilt-weight produces the outer physical posture of downcast face; (3) *Outer violation → inner guilt*: Lev 5:2/3/4 — the outer act (touching unclean thing, rash oath) produces the inner guilt-state when it "comes to knowledge"; (4) *Inner guilt → bodily consequence*: Eze 4:17 — "rot away because of their punishment" — the guilt-as-punitive-weight is expressed in bodily decay.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes — extensively. (1) *Inner heart → outer conduct*: Eze 14:3 — idols taken into the heart produce the stumbling block set before the face — the inner heart-level iniquity expresses outward; Job 15:5 — "your iniquity teaches your mouth" — the inner crime drives outer speech; (2) *Outer conduct → inner accumulation*: Psa 38:4 — acts of iniquity produce the accumulated inner weight that goes over the head; the outer acts generate the constitutional inner burden; (3) *Individual → communal/generational*: VCG-02 (Exo 20:5) — individual fathers' iniquity transmits to the community of descendants; the personal crime extends constitutionally to family lines; (4) *Inner → bodily*: Psa 31:10 — "my strength fails because of my iniquity, and my bones waste away" — the inner crime produces bodily constitutional decay.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes — extensively. (1) *Heart-inner to outer speech and act*: Psa 36:1 — transgression speaks deep in the heart → Isa 59:13 — "uttering from the heart lying words" → outer rebellion; (2) *Inner will → outer bodily consequence*: Lam 1:14 — "transgressions were bound into a yoke... set upon my neck; he caused my strength to fail" — the inner transgressions produce the bodily yoke and physical weakening; Isa 1:5 — inner revolt → "whole head is sick, whole heart faint" — constitutional physical-spiritual deterioration; (3) *Outer law-known → inner will crossing*: Rom 4:15 — the law (external) must exist before the inner will can generate the crossing — the constitutional movement is from external boundary to internal volitional act.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes. (1) *Spirit → will → outer act*: the spirit-level faithlessness (Mal 2:15 — requiring spirit-guarding) produces the will's allegiance-transfer (1Ch 5:25 — "broke faith with the God of their fathers, and whored after the gods") which produces outer acts (2Ch 36:14 — "polluted the house of the Lord"); (2) *Inner disposition → bodily consequence*: Num 5:27 — the wife who broke faith with her husband; "the water that brings the curse shall enter into her and cause bitter pain, and her womb shall swell, and her thigh shall fall away" — the inner faithlessness produces specific bodily physical consequences through the ordeal; (3) *Individual → communal*: Jos 7:1 — Achan's individual faithlessness; "the anger of the Lord burned against the people of Israel" — the inner betrayal of one person radiates outward to the whole community.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes — across multiple levels and directions. (1) *Heart → speech*: Pro 6:14 — "perverted heart devises evil" → discord sown outwardly; Pro 23:33 — "your heart utter perverse things" — heart-corruption expressing through mouth; (2) *Desire → progressive inner corruption*: Eph 4:22 — "corrupt through deceitful desires" — the desire-faculty drives corruption inward and outward through the old self's manner of life; (3) *Inner perversity → bodily consequence*: Psa 38:6 — "I am utterly bowed down and prostrate" — the inner-perversity produces bodily bowing; Num 5:27 (cross-reg) — physical consequence; (4) *Individual inner → communal*: Pro 6:14 — "continually sowing discord" — the perverted heart's output radiates outward into community disruption.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes — extensively. (1) *Heart → hands*: Psa 58:2 — "in your hearts you devise wrongs; your hands deal out violence on earth" — the explicit heart-to-hands sequence; Psa 7:3 — "if there is wrong in my hands" — the hands as the conduct-level expression of the inner moral state; (2) *Inner character → scaled behaviour*: Luk 16:10 — "dishonest in very little is also dishonest in much" — the inner character scales outward consistently to all behavioural contexts; (3) *Inner devising → social consequence*: Psa 64:6 — "they search out injustice... for the inward mind and heart of a man are deep" — the inward devising produces societal wrongdoing; Mic 3:10 — "build Zion with blood and Jerusalem with iniquity" — inner disposition produces civic corruption.

---

### T2.10.2

**Question:** What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The evidenced sequence is: *inner moral orientation (heart/will) → decision point → outward act → relational consequence*. Gen 39:9 (Joseph) shows the inner point — conscience names the act as "great wickedness" before the decision is made, then the decision point is the refusal. 1Sa 15:24 shows an alternative sequence: social pressure (external) → will-deflection (internal) → act of disobedience (outward). The cultic-atonement corpus (VCG-04) shows the post-act sequence: "the sin which he has committed is made known to him" (Lev 4:23) — the act precedes the realisation → realisation triggers the cultic obligation. Ecc 5:6 shows the mouth leading the person into sin — speech-organ as a site where inner restlessness externalises before the person has named it as sin.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The evidenced movement sequence is: *outward act (sin committed without inner awareness) → external information arrives (sin becomes known, Lev 5:5; angel appears, Num 22:34; report reaches Saul, 1Sa 14:33) → inner conscience engages (realisation of guilt) → outward remedy sought (confession, offering)*. The movement is thus outer → inner → outer: the sin begins in an outward act, processes through inner conscience, and resolves through outward ritual remedy. The characteristic mediates between the outer world (the act, the law's requirement) and the inner conscience (the moral realisation) through the knowledge-event.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The sequence evidenced most clearly in the paradigm cases is: (1) *Conscience fires* (heart struck — 2Sa 24:10; "knows that I have sinned" — 2Sa 19:20); (2) *Will agrees to name* (the decision to speak — Luk 15:18: "I will say"); (3) *Mouth speaks* (the confession enacted — Luk 15:21; Exo 9:27; Dan 9:5). This inner-to-outer sequence makes confession constitutionally a *completion event*: it completes what conscience began by bringing the inner recognition to external named expression. The sequence can be short (Exo 9:27 — Pharaoh responds quickly to plague) or extended (Dan 9:5/8/11/15 — Daniel's confession unfolds over many verses of sustained prayer).

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The evidenced sequence in the active-denial mode (Jer 2:35): (1) inner refusal of the conscience's registration (if any); (2) will claiming the false verdict; (3) speech enacting it outward ("you say, 'I am innocent'"). The reverse reinforcement loop: the spoken false claim shapes the inner self-understanding, deepening the suppression over time. This sequence makes the active-denial mode of conscience suppression self-perpetuating: the inner suppression produces the outer claim, and the outer claim deepens the inner suppression.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The evidenced sequence: (1) inherited sinful orientation received (the Jeroboam-sin pattern transmitted — 2Ki 15:9 "as his fathers had done"); (2) will's implicit choice not to depart ("did not depart from" — the pattern is accepted by non-rejection); (3) outer conduct continues in the sinful course ("walked in them" — 2Ki 13:6); (4) the outer conduct-pattern consolidates the inner refusal over time (from "did not depart" to "clung to" — 2Ki 3:3); (5) at advanced stages, the inner refusal becomes constitutional hardening ("stubborn shoulder... stiffened neck" — Neh 9:29). The sequence reveals a feedback loop: inner refusal → outer conduct → inner consolidation → constitutional hardening.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The evidenced sequence: (1) inner disposition of sinning orientation established (by repetition — Exo 9:34; by inherited pattern — Hos 10:9; by allegiance transfer — 2Ki 17:7); (2) outward expression through practice and institution (altars — Hos 8:11; worship of other gods — 2Ki 17:7); (3) outward structures feed back to reinforce inner orientation ("they have become to him altars for sinning" — Hos 8:11); (4) constitutional hardening deepens as the feedback loop runs (hardened heart — Exo 9:34). The sequence is a self-reinforcing inner-outer-inner cycle that deepens the habitual pattern with each iteration.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The evidenced sequence: (1) leader's personal inner commitment to the sinning course (walking in it — 1Ki 16:26); (2) leader exercises authority in the direction of that commitment (building sinning structures, driving the people from following the Lord — 2Ki 17:21; Jer 32:35); (3) authority-exercise transmits the sinning direction to the community (the Hiphil causative — "made Israel/Judah to sin"); (4) community adopts the transmitted sinning direction (walks in it, provokes God with idols — 1Ki 14:22); (5) the structural deposit persists beyond the leader's death (Jeroboam's altar still transmitting — 2Ki 23:15). The constitutional movement thus crosses from individual inner being to community to permanent structure.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The sequence evidenced in 2Ch 21:10: (1) Jehoram's inner act of forsaking the Lord ("because he had forsaken the Lord, the God of his fathers"); (2) the withdrawal of divine legitimacy from his governing authority (implied — the Lord who is forsaken no longer sustains the authority structure); (3) outer political revolts as the consequence (Edom and Libnah revolt). The sequence is inner spiritual abandonment → political-authority vacuum → external revolts. This is the only verse in the corpus that evidences constitutional-level movement; the remaining verses address the political acts without the inner-constitutional causal chain.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The sequence evidenced in Mat 15:19: (1) the heart's moral corruption (inner origin — "evil thoughts"); (2) the will's consent to externalise the corruption as speech; (3) the speech act through the mouth ("slander" as the named output); (4) the speech reaches the relational target (God or persons — directed outward). Col 3:8 — "put them all away... from your mouth" — the mouth is named as the point of externalisation that the renunciation command addresses. The sequence is linear: inner corruption → volitional expression → bodily-speech act → relational impact.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — The sequences vary by mechanism. (1) *Enticement*: inner desire-faculty (the hook) → bait presented (external) → desire engaged → person drawn inward toward the temptation's object → sinful act produced. 2Pe 2:14's enticers: inner training (heart formed toward greed) → outer practice of enticing others → their inner constitution affected ("unsteady souls" captured). (2) *Hypocrisy*: outer social pressure (others acting hypocritically) → inner identity-performance adopted → authentic inner identity displaced. (3) *Apostasy*: inner departure decision (will choosing to stand away from) → outer practice changed (not circumcising — Act 21:21).

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The constitutional movement is multi-directional rather than single-sequence. (1) *Downward*: Rom 5:12 — "sin came into the world... and death spread to all" — sin enters (cosmic level) → death spreads (to all persons, at every constitutional level). (2) *Inward*: Rom 7:8/9 — the commandment arrives → sin seizes the opportunity → sin comes alive within the person → the person dies; the sequence is external stimulus (law) → internal activation (sin comes alive in the members) → total-person consequence (death). (3) *Bidirectional body-spirit*: Rom 8:10 — "the body is dead because of sin, the Spirit is life because of righteousness" — the condition's hold on the body is contrasted with the Spirit's life-giving work in the inner person simultaneously.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — The sequence evidenced in Joh 8:34: (1) practice of sinning (outer volitional acts); (2) the practice produces enslavement (inner constitutional state); (3) the enslaved state governs the will (inner → inner feedback: the captive will cannot exit). The sequence is: outer acts → inner enslavement → inner governance of the will's freedom. For Gal 3:22: the imprisonment is structural and all-at-once (everything under sin), not sequential — the constitutional confinement is a starting-state rather than a process.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Multiple movement sequences are evidenced. (1) *Inner-to-outer*: Deu 15:9 — "an unworthy thought in your heart" → grudging eye → withholding → the worker's cry reaching God → the employer "guilty of sin" — the sequence runs from inner thought to outer social act to divine register; (2) *Record-to-consequence*: Lev 26:18/21/24/28 — accumulated sins → sevenfold divine discipline — the stored record triggers covenant consequences; (3) *Individual-to-corporate*: VCG-04 — Jeroboam's personal sin → "he made Israel to sin" (1Ki 14:16) — the individual leader's recorded sin becomes the nation's recorded inheritance; (4) *Record-to-separation*: Isa 59:2 — accumulated sins → God's face hidden → prayer not heard — the record moves progressively from inner condition to outer relational consequence.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — The sequence across registers. (1) *Levitical sequence*: sin committed (inner act) → sin made known (recognition) → seeking initiated (will's movement) → offering brought (outer bodily act) → priestly mediation (institutional mechanism) → atonement accomplished (outer ritual completion) → cleanness before God (inner relational status change). (2) *NT sequence*: repentance (inner volitional turn) → baptism (outer bodily act) → forgiveness declared (relational status change) → Spirit received (spirit-level constitutional change — Act 2:38). (3) *Christological sequence*: Christ's blood poured out (outer historical event) → covenant established (relational framework) → forgiveness of sins (inner debt cancelled) → alive replacing dead (constitutional change — Col 2:13).

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The movement sequence evidenced in 1Ki 8:47 and Jer 8:14: (1) ancestral sinning acts (inner) → accumulated moral condition across generations → outer covenant-judgment (exile, doom, poisoned water); (2) outer consequence (captivity, doom) → inner recognition and heart-turning → corporate confession ("we have sinned"). The sequence is: inner-sinning-acts → outer-judgment-consequences → inner-repentance-recognition → (potential) divine-restoration. The outer catastrophe serves as the mechanism that drives the inner sequence from acknowledgment to potential restoration.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Two sequences. (1) *Formation sequence*: inner sinning acts (CHAR-1) accumulate → habitual pattern forms → inner moral character constituted as "sinner" → outer social recognition follows → social categorisation reinforces the identity. (2) *Imputation sequence*: Adam's disobedience (historical outer act) → "made sinners" (constitutional inner status imputed) → Rom 5:8 "still sinners" (inner condition experienced) → outer life shaped by the constituted status. Both sequences confirm: the sinner-identity moves between constitutional inner and social outer dimensions, mutually reinforcing.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Two primary sequences. (1) *Violation-to-guilt-to-remedy sequence*: outer act (sin/violation) → hidden → comes to knowledge → inner guilt-recognition (Lev 5:2-5) → inner guilt-state → inner confession → outer restitution; (2) *Accumulation-to-consequence sequence*: repeated violations → mounting guilt (Ezr 9:6 — "mounted up to the heavens") → divine judgment (outer consequences: captivity, sword — Ezr 9:7) → inner recognition (shame — Ezr 9:6) → corporate acknowledgment. Both sequences confirm: guilt moves between the inner (conscience-recognition, shame, weight) and the outer (violation that causes it, confession and restitution that address it, bodily/national consequences it produces).

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Two primary sequences. (1) *Heart-to-conduct-to-accumulation sequence*: heart takes in idols (VCG-08 — Eze 14:3) → outer conduct of iniquity → accumulation in divine record (VCG-03 — Hos 13:12 — "bound up") → weight on the person (VCG-05 — Psa 38:4) → separation from God (Isa 59:2); (2) *Confession-to-removal sequence*: iniquity acknowledged (Lev 26:40 — "confess their iniquity and the iniquity of their fathers") → heart humbled (Lev 26:41) → priestly bearing (VCG-01 — Lev 16:21/22) → iniquity removed (VCG-06 — Isa 40:2; Zec 3:4). Both sequences confirm bidirectional constitutional movement: inward generation → outward consequence; inward acknowledgment → outward resolution.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Primary sequence: (1) boundary established externally (divine law/covenant — Rom 4:15); (2) boundary known internally (cognitive awareness — Psa 36:1 — transgression speaks from within); (3) will chooses to cross (volitional act — Isa 1:2 — "they have rebelled"); (4) act produces constitutional damage (Isa 1:5 — head sick, heart faint; Lam 1:14 — yoke on neck); (5) accumulation moves toward divine threshold (Amos 1:3 — "three... and for four"). Secondary (remedy) sequence: internal recognition → volitional turning (Eze 18:28 — "considered and turned away") → external confession (Psa 32:5) → divine pardon (Psa 103:12 — removed as far as east from west).

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Primary sequence: (1) spirit-level vulnerability (Mal 2:15 — spirit requiring guarding); (2) will's allegiance-orientation (1Ch 5:25 — transferring loyalty to false gods); (3) outer act of covenant-breaking (Lev 26:40 — "treachery they committed against me"); (4) communal consequence (Jos 7:1 — divine anger against all Israel); (5) national-eschatological consequence (1Ch 9:1 — exile; Dan 9:7 — open shame in all lands). The sequence confirms: inner spirit → volitional act → outer deed → communal impact → national judgment. Secondary (reversal) sequence: Lev 26:40 — "if they confess their iniquity and... treachery" → Lev 26:42 — "I will remember my covenant" — confession reverses the sequence toward restoration.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Two primary sequences. (1) *Heart-to-conduct-to-consequence*: perverted heart (Pro 6:14 — inner) → devises evil → sows discord (outer communal) → ruin (Pro 13:6 — the wicked overthrown); (2) *Desire-to-corruption-to-slavery*: deceitful desires (Eph 4:22 — desire-level) → actively corrupt the old self → enslave the will (2Pe 2:19 — "slaves of corruption"). Both sequences confirm: perversion moves from the innermost level (heart/desire) outward to conduct and consequence, and inward to progressive self-corruption and volitional bondage.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Primary sequence: (1) God-ignorance at the heart-level (Psa 53:1 — "no God in heart") → (2) heart devises injustice (Psa 58:2 — "in your hearts you devise wrongs") → (3) hands enact the devised wrong (Psa 58:2 — "your hands deal out violence on earth") → (4) social-civic corruption (Mic 3:10 — "build Zion with blood") → (5) divine judgment (Pro 22:8 — "reap calamity"; 2Pe 2:9 — kept under punishment). Secondary (reversal) sequence: Eze 18:8 — "withholds his hand from injustice" (volitional restraint) → "executes true justice between man and man" (conduct-level) → "he shall surely live" (divine affirmation).

---

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Constitutional movement is evidenced (T2.10.1 and T2.10.2), though it is act-to-conscience rather than spirit-soul-body level movement. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Constitutional movement is evidenced (T2.10.1 and T2.10.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-5]** E — Constitutional movement is evidenced (T2.10.1 and T2.10.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Constitutional movement is extensively evidenced across all levels (T2.10.1 and T2.10.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Constitutional movement is evidenced across all registers (T2.10.1 and T2.10.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Constitutional movement (inner → outer → inner) is evidenced (T2.10.1 and T2.10.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Constitutional movement is extensively evidenced (T2.10.1 and T2.10.2). This prompt is superseded.
