## T2.2 — Soul-Level Location

### T2.2.1

**Question:** Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Yes. Eze 18:4 employs the nephesh (soul) term explicitly: "the soul of the father as well as the soul of the son is mine: the soul who sins shall die." Eze 18:20 repeats: "the soul who sins shall die." These declarations locate wilful sinning explicitly at the soul level — the individual nephesh is the unit of moral accountability. The soul is the locus of both the sinning act and its mortal consequence. This is the most explicit constitutional location in the entire corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Limited soul-level language. Lev 5:1 — "he shall bear his iniquity" — the bearing of iniquity is a soul-level statement in that the person as moral subject carries the moral liability. Num 15:27 ("if one person sins unintentionally") — the Hebrew nefesh appears in the construct ("nefesh echad ki tekheta bishgagah" — "if one soul sins unintentionally"), explicitly naming the individual soul as the subject of unintentional sinning. This is the clearest soul-level identification in the corpus: the soul is the moral unit that sins unintentionally and bears the liability.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Limited soul-level language. Lev 5:1 (adjacent context within M10-L corpus) uses "he shall bear his iniquity" — the bearing involves the soul. Within the CHAR-3 corpus proper, Mic 7:9 — "I will bear the indignation of the Lord because I have sinned against him" — names the confessor bearing divine indignation at the soul level: the person accepts the weight of God's displeasure upon themselves as the consequence of the sin they confess. The soul-level dimension is present in this bearing-capacity: the confessor who accepts indignation is engaging their whole personal self (nefesh-level) with the moral reality of what they have done.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The soul-level is implicated through the *nefesh*-level moral accountability that conscience suppression resists. Jer 2:35 — "I will bring you to judgment" — the judgment falls on the person as a moral subject (soul-level accountability). Job 35:6 — "If you have sinned, what do you accomplish against him?" — Elihu's argument addresses Job as a moral subject whose sin's effect returns to the sinner themselves (soul-level consequence). The conscience-suppression characteristic operates at the soul level in that it is the *nefesh* (the whole personal self) that fails to register or denies the moral reality of its own sin.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Eze 18:24 — "the sin he has committed, for them he shall die" — the death-consequence falls on the person as moral subject; the former-righteous person who turns to sin and does not turn back bears the consequence at the soul level (nefesh-level accountability). Eze 33:12 — "the righteous shall not be able to live by his righteousness when he sins" — the life/death framing (fundamental to nefesh-level existence) applies to the person who sins without turning back. The soul-level location is confirmed by the mortality consequence: the person who refuses to repent from sin is the soul that is under mortal judgment.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The universality statements locate habitual defection at the soul/nefesh level. 1Ki 8:46 — "there is no one who does not sin" — the universal scope applies to all persons as soul-level moral subjects. The person-type formulations (Pro 11:31 — "the sinner"; Ecc 9:2 — "the sinner... as the good one is, so is the sinner") present the habitually sinning person as a constituted moral identity — a soul-level characterisation rather than a situational description.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Soul-level (nefesh-level) accountability is evidenced through the divine charge to individual leaders. 1Ki 21:22 — God addresses Ahab as a personal moral subject: "because you have made Israel to sin" — the moral accountability is at the soul level of the individual leader: they personally bear the consequence for what their transmitted sinning produced in the community. 2Ki 21:17 — "the sin that he committed, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles" — Manasseh's personal sin is recorded, naming the soul-level moral account. The leaders are held as individual moral subjects for their contagious sinning.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Soul-level (nefesh-level) accountability is implied through the moral-weight dimension of pa.sha. The political revolt carried the full moral weight of transgression (pa.sha as wilful breaking-away — the same root as CHAR-19). The revolting parties (Moab, Edom, Libnah, Israel) are moral subjects whose revolt is a morally accountable act. 2Ch 21:10's causal chain — Jehoram's personal forsaking of the Lord — locates the originating moral-subject at the soul level: the person who forsakes the Lord bears soul-level moral accountability for the political consequences that follow.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The soul-level (nefesh-level moral subject) is engaged through the moral accountability dimension: Mat 12:31 — blasphemy against the Spirit carries permanent consequence for the person as a moral subject before God — the soul-level accountability is engaged at its most severe. 1Ti 1:13 — Paul as a former blasphemer bears personal moral accountability that required divine mercy. The practitioner of sinful speech is a moral subject whose speech is held to account at the soul level.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Soul-level (nefesh-level) engagement is evidenced through personal moral accountability. Jam 1:14 — "each person is tempted when he is lured and enticed by his own desire" — the "each person" universalises the soul-level engagement: every moral subject is susceptible to enticement through their own desire. Gal 2:13 — "even Barnabas was led astray" — Barnabas as a named individual moral subject bears the soul-level moral accountability for his participation in the hypocrisy.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes. Rom 3:23 — "all have sinned" — the "all" applies to every soul-level moral subject without exception: the universal scope names every person as a moral subject under the condition. Rom 6:17 — "you who were once slaves of sin have become obedient from the heart" — the heart-obedience that conversion involves confirms that the prior sin-condition was at the soul level (heart-slavery). The condition is thus a soul-level structural reality: every person as a moral-subject-before-God stands in this condition from birth (Joh 9:34).

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Yes. Joh 8:34 — "everyone who practices sin is a slave to sin" — "everyone" names every moral subject (soul-level) without exception who practices sin; the slavery is a soul-level condition affecting the whole person as a moral subject. 1Jo 3:8 — "whoever makes a practice of sinning is of the devil" — the "of the devil" is a soul-level identity-marker: the whole person's deepest belonging is what is at stake. The enslaving power engages the soul-level because it addresses the person's fundamental identity and governing allegiance.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes. Mic 6:7 — "the sin of my soul" — the soul is explicitly named as the locus of the sin requiring atonement. The soul-level location is confirmed through the personal accountability language: chet (VCG-01) — "each one shall be put to death for his own sin" (Deu 24:16) — the "own sin" is owned at the soul level of the individual person as a moral subject. The characteristic's definition — "the person carries this record whether they feel it or not" — names the soul-level person as the carrier.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes. Luk 7:47/48 — the woman's sins forgiven and her love-response — the forgiveness is received at the soul level of the person as a moral subject; it is her own sin-record that is addressed and her own love that responds. Lev 23:27 — "you shall afflict yourselves" — the self-affliction is a soul-level inner posture of the whole person before God. Act 2:38 — "repent and be baptized every one of you" — the "every one of you" names individual soul-level moral subjects each making the seeking-movement.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Yes. 1Ki 8:47 — "if they turn their heart in the land to which they have been carried captive, and repent and plead with you" — the heart-turning is a soul-level act; the repentance is the will's movement; the pleading is the whole-person's appeal to God. The corporate "we" of the confession (1Ki 8:47; Jer 8:14) names each member of the community as a soul-level moral subject participating in the corporate condition.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes. Luk 5:8 — "I am a sinful man, O Lord" — Peter's whole-person self-identification as a sinful man is a soul-level moral identity claim; Psa 26:9 — "do not sweep my soul away with sinners" — the soul is the entity at risk of being swept into the sinner's fate. Jam 5:20 — "whoever brings back a sinner from his wandering will save his soul from death" — the sinner's soul is the entity endangered by the sinner-identity's trajectory toward death. The sinner-identity thus engages the whole person as soul-level moral subject.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes. Gen 4:13 — "my punishment is greater than I can bear" — Cain's experience of unbearable punitive guilt is a soul-level existential statement: the whole person (soul-level) is overwhelmed; 1Sa 25:31 (pu.qah) — "pangs of conscience" — the conscience-stagger is a soul-level disruption of the person's inner equilibrium. Psa 65:3 — "when iniquities prevail against me" — the iniquities pressing against the person is a soul-level experience of guilt's weight.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes. Eze 18:20 — "the soul who sins shall die. The son shall not suffer for the iniquity of the father" — the soul is the entity that bears the personal iniquity and its death-consequence; iniquity is constitutively a soul-level moral attachment. Psa 40:12 — "my iniquities have overtaken me... my heart fails me" — the soul-level collapse under the weight of iniquity; the iniquities have overtaken the person's inner core.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes. Mic 6:7 — "shall I give my firstborn for my transgression, the fruit of my body for the sin of my soul?" — transgression is explicitly linked to the sin of the soul (*nepeš*); the soul is named as the site of the transgression's originating sinfulness. Psa 51:3 — "I know my transgressions, and my sin is ever before me" — the knowing and ever-present awareness is a soul-level existential condition; the transgression is experienced as a sustained inner-personal reality.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes. Eze 18:24 — "but when a righteous person turns away from his righteousness and does injustice... for the treachery of which he is guilty and the sin he has committed, for them he shall die" — the soul (*nepeš* implied in "he shall die") is the entity whose life is forfeit for the treachery; faithlessness is a soul-level moral liability. Pro 11:6 — "the treacherous are taken captive by their lust" — the lust-captivity is a soul-level bondage of the person's innermost desiring faculty.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes. 2Pe 2:19 — "For whatever overcomes a person, to that he is enslaved" — the person (*anthrōpos* — the whole human being) is the entity enslaved by corruption; Jude 10 — "destroyed by all that they, like unreasoning animals, understand instinctively" — the person's whole being is destroyed by instinct-driven corruption. Dan 9:5 — "we have sinned and done wrong and acted wickedly" — the communal self-assessment names perversity as a whole-person condition.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes — through the whole-person character passages. Luk 16:10 — "one who is dishonest in a very little is also dishonest in much" — the dishonesty is a character-property of the person (*anthrōpos*) at the whole-person level; 1Pe 3:18 — "the righteous for the unrighteous" — the *adikos* is named as the whole-person moral category; 2Pe 2:9 — "the unrighteous under punishment" — the whole person is held under divine custody for their injustice.

---

### T2.2.2

**Question:** What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Soul-level location in Eze 18:4/20 (nephesh) reveals that wilful sinning is constitutionally deep — it is not merely a surface behaviour but an act that engages the person's innermost self as the responsible agent. The soul here is the irreducible personal subject: "the soul who sins alone shall die" — the personal self cannot delegate the sinning to social forces, ancestry, or circumstance. This locates wilful sinning within the person's inalienable moral selfhood. The consequence (death) follows the soul-as-agent, not a transferred entity.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Soul-level location (Num 15:27 — nefesh as subject) reveals that unintentional sinning is attributed to the whole person as a moral unit — the soul is accountable for what the person did even without deliberate intent. The soul-location confirms that moral accountability is not conditioned on intentionality: the nefesh that sinned unintentionally bears the same kind of moral liability as the nefesh that sinned wilfully, though the prescribed remedy differs in scale. This reveals that in the Levitical framework, moral liability is constitutional — it attaches to the person (nefesh) regardless of the inner quality of the will at the moment of action.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Mic 7:9's bearing of divine indignation post-confession reveals that genuine confession involves a soul-level acceptance of moral consequence: not just the verbal naming but the accepting of the weight that follows — "I will bear the indignation of the Lord because I have sinned against him." This is the whole personal self engaged with the consequences of the named sin. It distinguishes genuine confession (which includes this acceptance) from hollow confession (VCG-03 — Deu 1:41 — where the words are spoken but the self does not accept the weight of what they imply, immediately proceeding autonomously).

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Soul-level location reveals that conscience suppression is not a peripheral cognitive failure but a failure of the whole personal self to receive its own moral reality. The *nefesh* that denies "I have not sinned" (Jer 2:35) is the whole personal subject claiming a false moral standing before God — a total-person moral position, not merely an intellectual error. This is what makes it so serious: the entire inner person has aligned itself against the truth of its own moral condition.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Soul-level location (Eze 18:24; 33:12) reveals that refusal to repent is not a peripheral moral failure but a soul-level condition that determines the person's fundamental standing before God. The life/death language — "for them he shall die" (Eze 18:24) — places refusal to repent at the deepest level of creaturely existence. The soul that persistently sins without turning back is the soul under mortal judgment. This deepens the gravity of the Kings pattern: each king who "did not depart from the sins of Jeroboam" was carrying a soul-level moral condition that, according to Ezekiel's framework, was life-threatening.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Soul-level location (through universality — 1Ki 8:46; Ecc 7:20 — and person-type — Pro 11:31/13:22; Ecc 9:2) reveals that habitual defection is not a peripheral or temporary condition but a characterisation of the person as a moral subject. The sinner-type terms describe a whole-person moral orientation: "the sinner" is what the person *is* at the soul level — their settled moral identity — not merely what they do occasionally. 1Jo 3:6's "no one who keeps on sinning has either seen him or known him" places the habitual sinning at the level of fundamental spiritual knowing — a soul-level epistemic-relational condition.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Soul-level accountability (1Ki 21:22; 2Ki 21:17) reveals that contagious sin does not dissolve the leader's personal moral responsibility into the community — the leader remains fully accountable as a moral subject for what they transmitted. The community's sinning does not reduce the leader's guilt; God explicitly holds the leader accountable for the community's sinning as the leader's own act. This is the reverse of the expectation: if anything, the transmitted sinning amplifies the leader's moral accountability (their sinning affected not just themselves but the whole community).

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Soul-level location (via the moral-accountability dimension of pa.sha and the personal forsaking in 2Ch 21:10) reveals that political revolt is not merely a political-social event but a moral act for which the persons involved bear personal accountability. The pa.sha root's moral weight confirms this: revolt is not merely a political-strategic decision but a transgressive act that carries moral consequence before God's covenantal order.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Soul-level location (Mat 12:31; 1Ti 1:13) reveals that sinful speech is not merely a social failing but a soul-level moral act: the person who blasphemes or slanders bears the moral weight of what they have said at the deepest level of their personal accountability before God. Mat 12:31's unforgivable blasphemy makes this most explicit: the soul-level consequence is total and permanent — the person's moral standing before God is permanently altered by this specific form of sinful speech.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Soul-level location (Jam 1:14 — "each person"; Gal 2:13 — Barnabas as individual moral subject) reveals that these mechanisms, despite their composite and mechanism-focused nature, engage real individual moral subjects who bear accountability for their response. The mechanisms are not impersonal forces but pathways through which individual persons are morally engaged and potentially captured. Jam 1:14's "his own desire" — the possessive — confirms: the enticement mechanism is person-specific; the desire that is the hook belongs to the individual person.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Soul-level location (Rom 3:23 — universal moral subjects; Rom 6:17 — heart-enslaved) reveals that sin as universal condition is not a peripheral social or behavioural phenomenon but a structural reality at the level of the person as a moral subject. Every moral subject's self-determination, identity, and accountability before God is shaped by this condition. The condition does not merely constrain behaviour but constitutes the person's standing: Eph 2:1 — "dead" — the soul-level life that the person requires for relation with God is absent due to the condition.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Soul-level location (Joh 8:34 — everyone; 1Jo 3:8 — whoever) reveals that sin's enslaving power does not target only one faculty (e.g. the will) but constitutes the whole person as a slave. The slave-identity is a total-person condition; every faculty operates within the slave-status. The soul-level enslaving means that liberation requires a total-person transformation (new birth — 1Jo 3:9) rather than faculty-specific correction.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Soul-level location (Mic 6:7 — "sin of my soul") reveals that the divine record is not merely a legal external notation but is carried at the level of the person's innermost selfhood. The soul is the level at which the record produces its most personal burden: Psa 51:3 — "my sin is ever before me" — the persistent inner presence of the record is a soul-level experience of the divine accounting. Every moral subject as a soul carries a sin-record; this is what makes the characteristic universal at the soul level.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Soul-level location (Luk 7:47 — her sins; Lev 23:27 — self-affliction; Act 2:38 — every one of you) reveals that forgiveness sought and received is irreducibly personal: every moral subject must make the seeking-movement individually and receive the forgiveness individually. Col 2:13 — "having forgiven us all our trespasses" — the corporate "us" does not eliminate the individual dimension; the characteristic operates at the soul level of each person as a moral subject, not merely as a collective event.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Soul-level location (1Ki 8:47 — heart-turning; Jer 8:14 — "we have sinned") reveals that generational sin, though corporate in origin, engages the individual soul-level moral subject: each person who confesses "we have sinned" participates personally in the corporate condition's acknowledgment. The characteristic is not merely an external legal-status imputed from outside but is genuinely carried at the soul level of each community member who stands within the lineage.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Soul-level location (Luk 5:8 — "sinful man"; Psa 26:9 — soul swept away; Jam 5:20 — soul saved from death) reveals that the sinner-identity is not merely a social label or external imputation but penetrates to the innermost personal identity: the soul is endangered by the identity (Jam 5:20 — heading toward death), is at risk of contagion from others who bear it (Psa 26:9), and spontaneously recognises itself through it (Luk 5:8). The characteristic thus operates at the soul's constitutive level.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Soul-level location (Gen 4:13 — unbearable; 1Sa 25:31 — conscience-stagger; Psa 65:3 — iniquities prevailing) reveals that guilt-as-inner-state engages the whole person as soul-level moral subject. The guilt is not merely cognitive recognition or legal status but a felt condition of the whole inner person — Cain's "I cannot bear it" names the soul's total engagement with the punitive weight of guilt. The soul is the locus where the objective guilt-record (CHAR-13) is experienced subjectively as unbearable weight (CHAR-17).

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Soul-level location (Eze 18:20 — "the soul who sins shall die"; Psa 40:12 — "my heart fails me") reveals that iniquity-as-accumulated-crime is not merely a legal abstraction but attaches to the whole person at their deepest level. Eze 18:20's "the soul who sins" uses *nepeš* as the total-person subject of iniquity: the iniquity belongs to the whole person (soul) not merely a faculty. The death-consequence falls on the soul-level entity; the iniquity is the soul's personal crime.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Soul-level location (Mic 6:7 — "sin of my soul"; Psa 51:3 — "ever before me") reveals that transgression-as-deliberate-boundary-crossing is not merely a legal category but a soul-level moral reality that the person inhabits. The "ever before me" (Psa 51:3) names the sustained soul-level experiential weight of the acknowledged transgression. Mic 6:7's "sin of my soul" names the soul (*nepeš*) as the total-person subject of the transgression — the crossing implicates the whole person at their innermost level, not merely a faculty or action.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Soul-level location (Eze 18:24 — death for treachery; Pro 11:6 — soul-level lust-captivity) reveals that faithlessness is not merely a legal status or behavioural pattern but attaches to the whole person at their innermost level. Eze 18:24's death-verdict for treachery names the soul as the entity bearing the full weight of the faithlessness-consequence. The lust-captivity of Pro 11:6 names the soul's desiring faculty as captured by the very desire that drove the faithlessness.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Soul-level location (2Pe 2:19 — whole-person enslavement; Jude 10 — whole-person destruction) reveals that perversion-as-inner-inversion is not compartmentalised to one faculty but encompasses the whole inner person. The slavery of 2Pe 2:19 is total: whatever overcomes the person (*anthrōpos*) enslaves the person — the entire person is subject to the corruption's mastery. Jude 10's destruction by instinct similarly encompasses the whole person.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Soul-level location (Luk 16:10 — whole-person character; 1Pe 3:18 — person-category; 2Pe 2:9 — whole-person divine custody) reveals that injustice is not compartmentalised to specific acts but constitutes the person's moral character at the whole-person level. Luk 16:10's scaling from small to large confirms: the inner character of injustice pervades the whole-person across all behavioural contexts, making CHAR-22 a soul-level character trait rather than merely a collection of specific unjust acts.

---

**Question:** If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*
