## T2.3 — Heart

### T2.3.1

**Question:** Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Yes. Job 1:5 provides the clearest heart-location: "It may be that my children have sinned, and cursed God in their hearts" — sinning is here explicitly an inner-heart act, a cursing of God not yet externalised in speech or visible deed but real and culpable in its heart-location. Psa 119:11 ("I have stored up your word in my heart, that I might not sin against you") presupposes that the heart is the site where the battle against sinning is fought and won — the heart's inner repository of the word is what keeps the will from sinning. Psa 51:4 ("against you, you only, have I sinned and done what is evil in your sight") is contextually heart-language, located within Psalm 51's entire heart-renewal discourse.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — The 18-verse corpus contains no explicit heart-location for unintentional sinning. The heart (lev/lebab) does not appear in the CHAR-2 evidence base. This is analytically significant given that CHAR-1's wilful sinning has heart-location (Job 1:5 — "cursed God in their hearts"): the absence of heart-language in the unintentional sinning corpus confirms that unintentional sinning does not originate from the heart's moral orientation in the same way as wilful sinning. The characteristic bypasses the heart's deliberative centre precisely because it lacks the knowing, willing character that engages the heart.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Yes. 2Sa 24:10 is the clearest heart-location: "David's heart struck him after he had numbered the people." The heart (lev) is named as the faculty that initiates the confessional sequence — the conscience-in-the-heart fires before any external word arrives, producing the confession to God that follows. This is the paradigm case: the heart as the originating inner location of genuine confession.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(S)*

**[CHAR-4]** S — The 8-verse corpus does not explicitly name the heart (lev/lebab) in connection with conscience suppression. The characteristic operates at the conscience and cognitive level without explicit heart-location language.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Yes. 2Ki 10:31 — "he did not turn from the sins of Jeroboam... He did not turn from the sins of Jeroboam, which he made Israel to sin" — the preceding clause is explicit: "He was not careful to walk in the law of the Lord, the God of Israel, with all his *heart*." The heart is named as the site of the incomplete commitment that produces refusal to turn. "Not with all his heart" is the heart-level diagnosis of what enables refusal to repent: the heart's divided state — partially oriented elsewhere — allows the sinful course to continue.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Yes. Exo 9:34 — "he sinned yet again and *hardened his heart*, he and his servants" — the heart is explicitly named as the site of the hardening that drives repeated sinning. The heart is the inner constitutional centre that is being progressively hardened through the sinning-and-hardening cycle: each act of sinning hardens the heart, making the next sinning more natural and the heart more resistant to turning.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-7]** S — The 19-verse corpus does not explicitly name the heart (lev/lebab) in connection with contagious sin. The characteristic is expressed through volitional verbs (walked, made, drove, built) and the Hiphil causative rather than through explicit heart-location language. The heart's implicit engagement is through the will, but the vocabulary does not name the heart directly.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — The 9-verse corpus does not explicitly name the heart (lev/lebab) in connection with political revolt. The characteristic is expressed through political-social actions (revolted, rebelled, set up a king) rather than through explicit heart-location language.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Yes — explicitly. Mat 15:19 — "out of the heart come evil thoughts, murder, adultery, sexual immorality, theft, false witness, *slander*" — the heart is named as the origin of slander. Mar 7:22 — slander appears in the list of evils that originate from within (the broader passage, Mar 7:21 — "from within, out of the heart of man, come evil thoughts"). The heart is the explicit constitutional location of sinful speech's origin.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Yes — explicitly for enticement. 2Pe 2:14 — "they have *hearts* trained in greed" — the heart is the explicitly named constitutional locus of the enticement-apparatus: the enticers' hearts have been trained toward sinful appetite. Jam 1:14's "desire" (epithumia) is a heart-faculty term. For hypocrisy and apostasy, the heart is not explicitly named in the corpus.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes. Heb 3:13 — "hardened by the deceitfulness of sin" — the heart is the site of the hardening that sin's deceitfulness produces; the condition operates through deceit on the heart's moral responsiveness. Rom 6:17 — "obedient from the heart to the standard of teaching to which you were committed" — the former slavery to sin was a heart-level condition from which the person has been freed; the heart is the site of the prior sin-enslavement and of the subsequent obedience. Gen 4:7 — sin crouching at the door is addressed to Cain's will, which is centred in the heart.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — The 9-verse corpus does not explicitly name the heart in connection with sin's enslaving power. The characteristic operates through will-captivity and identity-allegiance without explicit heart-location vocabulary in this corpus.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes — most explicitly in the corpus. Jer 17:1 — "the sin of Judah is written with a pen of iron; with a point of diamond it is engraved on the tablet of their heart" (VCG-02) — the heart is explicitly named as the internal inscription-site of the divine record. The record is not only before God externally but engraved within at the heart's constitutional centre. Additionally: Deu 15:9 — "an unworthy thought in your heart" — the heart is where the sin originates before it enters the divine record; 1Ki 15:3 — "his heart was not wholly true to the Lord his God" — the divided heart's state is the inner source of the sin-pattern walked in.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes — implicitly through the inner-disposition requirements. Lev 10:19 — Aaron's question about whether eating the sin offering while grief-stricken "would the Lord have approved" — implies the heart's inner state affects the ritual's acceptance; the heart's condition (grief, affliction) is relevant to whether the seeking is rightly oriented. Lev 23:27 — "you shall afflict yourselves" — self-affliction in the Day of Atonement seeking is a heart-level posture, not merely an external act. The seeking posture required is at the heart level.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Yes. 1Ki 8:47 — "if they turn their heart in the land to which they have been carried captive, and repent" — the heart is explicitly named as the constitutional centre of the turning-toward-God movement; the heart is also implicitly the site of the prior condition that needs turning from. The heart's wrongly-oriented condition (having produced or sustained the generational sinning) requires turning as the response.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes. Jam 4:8 — "cleanse your hands, you sinners, and purify your hearts, you double-minded" — the parallel structure calls sinners to hand-cleansing while the double-minded are called to heart-purification; the heart is the complementary inner locus alongside the sinner's outer conduct. Pro 23:17 — "let not your heart envy sinners" — the heart is the faculty that can be drawn toward the sinner's apparent prosperity; the sinner-identity operates on the heart of those who observe sinners. Mar 8:38 — "this adulterous and sinful generation" — the "adulterous" (*moichalis*) naming of the generation implies a heart-level condition (adultery in Markan usage includes the heart's divided allegiance — cf. Mar 7:21).

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes. Hos 10:2 — "their heart is false; now they must bear their guilt" — the false heart is explicitly named as the inner source that generates the guilt-burden; the heart's condition is what produces the guilt the person must bear. The heart-guilt connection is direct: false heart → guilt borne. Additionally: Gen 42:21 — "we saw the distress of his soul" — the brothers' conscience recognises that they ignored another's soul-distress; the conscience's retrospective assessment operates at the heart-level of moral awareness.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes — centrally in VCG-08. Eze 14:3 — "these men have taken their idols into their hearts, and set the stumbling block of their iniquity before their faces" — the heart is the explicit origin of the iniquity; the idols are taken into the heart as an act of will; Eze 14:4/7 repeat this heart-location pattern. Job 31:33 — "if I have concealed my transgressions as others do by hiding my iniquity in my heart" — the heart is the hiding-place of deliberately concealed iniquity; the crime can be buried at the heart-level to avoid acknowledgment.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes — most explicitly in the corpus. Psa 36:1 — "transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart; there is no fear of God before his eyes" — the heart is the named site from which transgression speaks; its location "deep in the heart" (*qereb*) names the innermost centre of the person. Isa 59:13 — "conceiving and uttering from the heart lying words" — revolt is conceived at the heart-level before outward utterance. Eze 18:31 — "cast away from you all the transgressions... and make yourselves a new heart and a new spirit!" — the remedy is a new heart, confirming transgression has damaged the existing heart.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes — through the heart-posture passages. 2Ch 29:6 — "our fathers have been unfaithful and have done what was evil in the sight of the Lord our God. They have forsaken him and have turned away their faces from the habitation of the Lord and turned their backs" — turning faces and backs is the bodily expression of what the heart has done; the heart has turned away from God; 2Ch 26:16 — "when he was strong, he grew proud, to his destruction. For he was unfaithful to the Lord his God" — pride is a heart-condition (the heart lifted up) that produces faithlessness; Psa 73:15 — "if I had said, 'I will speak thus,' I would have betrayed the generation of your children" — the heart's inner deliberation about speech constitutes the potential treachery.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes — the heart is the primary named origin of perversity within the corpus. Pro 6:14 — "with perverted heart devises evil, continually sowing discord" — the heart is the explicitly named seat of perversity that drives evil-devising; Pro 23:33 — "your heart utter perverse things" — the heart as the source of the perverted verbal output; Deu 32:20 — "a perverse generation, children in whom is no faithfulness" — the perversity characterises the inner disposition the generation's hearts carry.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes — most explicitly in Psa 58:2. "No, in your hearts you devise wrongs; your hands deal out violence on earth" — the heart is the explicitly named origin of the devised wrong; Psa 64:6 — "for the inward mind and heart of a man are deep" — naming the heart as the deep origin of the searched-out injustice; Psa 53:1 — "the fool says in his heart, 'There is no God'" — the heart's atheism as the cognitive foundation of the unjust conduct.

---

### T2.3.2

**Question:** What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Heart-location engages the heart's *willing and moral-evaluating* functions. Job 1:5 shows sinning in the heart as a heart-orientation (cursing God) — the heart's alignment with or against God is the register. Psa 119:11 shows the heart as the site where the word is stored and where the will-to-not-sin is formed — the heart's *holding* and *deciding* function. The heart here is integrating function in the sense that it is where the person's stance before God is formed: the heart that curses God (Job 1:5) is the heart that has turned its deepest orientation against him, while the heart that stores his word (Psa 119:11) is the heart aligned with him. Sinning in the heart is thus sinning at the person's deepest evaluative and volitional centre.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The absence of heart-language (T2.3.1) is a defining structural feature of unintentional sinning. The heart, as the integrating moral centre of the inner person (knowing, willing, feeling), is *not engaged* at the moment of unintentional sinning — which is precisely why the sinning is unintentional. The heart's absence from the act confirms that the characteristic operates below the level of heart-engagement: it is an act that proceeds without the heart's informed moral consent. Lev 4:2 ("sins unintentionally") — the absence of heart-language signals that the heart's moral-evaluation function did not process the act as prohibited. The heart engages *after* realisation (Lev 5:5 — guilt realised and confessed), not during the sinning itself.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Heart-location (2Sa 24:10) reveals that genuine confession is not primarily a social or religious obligation performed externally but an inner event initiated by the heart's own moral witness. The heart here functions in its *moral-awareness and conscience* capacity: it registers that a wrong was done and responds by striking — producing inward conviction before external prompt. This confirms that CHAR-3's deepest constitutional seat is the heart: the heart confesses first (within itself, in the form of conviction), then the mouth confesses second (externally, in the form of speech). The heart-initiation distinguishes genuine confession from its hollow form — where the heart has not struck but the mouth still speaks.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The absence of explicit heart-language in this corpus is analytically significant. In CHAR-3 (Confession), "David's heart struck him" — the heart is where genuine conscience-engagement originates. The absence of heart-language in CHAR-4 may reflect that conscience suppression operates *below* the heart's full moral engagement — the heart's warning function is what is suppressed, which is why it does not appear actively in the corpus. Tit 3:11's "warped" (*exestraptai* — to be distorted/turned inside out) may imply a heart-level distortion that the term "warped" carries, though the heart is not explicitly named.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Heart-location (2Ki 10:31) reveals that refusal to repent is seated in the heart's *incomplete volitional commitment*. "Not with all his heart" — the heart is the integrating centre of the will's commitment to God and his law; where the heart is not wholehearted, a portion of it remains available for the sinful course to continue unchallenged. The refusal to repent is thus not located in a single moment of will-act but in the heart's ongoing failure to commit entirely — the characteristic is as deep as the heart's partial alignment.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Heart-location (Exo 9:34) reveals that habitual defection is seated at the heart's *dispositional-volitional centre* and produces a progressive deformation of that centre. The hardening of the heart is both the mechanism and the symptom: each sinning act hardens the heart, and the hardened heart drives the next sinning act. The heart in habitual defection is not merely passively shaped but actively hardens itself ("hardened his heart" — the Hiphil causative suggests the agent is Pharaoh himself, not an external force). Habitual defection thus represents the heart's own participation in its constitutional deformation.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The absence of explicit heart-language in this corpus is analytically significant. The Jeroboam-formula focuses on the leader's conduct (walking in the way, making Israel to sin) and the community's outcome (sinning, provoking God) rather than on the leader's inner heart-state. This contrasts with CHAR-5 (2Ki 10:31 — "not with all his heart") where the heart is explicitly named as the site of incomplete commitment. CHAR-7's evidence base is behavioural-relational rather than introspective — the corpus describes what the leader does and what the community undergoes rather than the internal heart-condition that drives the leader.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The absence of explicit heart-language reflects the corpus's focus on the outer political acts rather than the inner generating conditions. The one verse that comes closest to inner location is 2Ch 21:10's "forsaken the Lord" — forsaking is a heart-level act — but the heart is not named directly. The corpus is descriptive at the political-social level; the inner heart-conditions that produce revolt (such as the decision to break submission) are not named. This is consistent with the corpus's literary form (regnal narrative) which describes political outcomes rather than inner states.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Heart-location (Mat 15:19; Mar 7:22) reveals that sinful speech is not primarily a failure of speech-regulation but a *diagnostic of the heart's moral condition*. The speech does not corrupt the heart — the corrupted heart produces the speech. This is the characteristic's most theologically significant finding: addressing sinful speech by regulating the mouth (without addressing the heart) is insufficient; the mouth speaks what the heart contains. Eph 4:31's "put away from you" and Col 3:8's "put them all away" are therefore ultimately heart-level renunciation commands, not merely verbal-hygiene commands.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Heart-location (2Pe 2:14 — "hearts trained in greed") reveals that the enticement mechanism reaches the constitutional centre of the person: the heart is not merely performing sinful appetite but has been *trained* into it — the training implies sustained formation of the heart's motivational centre toward sin. The heart's training is what makes the enticement self-generating: the heart has become the bait-mechanism itself, not merely a passive recipient of external lures.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Heart-location (Heb 3:13 — hardening through deceit; Rom 6:17 — heart-enslavement preceding heart-obedience) reveals that the universal sin-condition is not merely behavioural or cognitive but penetrates to the person's moral-volitional centre. The heart's hardening (Heb 3:13) means sin's deceitfulness progressively closes the heart's capacity to respond to God's voice — the more thoroughly the condition operates on the heart, the less the person can hear and respond to correction. This is why the remedy addresses the heart: the forgiveness-declaration (VCG-02) reaches the heart level, and the Spirit's conviction (Joh 16:8/9) addresses the heart's resistance to acknowledging the condition.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — The absence of explicit heart-language reflects the corpus's focus on the will's captivity (Joh 8:34), the universal structural imprisonment (Gal 3:22), and the allegiance-level identity (1Jo 3:8). The heart's implicit engagement is through the will's captivity, but the vocabulary does not name it directly in this corpus.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Heart-location (Jer 17:1 — iron pen, diamond point engraving on the heart's tablet) reveals that the divine record has a dual location: before God externally and within the person internally. The engraving metaphor is the most analytically significant image in the 205-verse corpus for constitutional location: the sin is inscribed in the person's innermost moral core with such permanence ("iron pen... diamond point") that it cannot be self-erased. The heart bears the record as an internal impression while God maintains it as an external account. The record's internal inscription explains why it persists even when hidden from others: the engraving is within.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Heart-location (Lev 10:19 — inner state affecting offering's validity; Lev 23:27 — affliction as inner-posture) reveals that the seeking dimension of the characteristic is not merely formal (bringing the prescribed offering) but requires an appropriate inner orientation at the heart level. The priestly officiants' inner state matters (Lev 10:19); the individual seeker's self-affliction matters (Lev 23:27); and in the NT register, Luk 7:47 — the woman's love is the heart's response to forgiveness received, confirming that the heart is the primary relational-receptive faculty engaged throughout.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Heart-location (1Ki 8:47 — "turn their heart") reveals that generational sin has penetrated to the person's moral-volitional centre: the heart must turn, which implies it was previously oriented in a wrong direction sustained by the generational pattern. The heart's turning is the required reversal of what the generational sin-condition has made the heart's default orientation. The heart is thus both the site of the condition's hold and the site of the potential turning that addresses it.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Heart-location (Jam 4:8 — heart requiring purification alongside the sinner's hand-cleansing; Pro 23:17 — heart tempted toward sinners' prosperity) reveals that the sinner-identity operates through and on the heart in complementary ways: the sinner's own heart requires purification (Jam 4:8 — the heart is the inner dimension of the sinner's condition); and the observing person's heart is at risk of envy toward sinners (Pro 23:17 — the sinner-identity's apparent prosperity can misdirect the onlooker's heart). The heart is thus both the site of the sinner's internal condition and a faculty vulnerable to the sinner's external situation.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Heart-location (Hos 10:2 — "false heart... must bear guilt") reveals that the guilt-state is rooted in the heart's dispositional condition: it is not merely the result of isolated acts but flows from the heart's sustained false-orientation. The heart generates the acts that create guilt entries, and the guilt-bearing is thus the heart's consequence. This connects CHAR-17 to CHAR-16 (sinner as moral character): the false heart that generates guilt is the heart of the sinner-type.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Heart-location (Eze 14:3/4/7 — idols taken into the heart; Job 31:33 — iniquity hidden in the heart) reveals two distinct heart-iniquity functions. (1) *The heart as iniquity's origin*: Eze 14:3 — the will chooses to receive idols inward; the heart is the site of the originating criminal allegiance that produces all subsequent iniquity; (2) *The heart as iniquity's hiding-place*: Job 31:33 — the heart can conceal acknowledged iniquity to avoid accountability; the hiding is a deliberate inner act. VCG-08's heart-seated register is thus the most foundational: it locates iniquity at the person's innermost will-level, making it the source-register from which other VCGs flow.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Heart-location (Psa 36:1 — "deep in his heart"; Isa 59:13 — "conceiving from the heart"; Eze 18:31 — new heart as remedy) reveals that CHAR-19's transgression is not primarily an external act but an inner-heart condition that drives external behaviour. Psa 36:1's "transgression speaks deep in the heart" is the single most important inner-being statement in the entire 147-verse corpus: it personifies transgression as an internal counsellor installed at the heart's deepest level, displacing the fear of God and steering the will toward rebellion. The heart is both the origin of transgression (where it speaks from) and the site requiring renewal when transgression is addressed (Eze 18:31).

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Heart-location (2Ch 29:6 — turning away from God; 2Ch 26:16 — proud heart producing faithlessness; Psa 73:15 — heart's inner deliberation as potential betrayal) reveals that faithlessness operates at the heart's allegiance-level: the heart that has turned its face and back toward God (2Ch 29:6) is the heart in the faithlessness-condition. The heart's disposition of allegiance — toward God or away — is the constitutional location of faithlessness. When the heart turns away from God (2Ch 29:6 — "turned their backs"), the turn is faithlessness at its heart-origin.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Heart-location (Pro 6:14 — "perverted heart"; Pro 23:33 — heart uttering perverse things; Deu 32:20 — perverse generation) reveals that perversion-as-inner-inversion originates at the heart's deep centre. Pro 6:14's "perverted heart devises evil continually" is the corpus's defining inner-being statement: the heart is both the origin and the continual driver of perversity; the perversion is not episodic but continuous because it is seated in the heart's dispositional centre. The heart is the characteristic's primary constitutional location.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Heart-location (Psa 58:2 — "in your hearts you devise wrongs"; Psa 64:6 — "inward mind and heart... deep"; Psa 53:1 — heart-atheism) reveals that CHAR-22 originates in the heart's deliberating function: the heart does not passively receive injustice but actively *devises* it. The heart is the scheming centre — the same faculty that, when rightly oriented, devises justice, is here engaged in the deliberate planning of wrongs. Psa 64:6's "diligent search" confirms the deliberateness.

---

### T2.3.3

**Question:** If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Heart-location is evidenced (T2.3.1 and T2.3.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — The evidence is silent on heart-location in the unintentional sinning act. Noted explicitly and analytically significant (T2.3.2).

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Heart-location is clearly evidenced (2Sa 24:10). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(S)*

**[CHAR-4]** S — The evidence is silent on explicit heart-location. The absence is noted and analytically significant (T2.3.2).

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Heart-location is evidenced (2Ki 10:31). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Heart-location is evidenced (Exo 9:34). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-7]** S — The evidence is silent on explicit heart-location. The heart is implicitly engaged through the will but not named directly. Noted.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — The evidence is silent on explicit heart-location. The heart's implicit engagement is through the will, but the vocabulary does not name it directly. Noted.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Heart-location is explicitly evidenced (Mat 15:19; Mar 7:22). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Heart-location is explicitly evidenced for enticement (2Pe 2:14). Hypocrisy and apostasy do not name the heart explicitly in the 5-verse corpus. Noted.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Heart-location is evidenced (Heb 3:13; Rom 6:17; Gen 4:7). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — The evidence is silent on explicit heart-location for CHAR-12. Noted.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Heart-location is most explicitly evidenced of any constitutional level (Jer 17:1). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Heart-location is evidenced implicitly (Lev 10:19; Lev 23:27; Luk 7:47). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Heart-location is evidenced (1Ki 8:47). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Heart-location is evidenced (Jam 4:8; Pro 23:17; Mar 8:38). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Heart-location is evidenced (Hos 10:2; Gen 42:21). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Heart-location is centrally evidenced in VCG-08 (Eze 14:3/4/7; Job 31:33). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Heart-location is the most explicitly evidenced constitutional location in the corpus (Psa 36:1; Isa 59:13; Eze 18:31). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Heart-location is evidenced (2Ch 29:6; 2Ch 26:16; Psa 73:15). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Heart-location is explicitly evidenced (Pro 6:14; Pro 23:33; Deu 32:20). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Heart-location is explicitly evidenced (Psa 53:1; 58:2; 64:6). This prompt is superseded.

---

## T2.4 — Mind

### T2.4.1

**Question:** Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The corpus contains evidence of mind-engagement, though not by explicit mind-terminology. Psa 4:4 ("ponder in your own hearts on your beds, and be silent") — the word "ponder" engages the reflective mind as the instrument for preventing sinning; the cognitive faculty of reflection is what the psalmist directs against the impulse to sin in anger. Ecc 5:6 ("let not your mouth lead you into sin") implies that the mind's lack of reflective oversight (the mouth leading ahead of considered thought) is what enables speech-mode sinning. The implication is that sinning bypasses or overrides reflective mind-engagement — it is an act where the will moves without adequate cognitive processing of the moral stakes.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The mind-engagement is evidenced primarily in the *realisation* phase rather than the sinning phase. Lev 5:5 ("when he realizes his guilt") — the realisation event is a cognitive act: information is processed and the moral status of the past act is understood. Num 22:34 ("I did not know that you stood in the road against me") — the absence of prior knowledge is a mind-statement: the mind did not have the morally relevant information. The mind is thus engaged at the moment of realisation (bringing knowledge that was previously absent) but specifically absent during the sinning act (which occurred without the mind's knowledge of the prohibition or relevant fact).

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Mind-engagement is evidenced through the cognitive component of confession: the naming of sin requires knowing what was done and knowing it was wrong. 2Sa 19:20 — "your servant *knows* that I have sinned" — the cognitive faculty ("knows") is explicitly named as the basis of the confession. Dan 9:5/8/11/15 — the extended multi-dimensional confession shows a highly articulated cognitive engagement: each named dimension of failure ("sinned and done wrong and acted wickedly and rebelled, turning aside from your commandments") requires the mind to differentiate and name specific aspects of what went wrong.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Yes. The cognitive dimension is the most clearly evidenced constitutional location. Jer 16:10 — the people's failure to recognise their sin is a *cognitive-perceptual failure*: the mind does not know ("what sin have we committed?"). 1Cor 15:34 — "some have no knowledge of God" — *knowledge* (gnōsis) is explicitly the cognitive category at stake; the absence of God-knowledge is a mind-level deficit. The mind in these verses is the site of the perceptual/epistemic failure that constitutes conscience suppression in its blindness mode.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The mind is engaged through the *knowledge* dimension in Heb 10:26: "sinning deliberately after receiving the knowledge of the truth" — the person who deliberately sins after knowing the truth has the relevant knowledge in their mind and acts against it. 1Ki 16:31 — "as if it had been a light thing for him to walk in the sins of Jeroboam" — the mental assessment/evaluation ("a light thing") is a cognitive act. The mind is engaged in the characteristic through its evaluative and knowledge-holding functions.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The mind is engaged in habitual defection through the epistemic deficit it produces. 1Jo 3:6 — "no one who keeps on sinning has either *seen* him or *known* him" — the cognitive-perceptive faculties of seeing and knowing are the site of the deficit: the habitual sinner does not see or know Christ. This is a mind-level consequence of habitual defection: the settled sinning pattern has produced or revealed an epistemic blindness. 1Sa 2:25 — "they would not listen" — the non-listening is also a mind-level phenomenon: the auditory-cognitive capacity to receive and process the corrective word is being refused.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The mind is engaged through the teaching mechanism. Deu 20:18 — "that they may not *teach* you to do according to all their abominable practices" — the teaching mode names a cognitive-instructional transmission: the Canaanite nations transmit sinning practices through instruction, which is a mind-targeted mechanism. The community's mind receives the instruction in abominable practices, which reshapes their moral knowledge and behavioural orientation. The cognitive dimension of the teaching-mode is the mind-level location of contagious sin.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — The 9-verse corpus does not locate political revolt in the mind. No cognitive terminology appears — the corpus describes actions (revolted, rebelled, set up a king) without naming the cognitive processes of the revolting parties.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The mind is engaged through the cognitive dimension of sinful speech. Mat 15:19 — "out of the heart come evil *thoughts*" — the evil thoughts are a cognitive faculty output alongside slander; cognition and speech are co-products of the corrupted heart. 1Ti 6:4 — "understands nothing" — the person given to slander has a corrupted cognitive faculty ("understands nothing") that enables and produces the slanderous speech. The mind's cognitive failure (not understanding) is part of the enabling condition for sinful speech.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — The 5-verse corpus does not explicitly name the mind in connection with any of the three mechanisms. The mechanisms engage the desire-faculty, social-identity, and covenantal-standing without explicit mind-location vocabulary.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes. Rom 7:23 — "the law of sin that dwells in my members" wages war "against the law of my mind" — the mind is the faculty that recognises and aligns with God's law, while sin's competing law operates in the members against it. Rom 7:25 — "I myself serve the law of God with my mind, but with my flesh I serve the law of sin" — the mind is explicitly named as the faculty that knows and wills God's law; the condition's hold is in the flesh rather than the mind, creating the divided-person experience. Rom 3:20 — "through the law comes knowledge of sin" — the mind is the cognitive faculty through which the law produces the knowledge of the condition.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — The 9-verse corpus does not explicitly name the mind in connection with sin's enslaving power. The characteristic operates through will-captivity (Joh 8:34), structural imprisonment (Gal 3:22), and constitutional identity (1Jo 3:8/9) without explicit mind-location vocabulary.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The mind engages the record primarily through knowledge and memory. Gen 41:9 — "I remember my offenses today" — the cupbearer's mind recalls a past failure at a moment of moral relevance; Jer 13:23 (VCG-03) — "how many are my iniquities and my sins?" — Job's mind attempts but cannot self-enumerate the record; it requires divine disclosure. Pro 24:9 — "the devising of folly is sin" — the mind's cognitive act of scheming folly is itself a sin that enters the record.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — The mind is engaged through the recognition dimension. Lev 4:14 — "when the sin which they have committed becomes known" — the cognitive recognition that sin has been committed is the prerequisite for seeking; the mind's recognition is the gateway. Act 2:38 — "repent" (metanoeō — *meta* + *noeō* — a change of mind) — the NT seeking-term explicitly names the mind as the faculty undergoing change; metanoia is constitutively a cognitive reorientation.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The mind is implicitly engaged through the unbelief dimension. Psa 78:32 — "despite his wonders, they did not believe" — the failure to believe (the cognitive-trust faculty) is the mind-level operation through which the generational sinning is perpetuated; the mind's refusal to integrate God's demonstrated power into trust is the cognitive dimension of the persistent pattern.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — The mind is engaged through the presumption dimension. Amo 9:10 — "who say, 'Disaster shall not overtake or meet us'" — the cognitive self-assessment ("we are safe") is the mental form of the sinner-identity's self-deception; the mind's false conclusion about the sinner's security perpetuates the identity. Joh 9:25 — "whether he is a sinner I do not know" — the healed man's cognitive refusal to render the verdict the Pharisees demand reflects the mind's proper epistemic humility about the sinner-identity label.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — The mind is engaged through the knowledge-dimension of guilt-recognition. Lev 5:2/3/4 — "when he comes to know it" — the cognitive event of coming-to-knowledge is the trigger for guilt-recognition; the mind's acquiring of information about the violation is what activates the guilt-state. Gen 42:21 — the brothers' retrospective cognitive connection of their past cruelty to their present suffering is a mind-level interpretive act that activates conscience-recognition of guilt.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — The mind engages through the self-assessment and concealment dimensions. Psa 36:2 — "he flatters himself in his own eyes that his iniquity cannot be found out and hated" — the mind's self-assessment is systematically distorted by pride; the cognitive self-evaluation cannot accurately perceive the iniquity it carries. Hos 12:8 — "in all my labors they cannot find in me iniquity or sin" — the mind's verdict on the self is false; the cognitive faculty wrongly assesses the iniquity-condition. Job 13:23 — "how many are my iniquities and my sins? Make me know my transgression and my sin" — Job asks for mind-level knowledge of his iniquity-count; the mind needs divine revelation to accurately know it.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — The mind is engaged through the knowledge-prerequisite and the cognitive assessment dimensions. Rom 4:15 — "where there is no law there is no transgression" — the mind must possess knowledge of the boundary before transgression is possible; the cognitive awareness is the enabling condition. Isa 46:8 — "remember this and stand firm, recall it to mind, you transgressors" — the transgressors' minds need to recall and fix the remembered truth; their transgression is connected to a cognitive failure of recall. Job 13:23 — "how many are my iniquities and my sins? Make me know my transgression and my sin" — the mind's need for divine illumination to know transgression-count.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — The mind is engaged through the deliberative and knowing dimensions. Psa 73:15 — "if I had said, 'I will speak thus,' I would have betrayed the generation of your children" — the mental deliberation about speech constitutes potential treachery; the mind's deliberative choice is the locus at which faithlessness can be avoided or committed through speech. Psa 59:5 — "those who treacherously plot evil" — the mind's planning activity is named as treachery's cognitive mode.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes — most explicitly in the NT. 1Ti 6:5 — "depraved in mind (*noenous diephtharmenōn*) and deprived of the truth" — the mind (*nous*) is the specifically named corrupted faculty; the depravity has penetrated the seat of understanding. 2Cor 11:3 — "your thoughts will be led astray from a sincere and pure devotion to Christ" — the thoughts (*noēmata*) are the target of corruption. Isa 29:16 — "you turn things upside down! Shall the potter be regarded as the clay?" — the cognitive faculty inverts the proper creator-creature relationship.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes — through the devising and knowing dimensions. Psa 64:6 — "they search out injustice... for the inward mind (*lēb*) and heart of a man are deep" — the mind is paired with the heart as the deep origin of injustice-devising; Job 18:21 — "him who knows not God" — the knowledge-deficit is a cognitive-mind dimension; Isa 61:8 — "I love justice; I hate robbery and wrong" — God's mind's judgments about wrong define what injustice is.

---

### T2.4.2

**Question:** What does mind-location reveal — what aspect of the mind's function (thought, discernment, understanding) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The evidence implicates the mind's *discernment and deliberative* function: sinning occurs when the will acts without adequate moral deliberation. Psa 4:4 — pondering (reflective deliberation) is the remedy; the absence of pondering allows anger to become sinful action. Ecc 5:6 — the mouth outrunning the mind produces sinful speech. Joseph in Gen 39:9 shows the opposite: the mind actively deliberates ("how then can I do this?") and the named moral content (great wickedness, sin against God) provides the deliberative check. The mind's deliberative function — its capacity to name an act as wrong before committing it — is what wilful sinning must overcome or bypass.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The mind's pattern of engagement — present in realisation, absent during the sinning — reveals that unintentional sinning is constitutively a *knowledge-gap event*. The act and the mind's available information are out of alignment at the moment of sinning. When the mind's knowledge catches up to the act's moral reality (Lev 5:5 — realises; Num 22:34 — did not know, now knows), the sinning becomes retrospectively identified and the conscience engages. The characteristic thus operates in the space between what the mind knows and what the act requires — a space that the prescribed education in God's commandments (Lev 4:2 — "the Lord's commandments about things not to be done") is designed to narrow over time.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Mind-location (2Sa 19:20; Dan 9:5) reveals that confession is partly a *cognitive differentiation event*: the mind must identify the sin, name its character (foolishness — Num 12:11; betrayal of innocent blood — Mat 27:4; rebellion against commandments — Dan 9:11), and articulate its dimensions. The more complete the cognitive articulation, the more complete the confession. Dan 9:5's cascade ("sinned... done wrong... acted wickedly... rebelled... turning aside") shows the mind's differentiating function at full operation within confession — not merely "I did something wrong" but a precise taxonomy of what the wrong involved. The mind provides the vocabulary and the structure through which conscience's recognition is named.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Mind-location reveals that conscience suppression has a *cognitive dimension*: the failure to register sin is not only a conscience-faculty failure but a knowledge failure. 1Cor 15:34 — "no knowledge of God" — the mind's knowledge of God is the prerequisite for the moral discernment that conscience suppression lacks. Without knowing God, the standard against which sin is measured is absent from the mind, making conscience-activation impossible. Jer 16:10 — the mind that asks "what sin?" genuinely does not know — its cognitive-moral categories have been so deformed that the question is sincere. The mind-location shows that conscience suppression affects the cognitive faculty's ability to process moral reality accurately.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Mind-location (Heb 10:26; 1Ki 16:31) reveals that refusal to repent can operate through a corrupt cognitive assessment (minimising the sin's gravity — 1Ki 16:31) and through deliberate choice against available knowledge (Heb 10:26 — knowing the truth and sinning deliberately). The mind's evaluative function either produces false verdicts that enable the refusal (minimisation) or is bypassed/overridden by the will in its deliberate sinning mode. In Heb 10:26, the knowledge is present and correct; the will acts against it. The mind-location reveals that refusal to repent is not always a problem of ignorance (cf CHAR-4 — Conscience suppression) but can involve the will acting against what the mind knows.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Mind-location (1Jo 3:6; 1Sa 2:25) reveals that habitual defection produces *epistemic consequences*: the sustained sinning pattern either reveals or produces the inability to know and see God. 1Jo 3:6's "never seen him or known him" is not a momentary perceptual failure but a fundamental epistemic blindness correlating with the habitual sinning — the mind's capacity for theological-relational knowledge is impaired by or indicative of the habitual sinning condition. Similarly, 1Sa 2:25's non-listening shows the mind's receptive capacity being closed against corrective input.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Mind-location (Deu 20:18 — teaching mode) reveals that contagious sin can operate through the cognitive-instructional channel: the sinning practices are transmitted as *knowledge* to the recipient community, whose mind receives and internalises the content. The teaching mode is particularly insidious because it operates through the mind's designed learning capacity — the God-given ability to learn from others is turned toward learning sinning practices. This differs from the authority-structural mode (Kings corpus) in that it is explicitly cognitive-pedagogical: the Canaanite nations are not just modelling but actively teaching.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — The absence of mind-location reflects the corpus's action-reporting literary form. The political decision-making process (what the revolting parties thought and calculated) is not addressed; only the action and its consequences are named.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Mind-location (1Ti 6:4 — "understands nothing"; Mat 15:19 — "evil thoughts") reveals that sinful speech is accompanied by and enabled by cognitive failure: the slanderer does not properly understand the moral reality of what they are doing or the nature of the God they are speaking against. 1Ti 1:13 — Paul's blasphemy was from "ignorant unbelief" — cognitive-epistemic ignorance as the enabling condition. The mind's role is not the origin of sinful speech (the heart is) but the cognitive framework within which sinful speech is enabled or constrained.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(S)*

**[CHAR-10]** S — The absence of mind-location vocabulary is consistent with the mechanisms' character: enticement operates through the sub-rational desire-faculty (below the level of explicit cognitive deliberation); hypocrisy operates through social-identity performance (not primarily cognitive); apostasy operates through the will's departure (not primarily cognitive). The mechanisms characteristically bypass or operate below the level of explicit rational deliberation.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Mind-location (Rom 7:23/25 — mind versus law of sin; Rom 3:20 — knowledge of sin through the law) reveals a critical distinction within the condition's operation: the mind can know God's law and even will to comply with it (Rom 7:25 — "I myself serve the law of God with my mind") while the condition operates in the members against what the mind knows. This produces the characteristic divided-person experience of Romans 7: the condition is not ignorance (the mind knows) but constitutional incapacity (the members do not comply). The condition thus operates *around* the mind rather than exclusively *through* it — which is why knowledge alone (intellectual) cannot resolve the condition.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — The absence of mind-location reflects that sin's enslaving power in this corpus operates at the constitutional-volitional and allegiance levels rather than primarily through cognitive processes. The mind may know the enslaved condition (intellectually aware) but the enslaving power is not primarily a cognitive phenomenon in this corpus.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Mind-location (Gen 41:9 — remembering offenses; Job 13:23 — seeking to know the record; Pro 24:9 — devising folly as sin) reveals that the divine record engages the mind at two points: (1) the mind's acts can create entries in the record (Pro 24:9 — cognitive devising of folly is sin); (2) the mind can partially access the record through memory (Gen 41:9) but cannot fully enumerate it without divine disclosure (Job 13:23 — needing God to "make me know my transgression and my sin").

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Mind-location (Lev 4:14 — recognition as prerequisite; Act 2:38 — repentance as metanoia) reveals that the seeking dimension requires a cognitive component: the mind must recognise the sin and reorient toward God. Metanoia (repentance) is precisely the mind's change of direction — the mind that was directed toward sin now turns toward God. The mind does not merely register the seeking intellectually; it undergoes the directional reorientation that is the seeking's volitional dimension.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Mind-location (Psa 78:32 — unbelief despite wonders) reveals that the generational sinning pattern operates partly through the mind's persistent refusal to draw the correct cognitive conclusion from God's actions. The mind that has witnessed divine wonders and still does not believe is exhibiting a constitutively resistant cognitive orientation — a mind-level component of the generational pattern that makes it self-perpetuating: even extraordinary evidence does not break the inherited unbelief-pattern in the mind.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Mind-location (Amo 9:10 — cognitive self-deception about consequences; Joh 9:25 — cognitive uncertainty about sinner-label) reveals that the sinner-identity engages the mind in its self-assessment function: the habitual sinner's mind generates false security (Amo 9:10), while the observer's mind must exercise careful judgment about applying the sinner-label (Joh 9:25 — "I do not know"). The mind is the faculty through which the sinner either correctly or incorrectly assesses their own moral status.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Mind-location (Lev 5:2/3/4 — "comes to know"; Gen 42:21 — cognitive retrospection) reveals that the guilt-state requires a cognitive trigger: the person must come to know the violation before guilt-recognition occurs. Guilt is not merely the feeling of having done wrong but requires the mind's engagement with the knowledge of what was done. This is why Lev 5:17/19 is significant: "though he did not know it, then realizes his guilt" — even guilt from unknown violations becomes subjectively active once the mind acquires knowledge.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Mind-location (Psa 36:2 — self-flattery; Hos 12:8 — false self-assessment; Job 13:23 — need for divine disclosure) reveals that the mind's self-assessment of iniquity is constitutively unreliable without divine input. The mind flatters itself (Psa 36:2), generates false confidence (Hos 12:8), and requires God to reveal what it cannot see on its own (Job 13:23 — "make me know"). This unreliability is a symptom of the iniquity's effect on the mind itself: the accumulated crime distorts the very cognitive faculty that would assess it.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Mind-location (Rom 4:15 — knowledge-prerequisite; Isa 46:8 — recall failure; Job 13:23 — needs divine disclosure) reveals that transgression engages and distorts the cognitive faculty at two levels: (1) it requires the mind's prior knowledge of the law to be technically possible (Rom 4:15); (2) it progressively suppresses the mind's capacity to accurately assess its own transgression-state (Isa 46:8 — transgressors need to "recall it to mind"). The mind is both the prerequisite for transgression and a casualty of its sustained operation.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Mind-location (Psa 73:15 — deliberating whether to speak; Psa 59:5 — plotting evil) reveals that faithlessness engages the cognitive-deliberative faculty in two ways: (1) the mind can deliberate whether to speak (Psa 73:15) and thereby either commit or avoid betrayal through speech; (2) the mind can plan treachery (Psa 59:5 — those who treacherously plot evil). The mind is both the faculty that can restrain faithlessness through honest deliberation and the faculty that can plot and execute it.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Mind-location (1Ti 6:5 — mind depraved; 2Cor 11:3 — thoughts led astray; Isa 29:16 — cognitive inversion) reveals that CHAR-21's perversion operates at the level of the mind's basic cognitive function: the capacity to know God as creator (Isa 29:16), to hold truth (1Ti 6:5 — "deprived of the truth"), and to maintain sincere devotion (2Cor 11:3). When the mind is corrupted, the person cannot accurately perceive the most fundamental realities (creator-creature relationship, truth). This makes CHAR-21's mind-corruption the most epistemically devastating dimension.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Mind-location (Psa 64:6 — inward mind devising; Job 18:21 — not knowing God) reveals that injustice operates at the cognitive level through two mechanisms: (1) *active deliberation toward wrong* (Psa 64:6 — "diligent search" for injustice — the mind's analytical capacity deployed toward planning wrong); (2) *God-knowledge deficit* (Job 18:21 — "knows not God") — the mind's failure to know God produces the characteristic's enabling condition.

---

**Question:** If the evidence is silent on mind-location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Mind-location is evidenced (see T2.4.1 and T2.4.2). The engagement is implicit rather than terminologically explicit, but it is analytically clear.
