## T2.5 — Other Soul Subsets

### T2.5.1

**Question:** Does the verse evidence surface any soul-level location beyond heart and mind for this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Yes. The *conscience* is evidenced as a distinct soul-subset engaged by wilful sinning. The VCG-03 corpus (deterrence/restraint) presupposes conscience as the faculty that recognises the moral quality of a potential act before commission: Gen 39:9 (Joseph's conscience names "great wickedness"), Psa 39:1 (the conscience-driven resolve to guard the mouth). Post-act, conscience appears in Gen 42:22 (Reuben's conscience connects past sinning to present reckoning). The conscience operates as the inner moral witness that either deters sinning (pre-act) or registers it as wrong (post-act). This is distinct from the heart's volitional function and the mind's deliberative function.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The *conscience* is the primary soul-subset evidenced beyond heart and mind. Lev 5:5 ("when he realizes his guilt... and confesses") — the realization of guilt is a conscience-event: the moral witness within the person registers that a wrong was done, even though no deliberate defiance occurred. The conscience here operates *retrospectively*: it engages after the fact, processing the moral reality of a past act once the relevant information is available. Num 22:34 (Balaam's immediate confession) shows the same retrospective conscience pattern: knowledge arrives → conscience fires → verbal acknowledgment follows.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — *Will/volition* emerges as a distinct soul-subset beyond heart and mind in the CHAR-3 corpus. The contrast between genuine and hollow confession is precisely a will-contrast: in Deu 1:41 (VCG-03), the will proceeds autonomously despite the spoken words — the will is not aligned with the confession. In 1Ch 21:17, the will is fully engaged: "It is I who have sinned" — the will claims ownership without deflection. The will's alignment or misalignment with the confessional content is what distinguishes genuine from hollow confession — which makes the will a distinct inner location that confession either fully engages or only partially reaches.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The *will* is evidenced as a distinct soul-subset engaged in conscience suppression's active-denial mode. Jer 2:35 — "you say, 'I am innocent'" — the saying involves the will's active commitment to the false claim. The will is not merely passive in the face of suppressed conscience; it is the faculty that chooses to voice and maintain the denial. This distinguishes the active-denial mode (will engaged in suppression) from the perceptual-blindness mode (will not specifically engaged — Jer 16:10) and the habituated mode (will habituated to sinning — Ecc 8:12).

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The *will* as a distinct volitional faculty beyond the heart's integrating function is the primary soul-subset evidenced. The corpus's persistent "did not depart... did not turn... would not obey" formulations all name the will directly. Heb 10:26's *hekousiōs* (deliberately/willingly) is the most explicit naming of the will as the operative faculty. The will is what clings (2Ki 3:3 — *davaq*), refuses to depart, and stubbornly persists against correction (Neh 9:29 — "would not obey").

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — *Will/disposition* as a distinct volitional-dispositional faculty is the primary soul-subset beyond heart and mind. The continuous-present forms — "keeps on sinning" (1Jo 3:6), "they would not listen" (1Sa 2:25), "there they have continued" (Hos 10:9) — all name the will's settled directional commitment rather than discrete choices. The will has been formed into a disposition that produces sinning as its default: this is will-as-disposition, distinct from will-as-moment-of-choice (CHAR-1/CHAR-5).

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — *Will/volition* is the primary soul-level faculty evidenced. The corpus's dominant form — "walked in the way of Jeroboam and... made Israel to sin" — is constitutively volitional in the leader (walked = volitional commitment; made Israel to sin = volitional causative action). The community's will is redirected: 2Ki 17:21 — "drove Israel from following the Lord" — the driving-away is an act against the community's volitional orientation. The will operates at both ends of the transmission: the leader's will causes, the community's will is redirected.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — *Will/volition* is the primary evidenced soul-level location. Pa.sha — the deliberate act of breaking submission — is constitutively volitional: 2Ki 8:20 — "revolted from the rule of Judah and set up a king of their own" — the combined act of breaking from and establishing requires volitional decision and action. 2Ch 21:10 — "because he had forsaken the Lord" — *forsook* (*azav* H5800) is a volitional act of abandonment.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — *Will/volition* as a distinct soul-level faculty is clearly engaged. Jude 9 — Michael "did not *presume* to pronounce a blasphemous judgment" — the presume (*epitolmaō* — to dare) names the will's act of over-reaching. Rev 13:5 — the beast's blasphemous utterances are a willed, permitted, sustained act ("it was allowed to exercise authority for forty-two months") — the will exercises sustained blasphemous speech over time. 1Ti 6:4 — the "craving for controversy" is a volitional appetite. The will is engaged as the faculty that either restrains or enacts sinful speech.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — *Desire/appetite (epithumia)* as a distinct soul-level faculty is the primary location beyond heart and mind. Jam 1:14 — "his own desire" — the desire-faculty (epithumia) is the mechanism's operative site for enticement. 2Pe 2:14 — "insatiable for sin" — the appetite-faculty is named through its insatiability. 2Pe 2:18 — "sensual passions of the flesh" — the sensual-desire register of the epithumia faculty. This is the desire-faculty operating as a constitutional location distinct from (though related to) the heart.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — *Will/volition* as a distinct soul-level faculty is evidenced. Rom 7:15 (implied in the corpus's broader argument — the specific verse is outside the 112 but the pattern is evidenced within it): the condition operates at the will level through the split between intending good and doing evil — Rom 7:17/20 — "it is no longer I who do it, but sin that dwells within me" — the "I" (volitional self) is distinguished from the sin-force that operates within; (2) Rom 6:16 — "you are slaves of the one whom you obey" — the obedience is a volitional act; the condition operates by capturing the volitional obedience and directing it toward sin rather than God; (3) Gen 4:7 — "you must rule over it" — the will is addressed as the faculty that must exercise ruling authority against the sin-force.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — *Will/volition in its captive mode* is the primary evidenced soul-level location beyond heart and mind. Joh 8:34 — "a slave to sin" — the slavery is specifically the will's captivity (the definition explicitly names "governing the will so it cannot freely choose otherwise"). The will as the enslaved faculty is the distinctive soul-level location of CHAR-12. Additionally, *identity/allegiance* as a constitutional soul-level dimension: 1Jo 3:8 — "of the devil" — the person's deepest identity-belonging is the soul-level location of the allegiance captured by the enslaving power.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — *Conscience* as a distinct soul-level faculty is evidenced. Psa 51:3 — "my sin is ever before me" — the conscience's persistent awareness of the record is the primary soul-level location beyond heart and mind. Num 5:6 — "that person realizes his guilt" — the conscience's realisation of guilt is the moment the divine record becomes accessible to inner awareness. The conscience is the faculty that mediates between the objective divine record and the subjective inner-being experience of it.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — *Faith/trust* as a distinct soul-level faculty is evidenced. Act 10:43 — "everyone who believes in him receives forgiveness of sins through his name" — the believing (*pisteúōn* — present participle) is the soul-level receptive act through which forgiveness is received; faith is the faculty of trust-directed-toward-Christ through which the receiving dimension is completed. Faith is not merely cognitive (mind) or affective (heart) but a distinct trust-orientation of the whole person toward the forgiver.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — *Will* as a distinct soul-level faculty is evidenced through the rebellion dimension. Psa 78:17 — "yet they sinned still more against him, rebelling against the Most High in the desert" — rebellion (*mārāh* — to be contentious, to rebel) is a volitional act: the will actively sets itself against God rather than passively drifting. The "still more" indicates an escalating volitional commitment to the sinning pattern. The will's active rebellion is the soul-level faculty through which the generational pattern is individually sustained.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — *Conscience* as a distinct soul-level faculty is evidenced. Luk 5:8 — "I am a sinful man, O Lord" — Peter's spontaneous recognition of his sinner-identity is a conscience-operation: the moral self-assessment arises unbidden in the presence of holiness. Luk 18:13 — "would not even lift up his eyes to heaven, but beat his breast" — the tax collector's bodily self-abasement is the physical expression of conscience's internal verdict about the sinner-identity. Rom 3:7 — "why am I still being condemned as a sinner?" — the rhetorical question engages the conscience's assessment of moral status even when one's act produced divine glory.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — *Conscience* as the primary soul-level faculty of CHAR-17 is the defining element of the characteristic. 1Sa 25:31 (pu.qah) — "pangs of conscience" — the term directly names the conscience-faculty's experience of guilt-stagger; Lev 4:13/22/27; 5:2/3/4/5 — "realizes his guilt" (a.sham) — the repeated guilt-realisation pattern names the conscience as the recognition-faculty; Hos 5:15 — "until they acknowledge their guilt" — the acknowledgment is the conscience's output. The conscience is the primary inner-being faculty constituting the characteristic (per the definition: "conscience in its guilt-awareness mode").

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — *Conscience* as a distinct soul-level faculty is evidenced. 2Sa 24:10 — "David's heart struck him after he had numbered the people" — the heart-strike is a conscience event: the moral self-assessment faculty activates spontaneously in response to the iniquity; Psa 38:18 — "I confess my iniquity; I am sorry for my sin" — the conscience produces both confession and sorrow as its output; Lev 26:40/41 — "confess their iniquity... if then their uncircumcised heart is humbled" — the confession presupposes conscience engaging through heart-humiliation.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — *Will* as the primary soul-level faculty is the defining location of CHAR-19. The entire characteristic is built on the wilful act of crossing a known boundary — the will is the primary inner faculty. Isa 31:6 — "turn to him from whom people have deeply revolted" — the turning (the will's reversal) is the prescribed remedy, confirming the will is the primary locus. Eze 18:28 — "he considered and turned away from all the transgressions" — the turning of the will is the act that reverses the transgression's consequence. *Conscience* also appears: Pro 28:13 — "whoever conceals his transgressions will not prosper" — the concealment is a conscience-suppression act.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — *Will* as the primary soul-level faculty is central to CHAR-20. 1Ch 5:25 — "broke faith with the God of their fathers, and whored after the gods of the peoples" — the will's active transfer of allegiance is the volitional core; Eze 18:24 — "when a righteous person turns away from his righteousness" — the turning is a volitional act; Lev 26:40 — "treachery that they committed against me, and also in walking contrary to me" — the will walking contrary. *Conscience* appears in Ezr 9:4 — "all who trembled at the words of the God of Israel... sat appalled" — the conscience-engaged response to observed faithlessness; Ezr 10:6 — mourning over the exiles' faithlessness.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — *Desire* as a distinct soul-level faculty is explicitly the corruption-agent in the NT. Eph 4:22 — "old self... corrupt through deceitful desires (*epithumiais*)"; 2Pe 1:4 — "corruption that is in the world because of sinful desire (*epithumia*)"; Gal 6:8 — "sows to his own flesh" — the fleshly desire-orientation. *Will* is also engaged: Pro 6:14 — "devises evil" — the will drives the devising; 2Pe 2:19 — "slaves of corruption" — the will is captured. *Conscience* appears in Job 33:27 — "I sinned and perverted what was right" — the conscience producing the confession of perversion.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — *Will* is the primary operative faculty. Eze 18:8 — "withholds his hand from injustice" — the will's active restraint; Eze 3:20 — "a righteous person turns from his righteousness and commits injustice" — the volitional turn; Job 34:32 — "if I have done iniquity, I will do it no more" — the will's capacity to cease. *Conscience* is engaged through the shame-dimension: Zep 3:5 — "the unjust knows no shame" — the conscience's shame-response is the relevant faculty, absent in the unjust; Job 6:29 — "let no injustice be done" — appeal to the conscience of Job's interlocutors.

---

### T2.5.2

**Question:** If so, what is that location, and what does it reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The conscience location (T2.5.1) reveals that wilful sinning involves a three-way inner dynamic: (1) the *will* as the faculty that commits the act, (2) the *conscience* as the faculty that witnesses it as wrong (either before, deterring it, or after, registering guilt), and (3) the *heart* as the deep-orientation centre from which both proceed. The relationship between conscience and will is antagonistic in the resistance register (VCG-03): conscience deters what the will is tempted to commit. When conscience fails to deter, sinning occurs — which is precisely why Psa 119:11 (word in the heart) and Exo 20:20 (fear of God before the eyes) function as conscience-strengthening mechanisms.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The retrospective conscience location reveals a distinctive feature of CHAR-2: the conscience is not engaged *during* the sinning (which is why the sinning is unintentional) but engages *upon disclosure*. This temporal gap between sin and conscience-engagement is the defining inner-being structure of unintentional sinning. It contrasts with CHAR-1, where the conscience is engaged (and overridden) during the sinning act itself. CHAR-2's conscience functions in a reactive, retrospective mode — it responds to information rather than deterring an act-in-progress.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The will-location reveals that confession has a *volitional threshold*: the conscience may have registered (producing the words) without the will being fully reoriented toward the moral reality named. Genuine confession crosses this threshold — the will agrees with the conscience's verdict and the confession expresses that agreement. Hollow confession (VCG-03; Pharaoh; Saul) stays below the threshold — the conscience has registered enough to produce words but the will remains self-directed. The characteristic thus requires not just the heart's striking and the mind's naming but the will's submission to what is being named as wrong.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The will-location (Jer 2:35) reveals that in its active-denial mode, conscience suppression is a *volitional act*: the person chooses to maintain the claim of innocence against the available evidence (God's prophetic word has already declared judgment). This is not innocent ignorance but active refusal. The will's engagement makes the active-denial mode the most culpable form of conscience suppression: the person knows enough to be held to account (Jer 2:35 — God will judge for "saying") but chooses the false claim over honest acknowledgment.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Will-location throughout the corpus reveals that refusal to repent is constitutively and irreducibly a will-event: it is the will's persistent non-departure that constitutes the characteristic. No other faculty can produce refusal to repent — the conscience may register the need to turn (otherwise it would be CHAR-4), the mind may know the truth (Heb 10:26), but it is the will's non-departure that makes it CHAR-5. The will-location is the essential constitutional site of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Will-as-disposition location reveals that habitual defection is the condition where the will no longer needs to make a fresh choice to sin — the disposition has become the default, producing sinning naturally. 1Jo 3:6's "keeps on sinning" describes this: the present continuous is not a series of discrete choices but a sustained directional flow. Hos 8:11 — altars for sinning becoming altars that produce more sinning — shows how the will's settled sinning disposition generates structural supports that make continued sinning the natural path of least resistance. The will is engaged as its dispositional capacity to form habits rather than its episodic capacity to choose.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Will-location reveals that contagious sin is both a leader's volitional act and a community-reshaping volitional force. The leader's will must be committed to the sinning course and must exercise its authority causatively; the community's will is reshaped by the transmitted sinning direction. The key insight from will-location: the community's sinning after contagious sin transmission is volitionally real — the community members are not forced to sin; their will has been shaped toward the sinning direction by the leader's authority. The will is the target of the transmission, not just the instrument.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Will-location reveals that political revolt is constitutively an act of the will: the decision to break submission and assert independence is a volitional act that cannot occur without the will's decisive engagement. The pa.sha root confirms this volitional character — it is not a passive drifting but an active wilful breaking-away. 2Ch 21:10's forsaking (the inner volitional act preceding the revolts) shows that the will's abandonment of God precedes and enables the political will's revolting.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Will-location reveals that sinful speech requires the will's consent to externalise the heart's corruption through the mouth. The heart generates the corrupted content; the will determines whether that content is externalised as speech. Jude 9 — Michael's restraint shows the will can withhold the blasphemous word even where the inner might to say it exists; the will's exercise of restraint is what prevents sinful speech. This confirms the will as the decisive inner faculty that mediates between the corrupted heart and the spoken word.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — The desire/appetite location (Jam 1:14; 2Pe 2:14/18) reveals that enticement operates through a constitutional faculty below the level of explicit volition: desire draws the person before the will has made a conscious decision. The desire-faculty is the *pre-volitional* motivational field within which enticement operates. 2Pe 2:14's "insatiable for sin" shows what happens when this faculty is not governed by the will but governs it: the desire becomes constitutionally uncontrollable ("insatiable"), reshaping the person's entire motivational structure.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Will-level location (Rom 7:17/20 — the "I" distinguished from the indwelling sin-force; Rom 6:16 — volitional obedience as the site of the master-choice; Gen 4:7 — the will addressed as the ruling faculty) reveals that the condition engages the will at both ends of its operation: the will is the target sin seeks to capture (Gen 4:7 — "its desire is for you, and you must rule over it") and the faculty through which the condition's enslavement operates (Rom 6:16 — whoever you obey is your master). The condition is not fully separate from the will — it operates through the will's captivity — but it is also not identical with the will — Rom 7:17/20's distinction between "I" and "sin that dwells within me" preserves the person's identity even within the condition's operation.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Will-level captivity (Joh 8:34 — slave to sin) and identity-allegiance level (1Jo 3:8 — of the devil) reveal that sin's enslaving power penetrates to the two deepest soul-level faculties: the will (the faculty that chooses) and the identity (the faculty that constitutes who the person is). The enslaving power is thus comprehensive in soul-depth: it captures both the directive capacity (will) and the constitutive identity (allegiance-belonging).

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Conscience-level location (Psa 51:3 — "my sin is ever before me"; Num 5:6 — "realizes his guilt") reveals that the divine record has a conscience-facing dimension: the objective record held by God has a corresponding inner signal in the conscience that (when functioning) makes the record accessible to the person's own awareness. The characteristic's definition ("the person carries this record whether they feel it or not") notes the conscience's optional engagement: the record is objective; conscience engagement is variable. When conscience functions, it mirrors the divine record internally; when suppressed, the record remains but the inner signal is silenced.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — The faith-level location (Act 10:43 — "everyone who believes... receives") reveals that the receiving dimension of the characteristic has a specific inner faculty through which it is received: trust directed toward Christ is the mechanism of reception. The OT parallel is faith-through-the-prescribed-means (bringing the animal, laying hands — 2Ch 29:23); the NT crystallises this as explicit personal faith in Christ's name. Faith is thus the soul-level faculty that bridges seeking and receiving: the one who believes is simultaneously seeking (expressing trust in the forgiving God) and receiving (the forgiveness comes to those who believe).

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Will-level location (Psa 78:17 — rebellion; Psa 78:32 — "they still sinned" — volitional persistence) reveals that generational sin, though transmitted through lineage, is actively maintained by each generation's own volitional choices: the inherited pattern requires individual volitional engagement to persist. The "still sinned" language (Psa 78:17/32 — "still more," "still sinned") names the will's active continuation of the inherited pattern rather than passive reception of it.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Conscience-level location (Luk 5:8 — spontaneous recognition; Luk 18:13 — penitential self-abasement; Rom 3:7 — conscience's condemnation-assessment) reveals that the sinner-identity is not only externally assigned (social-stigma VCG-01) or constitutionally imputed (VCG-02) but is also registered internally by the conscience when functioning correctly. The conscience is the faculty that can most precisely assess and name the sinner-identity: Luk 5:8's recognition is accurate; Luk 18:13's plea is appropriate. The conscience's correct engagement with the sinner-identity is the first step toward the repentance that the identity calls for (Luk 5:32 — "sinners to repentance").

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Conscience-level location (1Sa 25:31 — pu.qah; Lev 4/5 sequences; Hos 5:15) reveals that CHAR-17 is constitutively a conscience-characteristic: the inner experience of guilt-as-inner-state IS the conscience operating in its guilt-awareness mode. The conscience is not merely a secondary faculty that registers guilt after it exists elsewhere; guilt-as-inner-state is the conscience's specific form of operation when moral liability is recognised. The conscience's stagger (pu.qah — 1Sa 25:31) is the single-term expression of what the guilt-state does to the conscience when it fully engages.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Conscience-level location (2Sa 24:10 — heart-strike; Psa 38:18 — confession and sorrow; Lev 26:40/41 — confession with humbled heart) reveals that conscience is the inner faculty that detects and responds to iniquity-as-accumulated-crime. However, unlike CHAR-17 where conscience is the primary faculty (the characteristic IS conscience in guilt-awareness mode), in CHAR-18 conscience is a secondary responder: the iniquity exists in the divine record independently of conscience (Hos 13:12 — "bound up" whether Ephraim recognises it or not); conscience detects what is already there. The conscience-engagement is productive when it produces confession (Psa 38:18) and suppressed when self-flattery operates (Psa 36:2).

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Will-level location (Isa 31:6 — "turn... from whom you revolted"; Eze 18:28 — "considered and turned away"; Eze 18:30 — "repent and turn from all your transgressions") reveals that CHAR-19 is the will-characteristic of M10: the defining inner-being faculty of transgression-as-deliberate-boundary-crossing is the will's volitional capacity to turn (in either direction — toward or away from God). Every remedy-call in the corpus addresses the will's turning: "turn from transgression" (multiple verses in VCG-06). Conscience-level is also engaged (Pro 28:13 — concealment suppresses conscience; Psa 36:1 — transgression speaks in place of conscience's God-fear).

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Will-level location (1Ch 5:25 — allegiance-transfer; Eze 18:24 — turning away from righteousness; Lev 26:40 — walking contrary) reveals that faithlessness is a will-act at the level of covenant-allegiance: the will that breaks covenantal loyalty (the definition). Conscience-level location (Ezr 9:4/10:6 — appalled, mourning) reveals that a functioning conscience is deeply troubled by faithlessness — both in the self and in others. The conscience's response is grief rather than guilt-suppression when faithlessness is recognised.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Desire-level location (Eph 4:22; 2Pe 1:4) reveals the most analytically significant inner-being finding for CHAR-21: desire (*epithumia*) is named as the active mechanism of corruption — "corrupt through deceitful desires." The desire-faculty is not merely associated with perversion but is identified as its engine: the deceitful desire is what the corruption operates through. This makes CHAR-21 M10's characteristic that most precisely locates sin's mechanism in the desire-faculty — a finding not present in any other M10 characteristic studied with this precision.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Will-level location (Eze 18:8 — withholding; Eze 3:20 — turning; Job 34:32 — will-to-cease) reveals CHAR-22 as a will-governed characteristic: the will that chooses to withhold its hand from injustice (Eze 18:8) is the same will that, in the unjust person, deploys the hand in wrong. Conscience-level absence (Zep 3:5 — "knows no shame") is CHAR-22's most distinctive inner-being feature: the shamelessness diagnostic names the conscience's complete non-functioning as the marker of the thoroughly constituted unjust person.

---

### T2.5.3

**Question:** If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The evidence is not silent (see T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Conscience location is evidenced (T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Will-location is evidenced through the genuine/hollow contrast (T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Will-location is evidenced in the active-denial mode (Jer 2:35; T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Will-location is evidenced throughout the corpus (T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Will-as-disposition location is evidenced throughout (T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Will-location is evidenced throughout the corpus (T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Will-location is evidenced (T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Will-location is evidenced (Jude 9; Rev 13:5; 1Ti 6:4). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Desire/appetite location is evidenced (Jam 1:14; 2Pe 2:14/18). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Will-level location is evidenced (T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Will-level and identity-level location are evidenced (Joh 8:34; 1Jo 3:8). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Conscience-level location is evidenced (Psa 51:3; Num 5:6). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Faith-level location is evidenced (Act 10:43). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Will-level location is evidenced (Psa 78:17/32). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Conscience-level location is evidenced (Luk 5:8; Luk 18:13; Rom 3:7). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Conscience-level location is primary and defining (1Sa 25:31; Lev 4/5 sequences; Hos 5:15). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Conscience-level location is evidenced as a secondary responder (2Sa 24:10; Psa 38:18; Lev 26:40/41). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Will-level and conscience-level locations are both evidenced (Isa 31:6; Eze 18:28/30; Pro 28:13; Psa 36:1). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Will-level and conscience-level locations are evidenced (1Ch 5:25; Eze 18:24; Ezr 9:4/10:6). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Desire-level, will-level, and conscience-level locations are all evidenced (Eph 4:22; 2Pe 1:4; Pro 6:14; 2Pe 2:19; Job 33:27). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Will-level and conscience-level locations are evidenced (Eze 18:8; 3:20; Job 34:32; Zep 3:5). This prompt is superseded.

## T2.6 — Body — Significance

### T2.6.1

**Question:** Does the verse evidence link this characteristic to a specific body part?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Yes. Multiple body-part links are evidenced. (1) *Lips/mouth*: Psa 39:1 ("sin with my tongue"), Job 2:10 ("sin with his lips"), Job 31:30 ("not let my mouth sin"), Ecc 5:6 ("let not your mouth lead you into sin") — the mouth/lips/tongue is the most frequently mentioned body-part link. (2) *Body (soma)*: 1Cor 6:18 ("the sexually immoral person sins against his own body") — the whole body as the site of damage in sexual sinning. (3) *Hands*: 1Sa 24:11 ("no wrong or treason in my hands") — hands as the instrumental body-part for sinning or not sinning in action. (4) *Eyes*: Isa 1:4 contextually ("evil in your sight") implicates the eyes in moral evaluation, though this is God's eyes rather than the sinner's.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The corpus contains limited body-part evidence. The ritual actions described in VCG-02 involve specific body-located acts: Lev 8:15 ("Moses took the blood, and with his finger put it on the horns of the altar") — the finger as the instrument of purification. Lev 9:15 (Aaron killing the goat of the sin offering) involves hands. However, these are priestly body-parts performing the remedial ritual, not body parts of the sinner. Within the personal-moral register (VCG-01), no specific body part is named in connection with unintentional sinning. The act occurs without a specified body-part instrument (unlike CHAR-1's tongue/lips/hands). The 1Sa 14:33/34 context (eating with blood) involves the mouth as the instrument — "eating" — but the Pass A meaning does not foreground the body-part specifically.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Yes. The *mouth and lips* are the body-part link for confession as a speech-act. The entire corpus is composed of spoken acts: "Pharaoh sent and called Moses and Aaron and *said*" (Exo 9:27), "the son *said* to him" (Luk 15:21), "he *sings* before men and says" (Job 33:27). The mouth/lips are the terminal organ through which the inner confession is externalised. Neh 1:6 — "confessing the sins... that I now *pray* before you" — prayer-speech as the mode. No body part other than the speech organs is evidenced in direct connection with the confessional act itself.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Yes — in the active-denial mode. Jer 2:35 — "you *say*, 'I am innocent'" and "'I have not sinned'" — the mouth/speech organs are the body-part through which the inner suppression externalises. The speech-act of false innocence-claiming is the body-level expression of conscience suppression's denial mode. Judg 20:16 — literal physical *missing* of a target with a sling — physical body context, but no moral inner-being content.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Yes. Neh 9:29 — "they turned a *stubborn shoulder* and *stiffened their neck*" — two body parts are used as constitutional metaphors. The *shoulder* (kateph) — giving a stubborn shoulder was the gesture of refusing to carry a yoke, refusing to submit to the burden of obedience. The *neck* (oreph) — stiffening the neck was the gesture of an animal resisting the yoke of control. Both are bodily-metaphor expressions of the will's refusal to submit to God's direction.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — The 14-verse corpus contains no explicit body-part link for habitual defection. The characteristic operates through the heart (Exo 9:34 — inner organ metaphor rather than external body part), the ears (1Sa 2:25 — "would not listen" implies ear-reception, but ears are not named explicitly), and through outer practices (altars — Hos 8:11) rather than through a named external body-part.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-7]** S — The 19-verse corpus contains no explicit body-part link for contagious sin. The characteristic operates through the volitional-institutional level (walking, building, driving) without named body-part connection.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — The 9-verse corpus contains no body-part link for political revolt. The characteristic operates through political-social action without named body-part connection.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Yes — the mouth is the body-part link throughout the corpus. Col 3:8 — "slander... *from your mouth*" — the mouth is explicitly named as the body-part of externalisation. Rev 13:5 — "a *mouth* uttering haughty and blasphemous words" — the beast's mouth is named as the instrument. Rev 13:6 — "It opened its *mouth* to utter blasphemies" — the mouth-opening is the bodily act. Jude 9 — Michael "did not presume to pronounce" — the pronouncing is a mouth-act. The mouth is the defining bodily instrument of sinful speech throughout.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Yes — for enticement. 2Pe 2:14 — "*eyes* full of adultery" — the eyes are explicitly named as the body-part organ through which enticement operates: the gaze is the primary sensory channel for desire-exploitation. 2Pe 2:18 — "sensual passions of the flesh" — "flesh" (sarx) names the bodily-appetitive dimension as the operative medium of enticement. For hypocrisy and apostasy, no explicit body-part link appears in the corpus.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes — the members/flesh are the most consistently named body-level location. Rom 6:12 — "let not sin therefore reign in your mortal body" — the mortal body is named as the site of sin's would-be reign through its passions; Rom 6:13 — "do not present your members to sin as instruments for unrighteousness" — the members are named as the body-parts that sin deploys as instruments; Rom 7:5 — "our sinful passions... were at work in our members" — the members are where sinful passions operate; Rom 7:23 — "the law of sin that dwells in my members" — the members are the explicit bodily location of the sin-law. Additionally: Rom 8:3 — "sinful flesh" — the flesh as the body-level location of the condition's embedded power; Rom 8:10 — "the body is dead because of sin."

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — The 9-verse corpus contains no explicit body-part link for sin as enslaving power. The characteristic operates through the will's captivity and structural identity-level enslavement without named bodily organ connections.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes — multiple body-part links. (1) *Bones*: Psa 38:3 — "there is no health in my bones because of my sin" — the bone-level deterioration is the body's register of the sin-record's weight; (2) *Flesh*: Psa 38:3 — "there is no soundness in my flesh because of your indignation" — the flesh is the body-level expression of the record's consequence; (3) *Lips/mouth*: Isa 6:7 — "this has touched your lips; your guilt is taken away, and your sin atoned for" — the lips are the body-part through which Isaiah's sin was located and atoned for; Psa 59:12 — "for the sin of their mouths, the words of their lips" — the mouth is the organ through which sin is generated and enters the record; (4) *Hands*: Isa 31:7 — "your hands have sinfully made" — the hands as the active instruments creating the record-generating act.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes — the hands. 2Ch 29:23 — "they laid their hands on them" — the laying of hands on the sin-offering animals is the bodily act through which the person identifies with the offering and transfers the sin-burden to it; the hands are the body-part through which the seeking is physically enacted. Lev 16:21 (CHAR-13 corpus — the high priest laying hands on the scapegoat) provides the archetype. Additionally: blood as the bodily substance of atonement — Mat 26:28 — "my blood... poured out for many for the forgiveness of sins" — the body's blood is the specific physical substance through which NT forgiveness is achieved.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-15]** S — The 8-verse corpus does not explicitly name a body part in connection with generational sin. The characteristic operates through the corporate moral condition, heart-turning, and volitional rebellion without explicit body-part vocabulary.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes — hands. Jam 4:8 — "cleanse your hands, you sinners" — the hands are the body-part through which the sinner's outer sinful conduct is enacted; the hand-cleansing called for is the bodily dimension of the identity's address alongside the heart-purification. Luk 18:13 — "beat his breast" — the tax collector's bodily self-abasement uses the breast/chest as the body-part of penitential expression. Jude 15 — "all their deeds of ungodliness... and of all the harsh things that ungodly sinners have spoken against him" — the mouth is implied as the body-part through which the sinner-identity is expressed verbally.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes — the face. Ezr 9:6 — "I am ashamed and blush to lift my face to you, my God" — the face is the body-part through which the guilt-state is expressed; the inability to lift the face is the guilt's bodily expression. Additionally: Aaron's forehead (Exo 28:38) — "on Aaron's forehead... Aaron shall bear any guilt" — the forehead is the body-part on which the high priest literally bore Israel's guilt; the guilt is physically located on his forehead before God. Isaiah's lips (Isa 6:7) — "this has touched your lips; your guilt is taken away" — the lips are the body-part through which Isaiah's guilt was located and from which it was removed.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes — three body-part links. (1) *Hands and fingers*: Isa 59:3 — "your hands are defiled with blood and your fingers with iniquity" — the hands and fingers are the body-parts through which iniquity is enacted; (2) *Bones*: Eze 32:27 — "whose iniquities are upon their bones" — iniquity clings to the bones of the fallen warriors; Psa 31:10 — "my bones waste away" — iniquity causes bodily skeletal decay; (3) *Head/shoulders*: Psa 38:4 — "my iniquities have gone over my head; like a heavy burden, they are too heavy for me" — the head and shoulders are the body-parts over which the iniquity-burden overwhelms.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes — three body-part links. (1) *Lips and mouth*: Pro 10:19 — "when words are many, transgression is not lacking" — the lips/mouth as the body-part through which transgression overflows; Pro 12:13 — "ensnared by the transgression of his lips"; Isa 59:13 — "uttering from the heart lying words"; (2) *Neck/shoulders*: Lam 1:14 — "transgressions were bound into a yoke... set upon my neck" — the neck/shoulders as the body-part bearing the yoke-burden of transgression; (3) *Head*: Isa 1:5 — "the whole head is sick" — sustained revolt-transgression incapacitates the whole head.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes — two body-part links. (1) *Face and back*: 2Ch 29:6 — "they have forsaken him and have turned away their faces from the habitation of the Lord and turned their backs" — the face and the back are the body-parts through which the inner faithlessness is expressed; turning the back on God is the bodily enactment of the heart's turning; (2) *Womb and thigh*: Num 5:27 — "her womb shall swell, and her thigh shall fall away" — the faithless wife's reproductive organs are the body-parts on which the curse of faithlessness falls; the bodily consequence is located at the very organ that embodied the covenant of marriage.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes — three body-part links. (1) *Mouth, lips, tongue*: Pro 4:24 — "put away from you crooked speech, put devious talk far from you"; Pro 10:31 — "the perverse tongue will be cut off"; Pro 10:32 — "the mouth of the wicked, what is perverse"; (2) *Eyes*: Pro 16:30 — "whoever winks his eyes plans dishonest things" — the eye-wink as the bodily signal of perverse inner plotting; Exo 23:8 — "a bribe blinds the clear-sighted" — the eyes as the faculty blinded by bribery-perversion; (3) *The bowed/bent back*: Psa 38:6 — "I am utterly bowed down and prostrate" — the body bent by sin's weight.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes — three body-part links. (1) *Hands*: Psa 58:2 — "your hands deal out violence on earth"; Psa 7:3 — "if there is wrong in my hands"; Eze 18:8 — "withholds his hand from injustice"; (2) *Tongue/lips/mouth*: Isa 59:3 — "your tongue mutters wickedness"; Job 6:30 — "is there any injustice on my tongue?"; Zep 3:13 — "speak no lies"; Mal 2:6 — "no wrong was found on his lips"; (3) *Fingers*: Isa 59:3 — "your hands are defiled with blood and your fingers with iniquity."

---

### T2.6.2

**Question:** If so, what is Scripture doing by making that link — is it emphatic, functional, expressive, indicative, or mediating?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The body-part links serve distinct functions. For the mouth/lips/tongue (Psa 39:1; Job 2:10; Ecc 5:6), the function is *expressive and mediating* — the mouth is the organ through which inner sinful impulse externalises and through which restraint can intercept the act. The body-part is both the problem (it leads the person into sin, Ecc 5:6) and the solution-site (guarding it prevents the sin, Psa 39:1). For soma in 1Cor 6:18, the function is *indicative* — Paul indicates that sexual sin uniquely damages the very body through which it is committed, making the body both instrument and victim. For hands in 1Sa 24:11, the function is *instrumental* — hands are the agents of action (killing) that David specifically restrains.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The finger in Lev 8:15 (Moses applying blood to altar horns) functions as the *mediating instrument* of purification — the precise physical action that conveys the atoning remedy to the defiled object. This is a functional body-part link in the remedial direction: the priest's finger is the means by which the unintentional defilement is addressed. The body-part here is in the remedy, not in the sinning act. This is the inverse of CHAR-1, where the body-part (tongue, lips, hands) is in the sinning act itself.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The mouth-link is *expressive and constitutive*: the mouth expresses the inner conscience-recognition, and the expression is constitutive of confession — without the speaking, the inner state is guilt (CHAR-17) but not yet confession (CHAR-3). Scripture consistently shows confession happening through speech because speech is what makes the inner moral reality public — before God (prayer-confession), before persons (Shimei before the king — 2Sa 19:20; Judas before the priests — Mat 27:4), or before a community (corporate confessions — VCG-02). The body-part link is thus *necessary but not sufficient*: the mouth must speak, but what the mouth speaks must arise from conscience and will engaged, not merely from social calculation.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The mouth-link in Jer 2:35 is *expressive and constitutive* — the spoken claim is not merely a symptom of the inner suppression but constitutes and reinforces it. God's judgment falls specifically on the speech-act: "I will bring you to judgment for *saying*, 'I have not sinned'" — the speaking of the denial is itself the judged act. The body-part link is emphatic: the mouth, which should confess (CHAR-3), instead denies, and God holds the person accountable for the specific speech-act of denial.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The body-part link (Neh 9:29) is *expressive and emphatic*: the shoulder and neck metaphors embody the inner attitude of refusal in physical-gesture language. The imagery is drawn from animal behaviour (the ox refusing the yoke) and applied to the human will: the person's inner refusal to repent takes the physical form of an animal's resistance to being guided. This is emphatic because it makes the inner disposition viscerally visible — refusal to repent is not an intellectual position but a physical posture of resistance. The link also makes the characteristic's active nature unmistakable: a stiffened neck is not passive but actively resistant.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — No explicit body-part link is evidenced. This prompt is not applicable.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-7]** S — No body-part link is evidenced. This prompt is not applicable.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — No body-part link is evidenced. This prompt is not applicable.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The mouth-link is *constitutive*: sinful speech is definitionally a mouth-act. Without the mouth, the inner corruption remains unexpressed as CHAR-9. The mouth-link also functions *diagnostically*: Col 3:8 — "from your mouth" — addresses the command of renunciation at the point of externalisation; the mouth is where the characteristic either occurs or is prevented. Rev 13:5/6 — the beast's mouth as the instrument of its constitutive blasphemy — the mouth is the beast's defining operative faculty for its anti-God identity. The body-part link is the most consistent and constitutive in the entire M10 corpus.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — 2Pe 2:14's eyes-link does two things. (1) *Names the perceptive channel of enticement*: the eyes are the sensory pathway through which the lure enters — "eyes full of adultery" names a gaze that has been formed to see through the lens of adulterous desire; the perceptive faculty has been captured by the desire-object. (2) *Connects the inner appetite to outer physical sensation*: the eyes bridge the inner desire and the outer world of visible lures — the body's sensory capacity is the interface through which external enticements engage the inner desire-faculty.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The members/flesh body-link (Rom 6:12/13; 7:5/23; 8:3/10) does four things. (1) *Locates the condition's operational site*: sin operates through the body's concrete physical capacities — not as an ethereal abstraction but through the members' actual motions; (2) *Explains the mind-flesh split*: the body-link explains why knowing what is right (Rom 7:23 — the mind's law) does not produce doing what is right (the members serving sin's law) — the condition has colonised the physical constitution; (3) *Establishes what the condition must be condemned in*: Rom 8:3 — God "condemned sin in the flesh" — the body-level is where the condition had to be addressed; (4) *Reveals the body's mortality as the condition's consequence*: Rom 8:10 — "the body is dead because of sin" — the physical body bears the terminal consequence of the universal condition.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — No body-part link is evidenced. This prompt is not applicable.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The body-part links (bones — Psa 38:3; lips — Isa 6:7; Psa 59:12; hands — Isa 31:7) perform three functions. (1) *Naming the instrument of sin*: the hands (Isa 31:7), the mouth (Psa 59:12) are named as the body-parts through which specific sins are enacted and the record entries are created; (2) *Naming the site of consequence*: the bones and flesh (Psa 38:3) are where the record's weight registers physically — the body bears the evidence of the record's moral cost; (3) *Naming the site of atonement*: Isa 6:7 — the lips are the specific body-part where the divine action of atonement addresses the sin; the coal touches the place of the sin's origination.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — The hands-link (2Ch 29:23) does two things. (1) *Enacts identification*: laying hands on the animal identifies the person (or community) with the offering — the sin is symbolically transferred to the substitute through the physical contact; the seeking is not purely inner but requires bodily engagement to be complete. (2) *Grounds the seeking in the body*: the bodily act of hand-laying makes the inner seeking externally visible and communally enacted — the king and assembly together lay hands, making the corporate seeking a shared bodily act.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-15]** S — No body-part link is evidenced. This prompt is not applicable.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Jam 4:8's hands-link does two things. (1) *Names the outer expression of the sinner-identity*: the hands are the visible instrument of sinful conduct; the call to cleanse them is a call to address the outer behavioural expression of the inner sinner-identity; (2) *Grounds the inner-identity in bodily action*: the parallel "cleanse your hands... purify your hearts" establishes that the sinner-identity has both an outer (hands — conduct) and an inner (heart — disposition) dimension that must both be addressed. The bodily expression is not separable from the inner identity.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Three distinct body-part functions. (1) *Face-avoidance* (Ezr 9:6): the downcast face before God names the body's expression of the guilt-state's shame dimension; the face cannot be lifted because the guilt precludes the standing-before-God that face-lifting implies; (2) *Forehead-bearing* (Exo 28:38): the forehead as the visible body-part that bore guilt before God establishes the priestly guilt-bearing as a physical and visible act — the guilt literally rests on the person's face/head in the representative's bearing; (3) *Lips-location* (Isa 6:7): the lips as the body-part of Isaiah's guilt names the speech-faculty as the site of his specific form of guilt (unclean lips before the holy God — Isa 6:5).

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Three distinct body-part functions. (1) *Hands as instruments of iniquity* (Isa 59:3): the hands name the body-part of active wrongdoing; iniquity is enacted through the body's working members; the moral crime has a bodily-enactment dimension; (2) *Bones as iniquity's permanent mark* (Eze 32:27): iniquity clings to the bones even in death, naming the body as the permanent carrier of the iniquity-record into Sheol; (3) *Head/shoulders as overwhelmed bearer* (Psa 38:4): the head-overflowing image names the body-part through which the accumulated weight is expressed; the burden metaphor uses the body's carrying capacity to name iniquity's weight.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Three distinct body-part functions. (1) *Lips as transgression's instrument* (Pro 10:19; Pro 12:13; Isa 59:13): the mouth is the outer organ through which the heart's transgression is expressed; "transgression of the lips" names the body's speaking-organ as the conduit for inner rebellion becoming outer act; (2) *Neck as transgression's burden-point* (Lam 1:14): the yoke on the neck images the transgression as an enslaving weight physically borne; the neck is the body-part that carries what the transgression has imposed; (3) *Head as revolt's victim* (Isa 1:5): the head incapacitated by sustained revolt names the body's commanding faculty as the location of systemic deterioration from persistent transgression.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Two distinct body-part functions. (1) *Face and back as bodily expression of inner allegiance-direction* (2Ch 29:6): turning the face toward God or away is the body's expression of the heart's covenant-orientation; the face-direction images the inner will's God-direction; turning the back is the bodily expression of the heart that has definitively turned away; (2) *Womb and thigh as the site of covenant-embodied consequence* (Num 5:27): the marriage covenant was embodied in the marital relationship; faithlessness in that embodied covenant produces bodily consequences at the embodied organs of the covenant's expression — the curse falls on what expressed the covenant.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Three distinct body-part functions. (1) *Mouth/tongue as perversity's primary expressive organ*: Pro 10:31/32 — the tongue and mouth are the body-parts through which inner perversity is most immediately expressed outward; the perverse tongue is the inner corruption's most visible bodily instrument; (2) *Eyes as perversity's corrupted perceptive organ*: the blinded eyes (Exo 23:8 — bribery) and the winking eyes (Pro 16:30 — planned dishonesty) name the eyes as the body-part through which perversity distorts perception and signals intent; (3) *The bowed body as perversity's consequence*: Psa 38:6 — the whole body bent and prostrate is the bodily expression of what sin's perversion has done to the person's inner posture.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Three distinct body-part functions. (1) *Hands as injustice's primary enacting organs* (Psa 58:2; Psa 7:3; Eze 18:8): the hands are the body-parts through which the heart's devised injustice is enacted in the world; "withholds his hand from injustice" (Eze 18:8) confirms the hand as the conduct-level instrument the will either deploys or restrains; (2) *Tongue/lips as injustice's verbal instrument* (Isa 59:3; Job 6:30; Zep 3:13): the tongue expresses inward injustice verbally — "mutters wickedness" (Isa 59:3); (3) *Fingers as injustice's detailed-action organs* (Isa 59:3): the fingers represent the precision instruments of the wrongdoing — "your fingers with iniquity" naming the detailed physical execution of the unjust act.

---

### T2.6.3

**Question:** If no body-part link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Body-part links are evidenced (see T2.6.1 and T2.6.2). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Limited body-part evidence is present (VCG-02 priestly finger/hands in remedy; 1Sa 14:33/34 implied mouth in eating). The link is in the remedy-action rather than the sinning-act. This is noted.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Body-part link (mouth/lips/speech organs) is evidenced throughout the corpus (T2.6.1). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Body-part link (mouth) is evidenced in Jer 2:35 (T2.6.1). The physical-literal Judg 20:16 is noted as having body-sling-target content with no moral inner-being link. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Body-part links (shoulder and neck — Neh 9:29) are evidenced (T2.6.1). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(S)*

**[CHAR-6]** S — No explicit body-part link is evidenced in the 14-verse corpus. Habitual defection operates through the inner constitutional faculties (heart, will, relational orientation) rather than through named external body parts. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-7]** S — No body-part link is evidenced in the 19-verse corpus. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(S)*

**[CHAR-8]** S — No body-part link is evidenced. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Body-part link (mouth) is extensively evidenced throughout the corpus (T2.6.1). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Body-part link (eyes — 2Pe 2:14; flesh — 2Pe 2:18) is evidenced for enticement. Hypocrisy and apostasy have no explicit body-part link in the corpus. Noted.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Body-part link (members/flesh/mortal body) is extensively evidenced throughout VCG-03 (T2.6.1). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(S)*

**[CHAR-12]** S — No body-part link is evidenced in the 9-verse corpus. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Multiple body-part links are evidenced (Psa 38:3 — bones/flesh; Isa 6:7 — lips; Psa 59:12 — mouth; Isa 31:7 — hands). This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Body-part link (hands — 2Ch 29:23; blood — Mat 26:28) is evidenced. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-15]** S — No body-part link is evidenced in the 8-verse corpus. Noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Body-part links (hands — Jam 4:8; breast — Luk 18:13) are evidenced. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Body-part links (face — Ezr 9:6; forehead — Exo 28:38; lips — Isa 6:7) are evidenced. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Body-part links (hands/fingers — Isa 59:3; bones — Eze 32:27/Psa 31:10; head — Psa 38:4) are evidenced. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Body-part links (lips/mouth — Pro 10:19/12:13/Isa 59:13; neck — Lam 1:14; head — Isa 1:5) are evidenced. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Body-part links (face/back — 2Ch 29:6; womb/thigh — Num 5:27) are evidenced. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Body-part links (mouth/tongue/lips — multiple VCG-01; eyes — Exo 23:8/Pro 16:30; bowed body — Psa 38:6) are extensively evidenced. This prompt is superseded.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Body-part links (hands — multiple; tongue/lips — multiple; fingers — Isa 59:3) are extensively evidenced. This prompt is superseded.
