## T2.8 — Body — Deposit

### T2.8.1

**Question:** Does sustained operation of this characteristic leave a constitutional deposit in the body or its design — including DNA or generational consequence?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The corpus offers limited but present evidence. Isa 1:4 ("sinful nation, a people laden with iniquity, offspring of evildoers, children who deal corruptly") describes a generational pattern in which sinning has become a constitutional characteristic of a people — "offspring of evildoers" suggests a hereditary dimension, though the text does not specify a biological mechanism. Neh 13:26 ("foreign women made even him to sin") implies that sustained exposure to sinning patterns erodes constitutional resistance. The strongest deposit-language in the corpus is Hos 4:7/13:2 — escalating sinning producing intensified idolatry — which suggests a formed disposition that progressively resists reversal. However, explicit DNA or bodily-deposit language is absent from the corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — The 18-verse corpus provides no evidence of a constitutional deposit from sustained unintentional sinning. The Levitical framework addresses each occurrence episodically (Lev 4:2; Num 15:27/28) without describing a cumulative deposit in the person. The daily and annual cultic purifications (Exo 29:36; Eze 45:18) imply that unintentional defilement *accumulates on sacred spaces* (requiring periodic comprehensive cleansing), but the corpus does not evidence a corresponding inner-person deposit from repeated unintentional sinning.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(S)*

**[CHAR-3]** S — The corpus does not evidence a constitutional body-deposit from sustained confession. The sustained practice of confession (Neh 1:6 — "day and night"; Dan 9:5 — extended prayer) produces formative effects in the inner person (moral transparency, intercession capacity — T1.6.2) but the corpus does not name a bodily or generational deposit.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Yes — Tit 3:11 provides the clearest deposit evidence: "warped and sinful" (*exestraptai kai hamartanei*) — the perfect participle "warped" (*exestraptai*) suggests a completed deformation that has become a settled constitutional state. Sustained conscience suppression has produced a person who is constitutionally distorted — not temporarily confused but structurally deformed. This is the deposit: a character whose moral faculty has been twisted out of its proper orientation through sustained refusal of the conscience's witness.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Yes. Neh 9:29 — "stubborn shoulder and stiffened their neck" — the bodily-metaphor language of *stiffening* (*qashu* — to harden, make stiff) describes a completed deformation: the neck that has been stiffened is a neck that has been hardened into a fixed posture. The perfect-aspect language implies a formed constitutional state. The Kings corpus's trajectory from "did not depart" (early kings) to "clung to" (2Ki 3:3 — Jehoram) shows a progression from passive non-departure to active attachment — consistent with a deepening constitutional deposit of the refusal-orientation in the will.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Yes. Exo 9:34 — "hardened his heart" — the hardening is a constitutional deposit: each sinning-and-hardening cycle leaves the heart in a harder state, which is the starting point for the next cycle. The hardening is cumulative: the heart becomes progressively harder with each iteration. Hos 8:11 — altars for sinning becoming established structures — shows the social-institutional deposit: habitual defection embeds itself in institutional structures that outlast any individual's disposition. Hos 10:9 — "from the days of Gibeah... there they have continued" — generational persistence as constitutional deposit.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Yes — and the corpus evidences this more concretely than any other characteristic. 2Ki 23:15 — "the altar at Bethel, the high place erected by Jeroboam the son of Nebat, who made Israel to sin" — Jeroboam's contagious sin has left a physical-structural deposit (the altar) that persists for generations after his death. The deposit is institutional: the physical structure at Bethel functions as an ongoing transmission mechanism long after the original leader is gone. This is the most explicit deposit evidence in the M10 corpus: a named structure built through contagious sin leadership that endures for centuries.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Yes — the "to this day" markers are the evidence. 1Ki 12:19 / 2Ch 10:19 — "Israel has been in rebellion against the house of David to this day" — the revolt has deposited a permanent political-relational fracture that persists to the narrator's present. 2Ki 8:22 / 2Ch 21:10 — "Edom revolted from the rule of Judah to this day" — similarly permanent. The deposit is a *political-relational* fracture: the governing relationship has been permanently broken and does not restore itself. This is a social-structural deposit rather than a bodily-constitutional one: the political community's relationship to the governing authority has been permanently altered by the revolt.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Yes. Two deposit dimensions. (1) *Constitutional character formed around sinful speech*: 2Ti 3:2 — the blasphemous/abusive disposition is named as a settled character trait in end-times persons; 1Ti 6:4 — conceit feeds on the slander it generates, deepening the inner corruption. (2) *The unforgivable blasphemy as an irreversible inner state*: Mat 12:31 — "will not be forgiven" — this is the most severe deposit: a permanent condition of foreclosed forgiveness resulting from the specific act of blasphemy against the Spirit. This is not a bodily deposit but a spiritual-moral constitutional deposit of permanent consequence.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Yes — most clearly for enticement. 2Pe 2:14 — "hearts trained in greed" — "trained" (*gegumnasmenos* — a perfect participle, indicating a completed formation with ongoing effect) names the constitutional deposit of sustained enticement: the heart has been systematically trained into greedy appetite through sustained engagement with the enticement mechanism. The deposit is the formed inner character: a heart constitutionally oriented toward greed.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes — the most extensive constitutional deposit evidence in the M10 corpus. Four deposit forms. (1) *Death*: Rom 6:23 — "the wages of sin is death" — death is the permanent constitutional deposit of the condition; Rom 8:10 — "the body is dead because of sin" — the mortality of the human body is the physical deposit of the condition inherited from Adam (Rom 5:12 — "death spread to all men"). (2) *Hardening*: Heb 3:13 — "hardened by the deceitfulness of sin" — the progressive hardening of the heart against God's voice is a formed constitutional deposit of the condition's sustained operation. (3) *Sin's indwelling*: Rom 7:17/20 — "sin that dwells within me" — the indwelling is a constitutional reality, not a passing state; the Greek (*oikousa* — present participle) names it as an ongoing inhabitation. (4) *Accumulating measure*: 1Th 2:16 — "filling up the measure of their sins" — the condition produces an accumulating divine-ledger deposit that moves toward a full measure triggering judgment.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Yes. Joh 8:34 — "everyone who practices sin is a slave to sin" — the slave-state is the constitutional deposit of sustained sinning practice: the accumulated practice has produced a constituted slave-identity. 1Jo 3:8 — "of the devil" — the allegiance-capture is the deepest constitutional deposit: the person's identity-belonging has been impressed toward the devil as its master. 1Jo 5:16 — "sin that leads to death" — the most severe deposit: the enslaving power in its most advanced form deposits the person in a condition where death is the trajectory.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes — the most extensive deposit evidence in M10. Four deposit forms. (1) *Internal heart-engraving*: Jer 17:1 — "engraved on the tablet of their heart" — the sin-record is inscribed internally as a permanent deposit on the heart's constitutional structure; the iron pen and diamond point indicate irreversibility without divine intervention; (2) *Separation from God*: Isa 59:2 — accumulated record produces a structured relational barrier as its deposit; (3) *National-institutional legacy*: VCG-04 — the Jeroboam-sin deposit persists across royal generations (46 verses) as a named institutional inheritance; (4) *Stored divine record*: Hos 13:12 — "his sin is kept in store" — the divine side of the deposit is the sealed, stored record awaiting reckoning.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes — but in the positive direction, uniquely among M10 characteristics. (1) *Love as deposit*: Luk 7:47 — "she loved much" — the forgiveness received deposits love as an ongoing inner orientation; the deposit is the love produced by the magnitude of forgiveness received; (2) *Life as deposit*: Col 2:13 — "made alive" — the life-constitutional change is a permanent deposit; the formerly-dead person is now constitutionally alive; (3) *Spirit-indwelling as deposit*: Act 2:38 — the Holy Spirit is received as a gift following forgiveness — the Spirit's indwelling is the characteristic's most profound constitutional deposit; (4) *Redemption-identity as deposit*: Col 1:14; Eph 1:7 — "we have redemption, the forgiveness of sins" — the forgiven person carries a permanent identity-deposit: they are redeemed, they have received the forgiveness.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Yes — two deposit forms. (1) *Prolonged sin-conditionedness*: Isa 64:5 — "in our sins we have been a long time" — the extended duration of the sinning-condition is a constitutional deposit; the community has been formed by the sustained pattern into a people characterised by it; (2) *Defilement*: Eze 37:23 — "they shall not defile themselves anymore... I will save them from all the backslidings in which they have sinned, and will cleanse them" — the defilement produced by the accumulated backslidings is the constitutional deposit requiring divine cleansing; the community's inner constitution has been defiled by the sustained sinning-pattern.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes — three deposit forms. (1) *Constituted identity*: Rom 5:19 — "made sinners" — the Adamic imputation is the constitutional deposit of the sinner-identity in all humanity; the deposit is the sinner-standing that precedes any individual's sinning acts; (2) *Accumulated sinning history*: Jam 5:20 — "cover a multitude of sins" — the sinner who wanders has accumulated a multitude of sins as the deposit of their sustained sinner-identity; (3) *Inner defilement*: Jam 4:8 — "purify your hearts" — the heart-defilement requiring purification is the constitutional deposit of the sustained sinner-identity on the inner person.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes — three deposit forms. (1) *Accumulated weight*: Ezr 9:6 — "our guilt has mounted up to the heavens" — the accumulated guilt is a measurable constitutional deposit that has risen above the head; (2) *Indelible stain*: Jer 2:22 — "the stain of your guilt is still before me" — the guilt-stain is an indelible deposit on the inner person that no self-generated cleansing removes; (3) *Punitive legacy*: Jer 32:18 — "you repay the guilt of fathers to their children after them" — the guilt-deposit is transmitted intergenerationally; the deposit from the fathers' guilt becomes the children's inherited moral-consequential burden.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Yes — three deposit forms. (1) *Divine-record deposit*: Hos 13:12 — "the iniquity of Ephraim is bound up; his sin is kept in store" — God maintains an accumulated sealed record; Gen 15:16 — "not yet complete" — the accumulation grows as a measured deposit; (2) *Body-bone deposit*: Eze 32:27 — "iniquities are upon their bones" — iniquity clings permanently to the person's physical remains; Psa 31:10 — bones wasting away — the physical deterioration is the bodily deposit of the crime; (3) *Generational deposit*: Exo 20:5 — "visiting the iniquity of the fathers on the children to the third and fourth generation" — the fathers' iniquity-deposit is transmitted as a generational moral inheritance.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes — three deposit forms. (1) *Record held in divine count*: Amos 1:3 — "for three transgressions... and for four" — God maintains a counted record; Dan 8:13 — "the transgression that makes desolate" — a specific transgression enshrined in heavenly discourse; Dan 9:24 — "to finish the transgression" — the accumulated transgression must be completed/finished, implying it persists as a deposit until that moment; (2) *Identity-level labelling*: Isa 48:8 — "from before birth you were called a rebel" — the identity deposit of transgression precedes birth; Isa 57:4 — "children of transgression" — the deposit passes generationally; (3) *Oppressive weight-burden*: Lam 1:14 — the yoke-burden bound and set on the neck — a persistent bodily-moral weight.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes — three deposit forms. (1) *Generational communal deposit*: 2Ch 30:7 — "your fathers and your brothers, who were faithless to the Lord God of their fathers, so that he made them a desolation" — the faithlessness of the fathers is what the children are warned not to repeat; the deposit is the pattern and consequence transmitted; 1Ch 9:1 — the exile as the deposit of accumulated faithlessness; (2) *Identity-level character deposit*: Isa 48:8 — "I knew that you would surely deal treacherously" — the constitutional bent foreknown from before birth is the deepest deposit; (3) *National shame deposit*: Dan 9:7 — "open shame... in all the lands to which you have driven them, because of the treachery that they have committed against you" — the shame persisting in every land of exile as the national deposit of faithlessness.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes — three deposit forms. (1) *Mind-depravity deposit*: 1Ti 6:5 — "depraved in mind and deprived of the truth" — the mind's depravity is a constitutional deposit that persists as the settled condition of the corrupted person's cognitive faculty; (2) *Desire-capture deposit*: Eph 4:22 — "corrupt through deceitful desires" — the ongoing corruption through desire is an accumulating deposit; 2Pe 2:19 — "slaves of corruption" — the enslavement is a constitutionally established condition; (3) *Bodily perishability*: Rom 8:21 — "bondage to corruption" — the creation's bondage to corruption is a constitutional condition awaiting eschatological liberation.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes — three deposit forms. (1) *Divine memory-record*: Rev 18:5 — "her sins are heaped high as heaven, and God has remembered her iniquities" — God's memory holds the accumulating record of injustice as a deposit; (2) *Fixed character deposit*: Luk 16:10 — "dishonest in very little is also dishonest in much" — the injustice is deposited as a stable character-trait that does not vary with scale; (3) *Shameless-conscience deposit*: Zep 3:5 — "the unjust knows no shame" — the sustained injustice deposits a conscience that is permanently insensible to its own wrongdoing.

---

### T2.8.2

**Question:** What evidence supports or contradicts this?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Supporting evidence: Isa 1:4 (generational sin-characterisation), Neh 13:26 (constitutional vulnerability acquired through exposure), Hos 13:2 (escalating sinning suggesting formed capacity). Contradicting evidence: Eze 18:19–20 explicitly rejects generational punishment for sin: "the son shall not suffer for the iniquity of the father" — which addresses legal accountability rather than constitutional deposit but does warn against reading generational consequence as constitutional transmission. The cultic-atonement corpus (VCG-04: Lev 4:22 — unintentional sinning still real and requiring remedy) suggests that even non-deposit sinning is morally consequential, implying that the deposit question is not the primary evidence-frame.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — No evidence directly supports a constitutional body-deposit from unintentional sinning in this corpus. The closest evidence is the communal dimension of priestly sinning (Lev 4:3 — "bringing guilt on the people"), which implies a corporate moral condition accumulating from a leader's inadvertent acts. But this is communal guilt-accumulation rather than a constitutional deposit in individual persons. The evidence is insufficient to confirm or deny a bodily-deposit finding.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(S)*

**[CHAR-3]** S — No direct evidence for or against a bodily deposit from confession is present in the 34-verse corpus. Lam 5:7 ("our fathers sinned, and are no more; and we bear their iniquities") names a generational consequence of sin, but this is about inherited iniquity from the fathers' sinning, not a deposit from the fathers' confessing. The evidential gap is noted.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Supporting: Tit 3:11 ("warped" — completed deformation); Ecc 8:12 ("does evil a hundred times" — habituated repeated sinning implying a formed capacity for conscience-absent evil). The progressive character of the deformation is implied by the habituated-mode evidence: the person who has sinned a hundred times without the fear of God has built a habit-structure that constitutes a deposit. Contradicting or complicating: Job 35:6 — "if you have sinned, what do you accomplish against him?" — Elihu's point that sin harms the sinner but does not injure God suggests the deposit is in the creature, not in the divine-creature relationship per se.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Supporting: Neh 9:29 ("stiffened their neck" — formed posture); 2Ki 3:3 ("clung to" — active attachment beyond mere non-departure); 2Ki 15:18 ("all his days" — lifetime orientation confirming deep formation). Contradicting or complicating: the corpus does not evidence any case where refusal to repent is described as biologically inherited or bodily-organic; the "as his fathers had done" (2Ki 15:9) is social-formational transmission rather than genetic deposit. The deposit is formational (character formed through sustained refusal) rather than biological.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Supporting: Exo 9:34 (progressive hardening — cumulative individual deposit); Hos 8:11 (institutionalised altars — social-structural deposit); Hos 10:9 (from Gibeah — generational transmission). Contradicting or complicating: 1Jo 3:6's positive statement — "no one who abides in him keeps on sinning" — implies that the deposit is not irrevocable: abiding in Christ structurally prevents the pattern, implying that the pattern can be broken by the abiding relationship. The deposit is real but not permanent in the face of the abiding relationship.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Supporting: 2Ki 23:15 (altar at Bethel — permanent structural deposit); 1Ki 22:52 — three generations receiving and passing on the sinning direction (Ahaziah following father, mother, and Jeroboam); Jer 32:35 — "they built the high places of Baal" — institutionalised structures. Contradicting or complicating: 2Ki 23:15 — Josiah was able to demolish the altar, showing the deposit is not permanent; but the fact that the altar survived for ~300 years since Jeroboam's reign shows the deposit's remarkable persistence.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Supporting: four "to this day" instances (1Ki 12:19; 2Ki 8:22; 2Ch 10:19; 2Ch 21:10) — each naming a permanent political fracture as the enduring deposit. 2Ki 8:20 / 2Ch 21:8 — "set up a king of their own" — the positive assertion of independence becomes a permanent structural reality. Contradicting or complicating: no verse evidences restoration of the broken relationship; the deposits appear total and permanent within the corpus's time horizon.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Supporting: Mat 12:31 (permanent irreversible deposit — unforgiven condition); 2Ti 3:2 (blasphemous character as settled end-times type); VCG-03's beast (blasphemy as constitutive identity — the deepest deposit: entire being formed around sinful speech). Contradicting or complicating: 1Ti 1:13 — Paul's former blasphemy was reversed by mercy, suggesting that at least the VCG-01/02 forms of sinful speech are reversible; not all sinful speech produces an irreversible deposit. The deposit is irreversible only at the Spirit-blasphemy threshold (Mat 12:31).

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Supporting: 2Pe 2:14 — "hearts trained in greed" — the perfect participle confirms completed formation with ongoing deposit; "insatiable for sin" — the insatiability is the deposited character of formed appetite. Contradicting or complicating: Jam 1:14 describes the enticement mechanism as episodic ("when he is lured") — not every instance of enticement produces a constitutional deposit; the deposit accumulates through sustained engagement. For hypocrisy and apostasy, the corpus does not explicitly name a deposit beyond the immediate consequence.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Supporting: all four deposit dimensions are multi-verse evidenced: death (Rom 5:12/6:23/8:10); hardening (Heb 3:13); indwelling sin (Rom 7:17/20); accumulating measure (1Th 2:16). Contradicting or complicating: Heb 4:15 — "without sin" — Christ's constitutional sinlessness and 2Cor 5:21 — "him who knew no sin" — demonstrate that the deposit is not uncreatable: a genuinely human person (Jesus) existed without it. The deposit is thus a fallen-condition deposit, not a creation-constitutional deposit. 1Cor 7:28/36 — "it is no sin" — the term's negative use confirms that not every human experience carries the deposit; the condition is universal but its specific acts are not.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Supporting: Joh 8:34 (slave — constituted state); 1Jo 3:8 ("of the devil" — identity deposit); 1Jo 5:16 (death-trajectory). Contradicting or complicating: 1Jo 3:9 — "no one born of God makes a practice of sinning" — the new birth deposit counters and prevents the sin-enslavement deposit; the born-of-God constitution produces a counter-deposit (God's seed abiding) that prevents the sin-enslavement deposit from forming. The deposit of sin-enslavement is real but not irresistible in the face of the new-birth deposit.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Supporting: Jer 17:1 (heart-engraving — permanent inscription); Isa 59:2 (separation — relational deposit); VCG-04 (Jeroboam-pattern — institutional deposit persisting 46 verses worth of kings); Hos 13:12 (kept in store — divine retention deposit). Contradicting or complicating: Isa 43:25 — "I will not remember your sins" — the deposit is not irremovable; Jer 31:34 — "I will remember their sin no more" — the new covenant promise erases the deposit from divine memory; Eze 33:16 — "none of the sins shall be remembered against him" — individual repentance can erase the deposit's record-against-me function. The deposit is real and deep but not permanently irremovable.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Supporting: Luk 7:47 (love — affective deposit); Col 2:13 (alive — vital deposit); Act 2:38 (Spirit — spirit-level deposit); Col 1:14/Eph 1:7 (redemption identity — relational deposit). The OT register (kip.pu.rim — VCG-01) presents annual atonement deposits that are provisional: each year's deposit covers the current year but requires renewal; the deposit is temporary. The NT register (VCG-02) presents permanent deposits: "in him we have redemption" (Col 1:14 — present tense, permanent possession) vs. the OT "once a year" (Exo 30:10). The NT deposit is permanent; the OT deposit is provisional and renewable.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Supporting: Isa 64:5 ("a long time in our sins" — duration as deposit); Eze 37:23 (defilement requiring cleansing — constitutional deposit). Contradicting or complicating: 1Ki 8:47 — "if they turn their heart... and repent" — the possibility of turning implies the deposit is not constitutionally irreversible; the heart can turn even within the accumulated condition. The deposit is real (long-duration sinning, defilement) but is addressable through divine intervention (Eze 37:23 — "I will cleanse them") and human heart-turning (1Ki 8:47).

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Supporting: Rom 5:19 (constituted standing — deposit from Adam); Jam 5:20 (multitude of sins — accumulated); Jam 4:8 (heart requiring purification — inner deposit). Contradicting or complicating: Luk 15:7/10 — joy over "one sinner who repents" — the deposit is reversible through repentance; 1Ti 1:15 — "Christ Jesus came into the world to save sinners" — the deposit is addressable through Christ's saving mission; Psa 51:13 — "sinners will return to you" — the sinner-identity can be transformed through return to God. The deposit is real but reversible through divine action.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Supporting: Ezr 9:6 (accumulation deposit — risen above head); Jer 2:22 (indelible stain deposit); Jer 32:18 (intergenerational deposit). Contradicting or complicating: Isa 6:7 — "your guilt is taken away" — the indelible deposit is removable through divine action; Jer 33:8 — "I will cleanse them from all the guilt" — divine cleansing addresses even the accumulated deposit; the deposit is real but not permanently irremovable. The deposit is constitutionally present and deepens without resolution, but yields to divine cleansing.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Supporting: Hos 13:12 (divine-record deposit — sealed); Eze 32:27 (bodily deposit — on bones); Exo 20:5 (generational deposit). Contradicting or complicating: Jer 50:20 — "iniquity shall be sought in Israel, and there shall be none" — the divine record is fully erasable through pardon; Zec 3:9 — "I will remove the iniquity of this land in a single day" — the accumulated deposit is removable by divine sovereign act; Eze 18:20 — the father's iniquity-deposit does not automatically transfer to the son (the Eze 18 personal-accountability register contradicts the simple generational transfer of Exo 20:5 at the level of punishable liability). The deposit is real but divinely removable.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Supporting: Amos 1:3 (divine count-record); Isa 48:8 (identity deposit); Lam 1:14 (yoke-burden deposit). Contradicting or complicating: Isa 43:25 — "I will not remember your sins" — the divine-count deposit is erasable by God's sovereign choice; Psa 103:12 — "as far as the east is from the west, so far does he remove our transgressions from us" — the deposit is completely removable; Eze 18:22 — "none of the transgressions he has committed shall be remembered against him" — the accumulated record can be rendered null. The deposit is real and persistent but divinely erasable.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Supporting: 2Ch 30:7 (generational deposit — desolation of fathers); Isa 48:8 (identity-level foreknown deposit); Dan 9:7 (national shame deposit). Contradicting or complicating: Lev 26:40-42 — "if they confess their iniquity and... treachery... I will remember my covenant" — the deposit is reversible through confession; Eze 39:26 — "they shall forget their shame and all the treachery" in the eschatological secure-dwelling — the deposit is fully resolved in restoration. The deposit is real and constitutionally significant but reversible through divine covenant-remembrance.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Supporting: 1Ti 6:5 (mind-depravity deposit — constitutionally settled); Eph 4:22 (ongoing desire-corruption deposit); Rom 8:21 (bondage-to-corruption). Contradicting or complicating: Eph 4:22-24 — the corrupt old self is to be "put off" — the deposit is addressable through the deliberate renewal act; 2Pe 1:4 — "having escaped from the corruption" — the deposit is escapable through participation in divine nature. The deposit is constitutionally real but not irreversible: it requires a counter-action at the same constitutional level (renewal of the mind — Eph 4:23; participation in divine nature — 2Pe 1:4).

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Supporting: Rev 18:5 (divine memory-deposit); Luk 16:10 (fixed character); Zep 3:5 (shameless conscience). Contradicting or complicating: Job 34:32 — "if I have done iniquity, I will do it no more" — the deposit is addressable through volitional repudiation; Eze 33:15 — "the wicked restores the pledge... not doing injustice, he shall surely live" — even the wicked person's injustice-deposit can be reversed through restoration and volitional change. The fixed-character deposit (Luk 16:10) is the most resistant — consistent dishonesty at all scales — but even this is not declared eschatologically irreversible until judgment.

---

### T2.8.3

**Question:** If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly. This finding feeds directly into T5.7.

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The evidence is not wholly silent but is limited (T2.8.1 and T2.8.2). The corpus suggests generational moral consequence (Isa 1:4) and disposition-formation (Hos 4:7; 13:2) without explicit constitutional-deposit or biological mechanism language. T5.7 will carry this as a limited evidential finding. Note: the carry-forward INTEGRATION_NOTEs (a.ven and BOUNDARY terms) are not evidenced in the CHAR-1 corpus — both are set-aside terms with no CHAR-1 verse presence.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(S)*

**[CHAR-2]** S — The evidence is silent on constitutional deposit. This finding closes T5.7: since T2.8 finds no deposit evidence, T5.7.1 and T5.7.2 will be closed accordingly.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(S)*

**[CHAR-3]** S — The evidence is silent on constitutional deposit from confession. T5.7 will be closed accordingly: no deposit, no developmental or generational consequence to report from this corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Deposit evidence is present (Tit 3:11 — constitutional warping; Ecc 8:12 — habituated formation). T5.7 will carry this as a limited but real deposit finding: sustained conscience suppression produces constitutional character deformation ("warped") as its developmental consequence.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Deposit evidence is present: formational-constitutional hardening (Neh 9:29); active attachment (2Ki 3:3); lifetime orientation (2Ki 15:18); generational social transmission (2Ki 15:9 — "as his fathers"). T5.7 will carry: deposit is formational-constitutional and social-generational, not biological.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Deposit evidence is present: individual constitutional hardening (Exo 9:34), social-institutional embedding (Hos 8:11), generational transmission (Hos 10:9). T5.7 will carry: deposit is multi-dimensional (individual, institutional, generational) and real but potentially broken by the abiding relationship.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Deposit evidence is present and exceptional: physical-structural institutional deposit (2Ki 23:15 — altar at Bethel); generational social deposit (1Ki 22:52 — three-generation pattern); community moral-directional deposit (2Ki 21:11 — Judah's corporate sinning orientation shaped by Manasseh). T5.7 will carry: the most multi-dimensional deposit evidence in the cluster, with a physical-structural component unique to CHAR-7.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Deposit evidence is present: political-relational fractures that persist "to this day" (1Ki 12:19; 2Ki 8:22; 2Ch 10:19; 2Ch 21:10). T5.7 will carry: the deposit is political-structural (permanent fracture in governing relationships) rather than bodily-constitutional.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Deposit evidence is present: character-formation deposit (2Ti 3:2; 1Ti 6:4), irreversible Spirit-blasphemy deposit (Mat 12:31), constitutive-identity deposit (VCG-03 beast). T5.7 will carry: the deposit is primarily character-forming and potentially irreversible in the unforgivable form; the beast-form is the extreme endpoint.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Deposit evidence is present for enticement: "hearts trained in greed" (2Pe 2:14) as formed constitutional character. For hypocrisy (Gal 2:13) and apostasy (Act 21:21), the corpus is silent on explicit constitutional deposit. T5.7 will carry: the enticement deposit is the trained-greed character; the hypocrisy and apostasy deposits are silent in the corpus.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Deposit evidence is the most extensive in M10: four dimensions (death, hardening, indwelling, accumulating measure). T5.7 will carry: the deposit is multi-dimensional, deeply constitutional (indwelling — Rom 7:17; bodily mortality — Rom 8:10), and ultimately eschatologically consequential (accumulating toward judgment — 1Th 2:16). Complicating factor: Christ's sinlessness demonstrates the deposit is fallen-not-created.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Deposit evidence is present: slave-identity (Joh 8:34), devil-allegiance (1Jo 3:8), death-trajectory (1Jo 5:16). Counter-deposit: God's-seed-abiding (1Jo 3:9). T5.7 will carry: the deposit is constitutional (slave-identity, devil-allegiance) and eschatological (death); the counter-deposit is the new birth's God-seed constitution.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Deposit evidence is the most extensive in M10: heart-engraving (Jer 17:1), relational separation (Isa 59:2), institutional legacy (VCG-04), stored divine record (Hos 13:12). T5.7 will carry: the heart-engraving deposit is permanent without divine action; the institutional legacy deposit spans generations; the divine-record deposit awaits eschatological reckoning; the deposit can be addressed by divine erasure (Isa 43:25; Jer 31:34; Eze 33:16) but not by human effort alone.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Deposit evidence is present in the positive direction: love (Luk 7:47), life (Col 2:13), Spirit (Act 2:38), redemption identity (Col 1:14; Eph 1:7). T5.7 will carry: the deposits are all positive; the OT deposits are provisional (annual renewal required); the NT deposits are permanent (present-tense possession — "we have redemption").

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Deposit evidence is present: prolonged sin-condition (Isa 64:5) and defilement (Eze 37:23). T5.7 will carry: the deposit is corporate-temporal (long duration) and spiritual-defiling; the deposit is addressable through divine cleansing (Eze 37:23) and not constitutionally irremovable.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Deposit evidence is present: constituted Adamic standing (Rom 5:19), accumulated sins (Jam 5:20), heart-defilement (Jam 4:8). T5.7 will carry: all three deposits are reversible through repentance/Christ's saving mission (Luk 15:7; 1Ti 1:15), but real and constitutionally located in the meantime.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Deposit evidence is present: accumulated weight (Ezr 9:6), indelible stain (Jer 2:22), intergenerational transmission (Jer 32:18). T5.7 will carry: the deposits are reversible through divine cleansing (Isa 6:7; Jer 33:8) but real and accumulating without it; the intergenerational deposit is the most severe form, reaching beyond the individual's lifetime.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Deposit evidence is extensive: divine-record (Hos 13:12), bodily (Eze 32:27), generational (Exo 20:5). T5.7 will carry: all three deposit-forms are divinely removable (Jer 50:20; Zec 3:9; Jer 31:34) but constitute real accumulated moral-crime burdens until removed; the Eze 18:20 personal-accountability principle sets limits on the generational deposit's punishable transmission.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Deposit evidence is present: divine-count record (Amos 1:3; Dan 9:24), identity-level labelling (Isa 48:8; Isa 57:4), yoke-burden (Lam 1:14). T5.7 will carry: all deposit forms are divinely erasable (Isa 43:25; Psa 103:12; Eze 18:22) but real and persistent until erased; the identity-deposit (Isa 48:8 — "from before birth") is the most deeply-rooted and the hardest to address through human effort.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Deposit evidence present: generational communal (2Ch 30:7), identity-level foreknown (Isa 48:8), national shame (Dan 9:7). T5.7 will carry: all deposit forms yield to covenant-renewal (Lev 26:40-42 — confession → covenant-remembrance) and eschatological resolution (Eze 39:26 — shame forgotten in secure dwelling). The identity-level deposit (Isa 48:8) is the most deeply constitutionally embedded.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Deposit evidence is present: mind-depravity (1Ti 6:5), desire-corruption (Eph 4:22; 2Pe 2:19), bodily bondage (Rom 8:21). T5.7 will carry: all deposit forms are addressed through Spirit-level renewal (Eph 4:23 — "renewed in the spirit of your minds"; 2Pe 1:4 — divine nature participation; Gal 6:8 — Spirit-sowing). The desire-capture deposit is the most analytically significant — "corrupt through deceitful desires" names the mechanism precisely.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Deposit evidence is present: divine memory (Rev 18:5), fixed character (Luk 16:10), shameless conscience (Zep 3:5). T5.7 will carry: the divine memory deposit (Rev 18:5) develops toward eschatological judgment; the fixed character deposit (Luk 16:10) develops toward either volitional reversal or eschatological exclusion from the kingdom (1Cor 6:9); the shameless conscience deposit (Zep 3:5) is the most constitutionally embedded and the hardest to reverse.

---

## T2.9 — Origin and Source

### T2.9.1

**Question:** Where does this characteristic originate constitutionally — is it generated from within the person, received from outside, bestowed by God, or carried generationally?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The origin evidence is multi-sourced. (1) *Internal — from within the will and heart*: Gen 39:9 (Joseph's description of the temptation as something he recognises as "great wickedness" — the sinful act originates in the responding will); Job 1:5 (sinning "in their hearts" — heart as origin site). (2) *External — received through temptation, pressure, or exposure*: 1Sa 15:24 ("I feared the people") — social pressure as external origin; Neh 13:26 (foreign women — relational exposure as origin); Neh 6:13 (enemies' trap — external manipulative pressure). (3) *Constitutional vulnerability in the creature*: 1Jo 1:10 ("if we say we have not sinned, we make him a liar") treats sinning as a condition from which no human is exempt — implying a constitutional susceptibility.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Unintentional sinning originates primarily from *creaturely epistemic limitation* — the person acts without the knowledge required to recognise the act as prohibited. Lev 4:2 ("sins unintentionally in any of the Lord's commandments about things not to be done") — origin is in the gap between the person's knowledge and the law's requirement. Num 22:34 ("I did not know that you stood in the road against me") — origin is in perceptual limitation (the angel was unseen). 1Sa 14:33/34 (eating with blood in battle urgency) — origin is in situational distraction overriding proper ritual care. The origin is thus: limited knowledge + limited perception + situational pressure = the conditions that produce inadvertent violation.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Confession originates primarily from the *heart/conscience*: 2Sa 24:10 — "David's heart struck him" — the heart as the origin-site of the confessional impulse. Secondary origins: (1) *Inner knowledge*: 2Sa 19:20 — "your servant knows that I have sinned" — conscience-as-knowledge as the originating faculty; (2) *External judgment*: Exo 9:27/10:16 (Pharaoh — plague), Num 21:7 (serpents), 1Sa 26:21 (David's mercy) — external events triggering recognition. (3) *Extended communal process*: Neh 1:6 — Nehemiah's sustained confession arises from his identification with his people's sin, not from personal guilt alone — a form of solidarity-origin. The primary origin is inner (heart/conscience); external events can trigger but do not substitute for inner conscience-origin in genuine confession.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Multiple constitutional origins are evidenced. (1) *From within — self-interested will*: Jer 2:35 — the person actively claims innocence from self-interest ("surely his anger has turned from me" — the desire to believe divine anger has passed). (2) *From within — habituated absence*: Ecc 8:12 — repeated sinning without the fear of God producing habituated conscience-absence. (3) *From epistemic deficit*: 1Cor 15:34 — "no knowledge of God" — the absence of God-knowledge as a cognitive origin. (4) *From generational or communal formation*: Jer 16:10 — the people's collective failure to recognise sin suggests a generational/communal formation process in which the moral self-awareness of a whole community has been degraded.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Multiple constitutional origins: (1) *Inherited moral orientation received by non-rejection*: 2Ki 15:9 — "as his fathers had done. He did not depart from the sins of Jeroboam" — the inherited sin-pattern is the origin, received by each king's non-rejection constituting implicit consent. (2) *Heart's incomplete alignment*: 2Ki 10:31 — "not with all his heart" — the divided heart that does not give full commitment to God is the inner origin of the partial-refusal. (3) *Minimisation of sin's gravity*: 1Ki 16:31 — "as if it had been a light thing" — cognitive minimisation as an origin-condition. (4) *Deliberate choice after knowledge*: Heb 10:26 — the will choosing to continue sinning despite knowing the truth.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Multiple constitutional origins: (1) *Individual psychological cycling*: Exo 9:34 — the plague-relief-resumption cycle; the origin is the internal pressure-responsiveness of the will that reverts to sinning when external pressure is removed. (2) *Communal/historical inheritance*: Hos 10:9 — "from the days of Gibeah, you have sinned"; 2Ki 17:7 — Israel's communal pattern; the origin is in received communal practices and orientations. (3) *Religious misdirection*: Hos 8:11 — altars that became sinning-producers; the origin includes religiously institutionalised sinning. (4) *Absence of God-pleasing disposition*: Ecc 7:26 — the sinner who lacks the inner God-orientation that would enable escape; the origin is in the absence of the positive disposition that would prevent the habitual pattern.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The origin is the leader's personal inner will committed to the sinning course. 1Ki 16:26 — "walked in all the way of Jeroboam" — Jeroboam's personal volitional walking in the sinning direction is the source. 1Ki 16:2 — "you have walked in the way of Jeroboam" — the king's personal walking precedes the causative ("and have made my people Israel to sin"). The origin is in the individual leader's personal inner commitment: without the leader's own sinning, the transmission cannot occur. The secondary origin is in the authority position that amplifies the personal sinning into communal transmission.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Two constitutional origins are evidenced. (1) *External opportunity trigger*: 2Ki 1:1 / 3:5 — Moab's revolts originate when the governing authority is perceived as weakened (Ahab's death). The origin is in the political calculation of the revolting party assessing the governing authority's vulnerability. (2) *Inner spiritual abandonment of the governing authority*: 2Ch 21:10 — the origin is in Jehoram's forsaking of the Lord, which creates a spiritual-authority vacuum that enables revolt. The two origins represent different causal pathways: external political calculation vs the consequence of the governing authority's inner spiritual condition.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The primary constitutional origin is the *heart*: Mat 15:19 — "out of the heart come evil thoughts... slander" — the heart is the named origin. Secondary origins: (1) *Conceit and diseased appetite*: 1Ti 6:4 — sinful speech originates from the pride-inflated will and its craving; (2) *Unbelief*: 1Ti 1:13 — Paul's blasphemy from "ignorant unbelief" — epistemic-spiritual ignorance as origin; (3) *Total anti-God orientation*: VCG-03 — the beast's blasphemy originates from the creature's constitutive defiance, not from a triggering moment.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Distinct constitutional origins by mechanism. (1) *Enticement*: Jam 1:14 — "his own desire" — the desire-faculty within the person is the constitutional origin; the enticement is not externally imposed but exploits what is already within the person. (2) *Hypocrisy*: Gal 2:13 — the origin is in the social-conformity pressure of the group; the constitutional entry point is the social-identity capacity that prioritises peer acceptance over authentic identity. (3) *Apostasy*: Act 21:21 — the origin is in the will's departure decision; the constitutional origin is the volitional faculty choosing to stand away from the covenantal commitment.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The origin is explicitly addressed: Rom 5:12 — "sin came into the world through one man" — the constitutional origin of the universal condition is federal/representational: through Adam as the representative head of humanity, the condition entered and spread universally. The entry was cosmic and positional, not individually generated by each person: the condition is received by birth (Joh 9:34 — "born in utter sin") rather than acquired through individual accumulation of acts. The condition is thus the constitutional starting-point of every human person's existence, not its endpoint.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Two constitutional origins. (1) *Practice-generated*: Joh 8:34 — "everyone who practices sin is a slave to sin" — the enslaving power is generated within the individual through the accumulation of sinning practices; the origin is in the person's own practice of sinning. (2) *Spirit-level adversarial*: 1Jo 3:8 — "the devil has been sinning from the beginning" — the enslaving power's ultimate origin is in the devil's originary sinning; the devil's sin from the beginning is the constitutional source of the enslaving power that individuals fall into through practice.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Multiple constitutional origins. (1) *From the heart's unworthy thoughts*: Deu 15:9 — "an unworthy thought in your heart" — the record originates in the heart's inner disposition before any outer act; (2) *From the will's sinning acts*: chat.tat (VCG-05) — the committed act (Lev 4:23 — "the sin which he has committed") creates the record entry; (3) *From inherited birth-condition*: Psa 51:5 — "in sin did my mother conceive me" — the record-bearing condition is received at birth, prior to any individual act; (4) *From corporate-representational transmission*: VCG-04 — Jeroboam's sin becomes Israel's recorded inheritance through the king's representational role.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Two constitutional origins. (1) *From conscience recognition*: Lev 4:14 — "when the sin which they have committed becomes known" — the seeking begins in the conscience's recognition of committed sin; (2) *From God's provision of the means*: Exo 29:36 — the daily sin offering is God-instituted; Lev 23:27 — the Day of Atonement is God-appointed. The characteristic cannot originate in the person alone: God must first establish the means (the sacrificial system; Christ's blood) before the seeking can become effective. The origin is thus both from within the person (conscience recognition triggering seeking) and from God's prior provision (establishing the means without which the seeking would be empty).

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Isa 43:27 — "your first father sinned" — the constitutional origin is in the first father's volitional sinning act. This is the explicit ancestral origin of the generational condition: the "first father" is the founding-originator whose sinning created the initial entry-point. The mediators' subsequent transgression (Isa 43:27 — "and your mediators transgressed against me") confirms that the condition was reinforced at each stage of institutional leadership, deepening what the first father began.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Two constitutional origins. (1) *Federal imputation*: Rom 5:19 — "by the one man's disobedience the many were made sinners" — the sinner-identity is constituted through Adam's representative act; the origin is external to the individual and prior to their individual sinning acts; (2) *Individual habitual formation*: Gen 13:13 — the men of Sodom "were wicked, great sinners against the Lord" — the extreme-sinner identity is constituted through accumulated individual sinning acts that have formed the person's total moral character.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Two constitutional origins. (1) *From an act that violates divine or moral standard*: Lev 5:2/3/4 — the specific acts (touching unclean thing, rash oath) that generate guilt when they become known; Lev 5:19 — "he has indeed incurred guilt before the Lord" — the act of commission creates the guilt; (2) *From accumulated inherited community condition*: Ezr 9:7 — "from the days of our fathers to this day we have been in great guilt" — the inherited communal accumulation is an origin prior to the individual's own acts. The constitutional origin thus operates at both the individual-act level and the inherited-community level.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Two constitutional origins. (1) *Heart-level willful choice*: Eze 14:3 — "taken their idols into their hearts" — the iniquity originates in the will's inner choice to embrace what God forbids; Job 31:33 — hiding iniquity in the heart is a deliberate act; (2) *Inherited constitutional condition*: Psa 51:5 — "I was brought forth in iniquity, and in sin did my mother conceive me" — the iniquity-condition precedes any individual act of will; it characterises the womb-context of human existence. Both origins operate: VCG-08 (heart-seated) names the willful-choice origin; Psa 51:5 names the pre-personal constitutional origin.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Two constitutional origins. (1) *Heart-level volitional choice*: Psa 36:1 — "transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart" — the heart is the named origin of the inner-voice that drives transgression; Isa 59:13 — "conceiving and uttering from the heart" — the conception is in the heart; (2) *Adamic inheritance*: Rom 5:15/16/17/18/20 (VCG-05 paraptōma) — "one man's trespass" entered condemnation for all; Isa 48:8 — "from before birth you were called a rebel" — the rebel-identity precedes personal choice; Isa 57:4 — "children of transgression" — inherited from parents. Both origins operate simultaneously: constitutional Adamic inheritance and individual volitional heart-choice.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Two constitutional origins. (1) *Spirit-level inner disposition*: Mal 2:15 — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and do not be faithless" — the spirit is the named origin that requires guarding; the faithlessness arises from within the spirit when not actively resisted; (2) *Pride as the triggering condition*: 2Ch 26:16 — "when he was strong, he grew proud, to his destruction. For he was unfaithful to the Lord his God" — pride in the heart is the originating inner condition that produces the outward faithlessness; the pride precedes and generates the unfaithfulness.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Three constitutional origins. (1) *Heart-level dispositional orientation*: Pro 6:14 — "with perverted heart" — the heart as the primary origin-faculty; (2) *Desire-faculty corruption*: Eph 4:22 — "corrupt through deceitful desires" — the desire-faculty is the active mechanism of corruption in the old self; 2Pe 1:4 — "corruption... because of sinful desire" — sinful desire as the world-corruption's origin; (3) *Instinctual unreasoning nature*: Jude 10 — "like unreasoning animals... understand instinctively" — the unreasoning instinct as the originating mode of the most extreme corruption.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Two constitutional origins. (1) *Heart-level God-denial and devising*: Psa 53:1 — "the fool says in his heart, 'There is no God'" — the heart's atheism as origin; Psa 58:2 — "in your hearts you devise wrongs" — the heart's deliberating function as origin; (2) *Self-trust displacing God-trust*: Hos 10:13 — "you have plowed iniquity... because you have trusted in your own way" — the misplaced self-reliance as the originating disposition.

---

### T2.9.2

**Question:** What does the evidence reveal about whether the origin is singular or multiple?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The origin is clearly multiple in the corpus. No single origin-source is evidenced as exhaustive. The corpus presents internal origins (will, heart, conscience-bypassed) and external origins (social pressure, temptation, exposure) operating alongside each other. Neh 6:13 (external trap) and 1Sa 15:24 (external pressure) show sinning arising from a combination of external pressure and internal capitulation of the will. Gen 39:9 shows sinning arising purely from internal temptation (Potiphar's wife's offer) met by internal resistance — external trigger, internal response. The multiplicity of origins supports reading wilful sinning as a relational phenomenon (always involving a setting, a pressure, and a will) rather than a purely internal generation.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The origin is multiple. No single cause is evidenced as exhaustive. The corpus presents: epistemic limitation as an inner origin (not knowing the prohibition, Lev 4:2), perceptual limitation as an inner origin (not seeing the morally relevant fact, Num 22:34), and situational pressure as an external-contextual origin (urgency of battle, 1Sa 14:33/34). The multiplicity reflects the variety of ways in which the gap between available knowledge and moral requirement can arise — through ignorance, through limited perception, and through situational distraction.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The origin is multiple. Conscience (2Sa 24:10), knowledge (2Sa 19:20), external judgment-pressure (Exo 9:27), intercessory solidarity (Neh 1:6), and communal recognition (VCG-02 corporate confessions — Judg 10:10; 1Sa 7:6) all appear as originating conditions. The multiplicity confirms that confession is not generated by a single faculty but by a convergence of inner conscience, situational pressure, relational orientation, and communal solidarity. What distinguishes genuine from hollow confession is which of these origins dominates: when inner conscience dominates (2Sa 24:10; Luk 15:18), the confession is genuine; when external pressure alone drives it (Exo 9:27/10:16 — Pharaoh) without inner conscience-origin, the hollow form results.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The origin is clearly multiple. Active denial (Jer 2:35) originates from the will's self-interested claim. Perceptual blindness (Jer 16:10) originates from communal-formational degeneration. Habituated absence (Ecc 8:12) originates from repeated sinning over time. Epistemic suppression (1Cor 15:34) originates from ignorance of God. The three modes of the characteristic (active denial, perceptual blindness, habituated absence) each have a distinct origin, sharing only the common outcome: conscience not performing its moral-witness function.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The origin is multiple. Inherited moral legacy (Jeroboam-pattern), divided heart (2Ki 10:31), cognitive minimisation (1Ki 16:31), and deliberate post-knowledge choice (Heb 10:26) all contribute to the origin in different instances. The Kings corpus shows inherited legacy as the dominant origin; Neh 9:29 shows communal formation; Heb 10:26 shows individual deliberate choice. The characteristic's diverse origins reflect its wide evidential base.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The origin is clearly multiple. Individual psychological cycling (Exo 9:34), communal inheritance (Hos 10:9; 2Ki 17:7), institutional misdirection (Hos 8:11), and dispositional absence (Ecc 7:26) all appear as distinct originating conditions. The multiplicity confirms that habitual defection can arise from several different starting points, all of which converge in the same outcome: the will's settled direction toward sin.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The origin is effectively dual: (1) the leader's personal inner sinful commitment (constitutional source), and (2) the authority position that makes the transmission possible (structural enabler). Neither alone constitutes contagious sin: personal sinning without authority produces CHAR-1/5/6; authority without sinful inner commitment does not transmit sin. The two must combine. The Kings corpus shows a third contributing origin: the received sinning pattern from prior leaders (1Ki 22:52 — following father, mother, and Jeroboam) — the leader's own sinful commitment is often itself a received pattern.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The origin is multiple. Opportunity-based origin (2Ki 1:1; 3:5), spiritually-grounded authority vacuum (2Ch 21:10), and unexplained decisive break (1Ki 12:19 — Israel's revolt from Davidic house in the Rehoboam context) represent distinct originating conditions. What is common across all: the presence of an established governing relationship that is broken by a decisive volitional act.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Multiple. Heart-corruption (Mat 15:19), conceit/craving (1Ti 6:4), unbelief (1Ti 1:13), and constitutive anti-God orientation (VCG-03) are distinct originating conditions across the corpus. The common element: all originate from an inner moral condition rather than from external triggers. The characteristic is generated from within; external provocations may occasion sinful speech but do not constitute its origin.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Multiple — with distinct origins for each mechanism. The composite nature of the characteristic (three mechanisms) produces necessarily multiple constitutional origins: desire-faculty (enticement), social-conformity pressure (hypocrisy), will's departure (apostasy). No single constitutional origin covers all three.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The origin is singular at its source (one man — Rom 5:12) but universal in its reach ("death spread to all men" — Rom 5:12; "all have sinned" — Rom 3:23). The singular origin (Adam) generates the universal condition. Rom 5:16 — "the judgment following one trespass brought condemnation" — one act at the origin produced a universal judicial standing (condemnation) for all. The singularity of the origin is what makes the condition's universality intelligible: it is not that each person originates their own sin-condition from scratch but that all share in the one origin's consequence.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Multiple. Individual practice (Joh 8:34 — the person's own sinning practice) and the devil's originary sinning (1Jo 3:8 — primordial spiritual source) are distinct constitutional origins. The individual practice is the proximate origin of each person's enslavement; the devil's originary sinning is the ultimate origin of the enslaving power that the individual's practice aligns with. The two origins work together: the individual's practice is what aligns them with and comes under the devil's originary sin-power.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Multiple — and constitutively so. The 205-verse corpus explicitly demonstrates at least four distinct constitutional origins (heart's thought, will's act, birth-condition, corporate transmission — T2.9.1). No single origin covers all 205 verses: chet (VCG-01) emphasises personal-liability origin; Psa 51:5 emphasises birth-condition origin; VCG-04 emphasises corporate-representational origin; VCG-05's broad chat.tat corpus emphasises the act-origin. The characteristic's scope is precisely its multi-originary nature.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Multiple — and structurally so. The seeking dimension originates in conscience recognition (Lev 4:14) and volitional turning (Act 2:38 — repent). The receiving dimension originates in God's provision of the atonement-mechanism (Exo 29:36 — God's daily sin-offering institution; Mat 26:28 — Christ's blood). These multiple origins reflect the characteristic's bi-directional structure: the seeking originates in the person; the receiving originates in God.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Both — a singular founding origin with multiple subsequent reinforcing origins. Isa 43:27 — "your first father sinned" — singular founding origin; "and your mediators transgressed against me" — multiple subsequent institutional transgressors who deepened and extended the condition. The origin is thus singular in its founding moment (first father) but multiplied through subsequent generations of leaders and communities who continued the pattern.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Multiple — and the multiplicity is analytically significant. The federal imputation origin (Rom 5:19 — Adam's one act) is singular in its initiating moment; the habitual-formation origin (Gen 13:13 — sustained extreme sinning) requires multiple acts over time. The characteristic thus has both a singular federal origin (applying to all through Adam) and a multiple individual origin (applying to the extreme sinner-type through accumulated formation). These are not competing origins but different levels of the same constitutional reality.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Multiple — and the multiplicity across five VCGs is the corpus's richest inter-origin complexity. Individual unintentional acts (VCG-01 — Lev 4/5 sequences), communal accumulation across generations (VCG-02 — Ezr 9:7), guilt loaded onto a representative bearer (VCG-03 — Exo 28:38), punitive inheritance from ancestors (VCG-04 — Gen 19:15), and indelibility before divine memory (VCG-05 — Jer 2:22; Eze 21:23/24) are all distinct guilt-origins operating simultaneously in the 97-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Multiple — and the multiplicity across eight VCGs represents the greatest origin-complexity in M10. Individual willful acts (VCG-04 — Eze 18:20 — personal crime), heart-originated allegiance (VCG-08 — Eze 14:3), inherited pre-personal condition (Psa 51:5), generational transmission (VCG-02 — Exo 20:5), cultic failure (VCG-01 — Lev 5:1/17), and communal accumulation (VCG-05 — Ezr 9:6) are all distinct iniquity-origins operating simultaneously across the 162-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Multiple — nine VCG registers name different originating contexts. Individual volitional choice (VCG-01 — Isa 1:2 — "they have rebelled"), Adamic inheritance (VCG-05 — Rom 5:15/16), heart-level inner voice (VCG-09 — Psa 36:1), inherited national identity (VCG-03 — Amos — nations whose transgression is counted), deceptive persuasion (VCG-04 — 1Ti 2:14 — Eve deceived), and revolt-speech (VCG-02 — Jer 28:16 — false prophecy as revolt). The characteristic has the most diverse origin-set of any M10 characteristic studied, covering individual, communal, inherited, coerced, and heart-generated origins.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Multiple — the three VCGs name distinct originating contexts. Spirit-level disposition (Mal 2:15 — VCG-03); pride-generated (2Ch 26:16 — VCG-01 Uzziah); allegiance-transfer (1Ch 5:25 — transferring loyalty to false gods — VCG-01); lust-captivity (Pro 11:6 — lust capturing the will — VCG-02); unguarded spirit (Mal 2:15 — VCG-02 marital). The characteristic has multiple originating pathways: all share the spirit-level as the constitutional location but reach that location through different triggering conditions (pride, misplaced desire, unguarded spirit).

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Multiple — across five VCG registers. Heart-origin (VCG-01/03 — Pro 6:14); desire-origin (VCG-05 — Eph 4:22; 2Pe 1:4); instinct-origin (VCG-05 — Jude 10); bribery-triggered cognitive corruption (VCG-02 — Exo 23:8); created-order violation (VCG-04 — Lev 18:23 — te.vel). CHAR-21 has the most diverse origin-set of any M10 characteristic studied in terms of the different inner faculties named as origin-points (heart, desire, instinct) plus external triggering conditions (bribery, bad company — 1Cor 15:33).

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Multiple across the three VCG registers. Heart-devising (VCG-02 — Psa 58:2/64:6); God-denial (VCG-01/03 — Psa 53:1; Job 18:21); self-trust (VCG-02 — Hos 10:13); material inducement (VCG-01 — 2Ch 19:7 — bribery); emergence from within a blameless being (Eze 28:15 — the cherub's internal emergence). CHAR-22 has diverse origins but all share the will-level as the constitutional location of the departure from right conduct.

---

### T2.9.3

**Question:** Does the origin of this characteristic change across different contexts evidenced in Scripture?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Yes. The OT corpus (VCG-01) predominantly shows sinning arising in covenantal contexts — Israel sinning against the Lord by failing to walk in his ways (Jer 44:23), breaking covenant (Jos 7:11), or following idolatrous influences (Hos 4:7; 13:2). The origin-context is covenantal relationship with God. The interpersonal corpus (VCG-02) shows sinning arising in relational contexts where obligations between persons are present — custody obligations (Gen 43:9/44:32), leader-servant relations (1Sa 19:4/5), sibling bonds (Gen 42:22). The NT corpus (VCG-05) shows sinning arising in the body-context (1Cor 6:18) and the community-context (Mat 18:15; Luk 17:3/4; 1Cor 8:12). The origin-context shifts from covenantal (OT) to anthropological and communal (NT) without changing the core — the will's known choice of wrong.

---

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Yes. The origin differs across the two VCG registers. In VCG-01 (moral-unintentional), the origin is within the person's epistemic and perceptual constitution: the knowledge-gap between what the person knew and what the law required. In VCG-02 (cultic-purification), the "origin" is not in a person at all — the sacred object (altar, sanctuary) accumulates defilement from the activities of a sinful community; the origin is environmental/communal rather than individual-epistemic. This contextual shift confirms that VCG-02 is a distinct register: its origin-mechanism is entirely different from VCG-01's personal knowledge-gap.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Yes. Individual confession (VCG-01) originates primarily in personal conscience (2Sa 24:10; 1Ch 21:8) or external judgment triggering personal recognition (Exo 9:27; Num 21:7). Corporate confession (VCG-02) originates in communal recognition of shared moral failure — Judg 10:10 ("we have forsaken our God"), 1Sa 7:6 (fasting and confessing together), Jer 3:25 ("from our youth even to this day, we and our fathers"). Daniel's confession (Dan 9:5) crosses the individual-communal boundary: an individual confessing on behalf of a community he identifies with. The origin-context shifts from personal conscience (individual) to communal recognition (corporate) without changing the fundamental structure: sin named as sin before God.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Yes. In the Jeremiah covenantal context (Jer 2:35; 16:10), conscience suppression originates from corporate Israel's history of accumulated unfaithfulness producing first active denial and then genuine self-blindness. In the Ecclesiastes wisdom context (Ecc 2:26; 8:12), it originates from the absence of the God-orientation that gives moral clarity. In the NT community context (1Cor 15:34; Tit 3:11), it originates from spiritual stupor and divisive character formation within the community of faith. The origin shifts contextually but in each case involves some failure of the God-ward orientation that keeps the conscience active.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — Yes. In the Kings covenantal-political context, the origin is primarily inherited legacy — each king who "did not depart from the sins of Jeroboam" inherited a formed religious-political pattern and chose to continue it. In the Neh 9:29 communal prayer context, the origin is communal formation across generations — a community's shared refusal. In the Heb 10:26 NT context, the origin is individual deliberate choice after receiving knowledge of truth — the most personally accountable origin. In Eze 18:24 / 33:12, the origin is an individual formerly-righteous person's personal decision to turn toward sinning and remain in it. The origin varies across contexts from inherited-legacy to communal-formation to individual deliberate choice.

---

  2. Scope marker:       31× [CHAR-5] ✓

  → PASS. Proceeding to Tier T3.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Yes. The individual psychological origin (Exo 9:34 — Pharaoh's hardening cycle) differs from the communal origin (2Ki 17:7; Hos 10:9 — national/historical patterns). The institutional origin (Hos 8:11 — altars) differs from the dispositional-absence origin (Ecc 7:26 — lacking the God-pleasing inner disposition). The NT context (1Jo 3:6) presents habitual defection's origin as the absence of the abiding relationship with Christ — a specifically new-covenant framing of the origin that the OT instances imply but do not name in these terms.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Yes. In the pre-Canaan entry context (Exo 23:33; Deu 20:18), the origin is in foreign nations through cultural-religious proximity and teaching — not monarchic authority but proximity-influence. In the monarchic context (Kings corpus), the origin is in royal authority and the Jeroboam-pattern inheritance. In Jer 32:35, the origin is in specific religious leadership (those who "built the high places of Baal") — a priestly/religious authority context. The common element across contexts is always an authority or influence relationship; the specific form of authority (cultural proximity, royal, religious) varies.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Yes. Moab's revolts (2Ki 1:1; 3:5) originate in political opportunism after leadership change. Edom's and Libnah's revolts (2Ch 21:8/10) originate in the governing authority's spiritual condition. Israel's revolt (1Ki 12:19; 2Ch 10:19) originates in the covenant-historical context of Rehoboam's harsh governance (implied by the broader 1Ki 12 narrative). The context shapes the specific originating condition; the common element is the volitional act of breaking submission when the conditions enable it.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — Yes. In the personal-relational community context (VCG-01), sinful speech originates from inner corruptions of pride, craving, and heart-corruption (1Ti 6:4; Mat 15:19). In the christological-judicial context (VCG-02), blasphemy originates from a false theological framework (the religious authorities do not recognise who Jesus is — their blasphemy-charge is itself an expression of theological misidentification). In the eschatological-cosmic context (VCG-03), blasphemy originates from the creature's constitutive anti-God orientation — no triggering moment, just total defiance as the nature.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Yes. For apostasy: the origin is in the relational-cultural context of the Gentile mission challenging the Jewish-covenantal framework (Act 21:21).

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The constitutional origin (Adam — Rom 5:12) is constant across all contexts. However, the *activation* of the condition varies across contexts: Rom 7:9 — "when the commandment came, sin came alive" — the condition, already present, is activated by the law's arrival; Joh 15:22/24 — Jesus's coming removes excuse, making the condition's accountability fully operative; Joh 16:9 — the Spirit convicts specifically regarding unbelief as the form of the condition in the gospel-context. The origin is singular (Adam) but the condition's experienced form and accountability differ depending on whether one has the law, has heard the gospel, or has encountered Jesus's works.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Yes. In the individual-practice context (Joh 8:34), the origin is in the person's own sinning acts accumulating into slavery. In the universal-structural context (Gal 3:22 — "the Scripture imprisoned everything under sin"), the origin is not individual practice but a structural declaration by Scripture itself. In the adversarial-spiritual context (1Jo 3:8/9), the origin is in the devil's primordial sinning from which the enslaving power flows. The three contexts name different originating dimensions of the same enslaving power.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes. In the individual moral context: the origin is in the person's own act or thought (Deu 15:9 — heart's thought → sin; Lev 4:23 — committed act). In the prophetic-national context: the origin is corporate — Jeroboam's sin becomes Israel's inherited record (VCG-04 — 46 verses). In the priestly-liturgical context (Lev 4-5; 16:21 — Day of Atonement): the origin presupposes already-accumulated record requiring priestly mediation. In the Job-surveillance context (VCG-03): the origin is scrutinised by God — Job can neither identify nor quantity his record without divine disclosure.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Yes. Isa 43:27 traces the origin to the first father (the founding individual transgressor). Psa 78:17/32 traces the origin of the specific desert-generation pattern to their own willful rebellion and unbelief — within the same community's history, different generations have their own originating sinning-moments. The origin is thus both historically fixed (first father as the chain's start) and generationally repeated (each generation has its own originating sinning in continuation of the chain).

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes across the nine VCG registers. (1) *VCG-01 covenant-against-God*: origin in the relational choice to betray the nurturing God (Isa 1:2); (2) *VCG-02 revolt*: origin in deliberate speech-act of false prophecy (Jer 28:16) or persistent refusal to stop despite judgment (Isa 1:5); (3) *VCG-03 threshold-crossing*: origin in specific national crimes (Amos — military brutality, slave-trading, desecration); (4) *VCG-04 law-violation*: origin in conscious law-knowledge (Rom 4:15); (5) *VCG-05 Adam-paradigm*: origin in the single primordial trespass (Rom 5:15); (6) *VCG-08 interpersonal*: origin in anger-driven social transgression (Pro 29:22 — anger causes much transgression).

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes across all three VCG registers. (1) *VCG-01 (toward God)*: origin in the departure of the heart's covenant-allegiance from God — 2Ch 29:6 — "turned away their faces... turned their backs"; pride-generated (2Ch 26:16 — Uzziah); allegiance-transfer (1Ch 5:25 — to false gods); (2) *VCG-02 (between persons)*: origin in marital desire-violation (Num 5:12/27); anger-betrayal (Judg 9:23); lust-captivity (Pro 11:6); (3) *VCG-03 (constitutional character)*: origin in the foreknown constitutional bent of the will (Isa 48:8) — the origin precedes specific circumstances and is embedded in the person's inner character from before birth.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes across the five VCG registers. (1) *VCG-01 (speech perversity)*: origin in the perverted heart (Pro 6:14) and the will's embrace of evil (Pro 2:14 — "delight in perverseness"); (2) *VCG-02 (judgment perversion)*: origin in external bribery corrupting the internal discernment-faculty (Exo 23:8); (3) *VCG-03 (mind/will/way)*: origin in the generational character of the perverted people (Deu 32:20) and the individual's twisting of what was right (Job 33:27); (4) *VCG-04 (sexual perversion)*: origin in violation of created-order categories (Lev 18:23 — te.vel — what God's creation-design separates); (5) *VCG-05 (corruption/decay)*: origin in sinful desire (2Pe 1:4) and unreasoning instinct (Jude 10).

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes across three VCG contexts. (1) *VCG-01 (judicial/commercial)*: origin in bribery-corruption of the discernment faculty (2Ch 19:7) and in the heart's devising of partial judgment (Psa 82:2 — "show partiality to the wicked"); (2) *VCG-02 (oppression and harm)*: origin in the heart's devising of violence (Psa 58:2) and self-trust (Hos 10:13); (3) *VCG-03 (character of the unjust)*: origin in the constitutional character-level — the person who IS unjust at every scale (Luk 16:10); the God-ignorance that defines the character-type (Job 18:21).
